# Foreward

Welcome, brave adventurers, to the twisted realm where animatronic nightmares come alive—a world where fantasy and horror intertwine, and reality bends beneath the weight of dark magic. This monster manual draws heavily from the chilling legacy of the Five Nights at Freddy’s saga, reimagining its eerie and unsettling creatures as fearsome foes within the expansive universe of Dungeons & Dragons. Prepare to face familiar yet transformed horrors, stalking the shadows of a haunted amusement park where every moment is a desperate struggle to survive.

Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza, once a lively and family-friendly venue filled with laughter and music, has fallen into ruin and darkness. Its cheerful façade conceals a labyrinth of despair and menace. The animatronics, once joyful entertainers, have become twisted predators fueled by an ancient and malevolent force. These beings have transcended their mechanical origins, becoming sentient, cunning, and merciless hunters who prowl the corridors with a chilling intelligence. Their playground is now a decaying, nightmarish maze—where shadows shift and the line between friend and foe is blurred.

Within this forsaken park, not only do the animatronics threaten intruders, but a host of otherworldly creatures drawn to the lingering dark magic lurk in every corner. From the spectral and elusive Shadow Freddy to the grotesque, corpse-infused Springtrap, these abominations challenge even the bravest souls. Each entity is steeped in supernatural dread, forcing adventurers to confront the unnatural and the uncanny.

The environments you will explore are as diverse as they are dangerous. The once-bustling Show Stage, now a macabre theater of twisted performances, stands in stark contrast to the eerily silent and maze-like Backrooms where animatronics silently await the perfect moment to strike. Hidden passages, secret chambers, and collapsing hallways create a treacherous landscape that demands vigilance and cunning to navigate. The atmosphere is thick with tension, every flicker of light and distant sound a potential herald of doom.

The animatronics themselves vary widely in form and function, each posing unique threats. Take Foxy, for example—swift, stealthy, and unpredictable, he emerges suddenly from the shadows to ensnare victims with razor-sharp precision before vanishing into darkness. On the other hand, Chica’s terrifying combination of brute strength and calculated traps makes her an unrelenting force, wearing down foes with sheer power and relentless pursuit. These creatures embody a perfect blend of physical might and sinister cunning.

Beyond their individual abilities, the animatronics command an army of minions that serve their dark will. From the swarming Mini-Animatronics—small, agile, and deadly—to the hulking Nightmare variants that spread terror and destruction, these servants form a complex ecosystem of horror. Their loyalty is absolute, and their ruthlessness unmatched, ensuring that every incursion into the park is met with overwhelming resistance.

What makes these horrors truly formidable is their sentience. They communicate through a haunting language of beeps, whirrs, and eerie melodies—known only to the most attuned adventurers as “Animatronic.” This intricate system conveys warnings, commands, and secrets, weaving a tapestry of sound that adds an unsettling layer of intelligence to these mechanical monstrosities. Their ability to coordinate and adapt makes them unpredictable adversaries.

But the threat of the animatronics extends far beyond physical violence. They are masters of psychological warfare, exploiting the deepest fears and insecurities of their victims. Their presence warps perception, turning safe havens into nightmarish prisons. The park itself becomes an extension of their will, distorting reality and bending minds, where shadows deceive and allies may betray. Every step taken within the park tests not just your strength but your sanity.

The supernatural ties binding these beings to the world of the living add a chilling depth to their menace. Legend whispers that the souls of those claimed by the animatronics are trapped within their metal shells, eternally bound to serve. This spectral imprisonment grants them insight into humanity, but also fuels a bitter hatred toward their former lives. The dead do not rest here; spirits are dragged back into the realm of the living, twisted into servants and guardians of this hellish domain. This undead ecology blurs the boundaries between life and death, creating a realm where spectral eyes gleam alongside glowing animatronic sensors.

Adventurers will also discover a variety of magical relics scattered throughout the park, each imbued with unique powers and histories. The enigmatic “Freddy’s Head,” a sentient artifact rumored to bestow great strength and dark knowledge, lies hidden amidst the ruins. The dreaded Springlock Suits, ancient armors that allow wearers to tap into animatronic power at great risk, represent a tempting but deadly prize. Such artifacts offer great power but come with dire consequences, often guarded fiercely by the park’s monstrous inhabitants.

The challenges within Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza range from the mundane to the maddeningly complex. You might find yourself taking the role of a night security guard, tasked with surviving the hours as relentless foes close in from every direction. Or you may be trapped in puzzle-filled rooms, racing against time and unraveling twisted enigmas to escape before being claimed. The pinnacle of these trials is the infamous “Five Nights” endurance test—five consecutive nights of escalating horrors that push the limits of survival, strategy, and courage.

Reality itself is warped by the dark magic suffusing the park. The animatronics manipulate space and perception, conjuring illusions and twisting the environment to confuse and trap victims. Their mechanical forms hum with an otherworldly energy, granting them superhuman strength, speed, and resilience. Even more terrifying is their power to possess and control other creatures, turning them into pawns in their deadly games, expanding their influence and threat beyond the park’s crumbling walls.

\pagebreakNum

At the heart of this nightmare stands Freddy Fazbear himself, a towering figure of menace and mastery. His seemingly cheerful facade masks a calculating predator, a master manipulator whose armor hides deadly springlocks capable of brutal violence. Freddy commands his domain with ruthless efficiency, supported by a cadre of minions ranging from the swarming Mini-Animatronics to the terrifying Nightmare variants, each fulfilling a role in his twisted hierarchy.

Exploring this cursed park is an exercise in terror and wonder. You will traverse environments alive with danger—from the cacophonous chaos of the Show Stage to the silence of shadowy back corridors. Each space holds secrets, traps, and threats that test both physical prowess and mental acuity. Only the most resourceful and determined adventurers can hope to claim victory, their rewards weighed against the cost of survival.

This manual invites you to step beyond the veil of reality into a world where animatronic horrors rule, and the boundary between life, death, and machine blurs into oblivion. Steel your nerves, sharpen your wits, and prepare to face a darkness that consumes body and soul alike. The horrors of Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza await—and only the bravest will emerge unscathed.

## About This Book

This book is a dark fantasy reimagining of the Five Nights at Freddy’s universe, woven into the mechanics and storytelling framework of Dungeons & Dragons. While it draws inspiration from the expansive and eerie lore of the original games, it ventures into new territory—literally and narratively—by reshaping the world, the characters, and the horror they bring.

In crafting this campaign setting, liberties were taken with the established canon to better suit the tone and mechanics of tabletop role-playing. The animatronics—once bound to the walls of neon-lit pizzerias—have been reimagined as cursed constructs, necromantic oddities, and tragic relics of a forgotten age. They are no longer just haunted machines; they are remnants of dark rituals, vessels of arcane torment, and monsters crafted by hands both mortal and monstrous.

Likewise, familiar locations have been reinterpreted to match a more fantasy-gothic aesthetic. The once-popular Pizza Plex, for example, now exists as a vast underground ruin—part crypt, part temple—left to rot beneath the bones of a forgotten civilization. The carnival-like energy of the old Fazbear attractions has twisted into a decrepit, decaying circus, where colorful tents sag under the weight of time and long-dead laughter echoes on the wind. You may explore shadow-drenched forests where stage lights flicker in the dark, sunken amphitheaters where broken animatronics reenact ghostly performances, and forgotten kingdoms ruled by spectral echoes of past mascots.

This project was born from a desire to combine two personal passions: the atmospheric, nerve-wracking tension of horror—especially that found in the FNaF franchise—and the rich, immersive storytelling of Dungeons & Dragons. The goal was not to simply recreate a familiar story, but to transform it—allowing players to live the terror, shape the outcome, and confront the horrors in real time through dice, decisions, and roleplay.

Where the original series leaned into jump-scare mechanics and subtle environmental storytelling, this adaptation offers a more deliberate sense of dread. Here, danger doesn’t flicker behind security monitors; it waits in the darkness of crypts, stalks through twisted halls of cursed amusement parks, and whispers from mechanical mouths powered by forgotten souls. Players are not passive observers but adventurers drawn into a living nightmare—one they might escape, conquer, or be consumed by.

While the names and themes may feel familiar to longtime fans, this version of Freddy and his twisted companions invites a new kind of experience—one filled with combat, exploration, and deeply unsettling moral choices. The animatronics themselves have undergone narrative evolution. Their personalities, roles, and appearances have been adapted to match the tone of a grim fantasy world—some appearing as clockwork wraiths, others as wandering revenants, and a few as tragic protectors bound by arcane oaths. Even their names may take on new meanings in this world, redefined by history, myth, and fear.

This is not a direct retelling of the FNaF saga, but a loving homage—a mythic reshaping of the world into something both familiar and fearsome. Whether you are a horror fan, a D&D enthusiast, or a curious adventurer, this book invites you to explore a nightmarish new realm. It’s a place where lore is reinterpreted, where terror has a tangible shape, and where you must ask not just what happened, but what will you do next?

Welcome to the crypts of Freddy Fazbear. Welcome to the circus of shadows. Welcome to your story.

\pagebreakNum

# The First Performers: Heralds of the Hollow Stage

The Core Animatronics
Once mere performers meant to delight children, the Core Animatronics now haunt the forgotten ruins of a shattered world. They are bound not by bolts and gears alone, but by sorrow, vengeance, and the lingering weight of what once was. Though their appearances may differ from the tales of old—more monstrous, more arcane—their essence remains eerily familiar. Each one carries a trace of tragedy beneath the metal and magic, remnants of lives twisted by forces no child should ever know.

#### Freddy
The so-called "King of Laughter" now rules over the silent crypt with hollow eyes and a cracked smile. Cloaked in regal decay, he roams like a guardian turned warden, enforcing a long-forgotten showtime. His footsteps echo with ritualistic purpose, and the ancient stage upon which he walks is etched with names that no longer have voices. There is something mournful in his song, something broken in his cheer.

#### Bonnie
Once the heartbeat of harmony, Bonnie now shambles through broken concert halls, his strings long since severed. His body, once vibrant, has become a blend of shattered porcelain and rusted wire, an instrument that plays only sorrow. He searches endlessly for a song half-remembered, or perhaps for someone who once listened. Those who hear his faint strumming often say it feels like a memory—not theirs, but someone else's pain.

#### Chica
A distorted vision of hospitality, Chica wanders the ruins of the Feast Pavilion with cracked plates and rusted cutlery clinking from her garb like funeral chimes. Her warmth is cold now, her kindness hollow. Still, she lays the table for guests who will never come, singing lullabies to shadows. She asks questions no one should answer, and offers sweets that taste like ash and dreams.

#### Foxy
The entertainer turned executioner, Foxy stalks the remains of the Grand Circus with jagged teeth and a voice of static. A pirate once beloved for his flair, he now moves like a storm caught in flesh and metal, unpredictable and hungry. There are whispers of a betrayal too deep to name, of a show that never ended, and of a captain who lost his crew to something far worse than mutiny.
<div style='margin-top:40px;'></div>
Each of these beings is more than a machine. They are echoes of forgotten joys, of crimes buried beneath stage lights, of souls twisted by cruelty and consequence. What they want—redemption, release, or revenge—is known only to the darkness that made them. Tread lightly in their domains, for even the rusted know how to bleed.

### Freddy Fazbear

Freddy Fazbear is the iconic and central animatronic figure of the Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza franchise, a fictional family entertainment center and pizzeria. Known for his signature bear suit, top hat, and microphone, Freddy serves as the main mascot of the chain and is both a symbol of nostalgia and terror within the series’ intricate lore.

##### Origins and Purpose
Freddy Fazbear was created as part of a group of animatronic entertainers designed to provide wholesome, fun experiences for children and families. Originally built by Fazbear Entertainment, Freddy was the lead singer of the animatronic band that performed live shows during the day at Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza locations. Alongside his companions—Bonnie the Bunny, Chica the Chicken, and Foxy the Pirate Fox—Freddy was meant to captivate audiences with cheerful songs and interactive performances, creating an inviting atmosphere where kids could enjoy birthday parties and family outings.

The animatronics themselves were advanced for their time, featuring sophisticated robotics to mimic human-like movements, facial expressions, and singing. This level of engineering was a marvel, making the Freddy Fazbear band an attraction drawing large crowds and generating a sense of community around the pizzerias.

##### The Dark Turn: Tragedy and Haunting
However, beneath the colorful exterior and joyful music, Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza harbors a dark and tragic history. The chain became infamous due to a series of chilling incidents tied to the animatronics, involving mysterious disappearances and deaths of children. This dark legacy is woven deeply into the fabric of Freddy Fazbear’s identity.

Central to the lore is the story of a man later known as William Afton, co-founder of Fazbear Entertainment and the sinister mind behind many of the tragedies. Afton’s gruesome crimes involve the kidnapping and murder of multiple children, whose restless spirits would come to haunt the animatronics, including Freddy. These spirits are said to inhabit the robotic suits, animating them with a terrifying consciousness beyond their original programming.

One of the most well-known incidents linked to Freddy is the “Bite of ‘87,” an event where an animatronic allegedly bit a customer, causing severe injury. Though the exact details remain ambiguous in the lore, this event symbolized a turning point where the animatronics were seen not just as malfunctioning machines but as potential threats.


\pagebreakNum

Freddy’s design reflects this dual nature—his friendly appearance with wide eyes and a welcoming smile contrasts sharply with his glowing, sometimes hollow eyes in darker moments, and the worn, damaged exterior that hints at years of neglect and the horrific secrets beneath.

##### The Spirits Within
A defining aspect of Freddy Fazbear’s legend is the belief that the animatronics are possessed by the spirits of the children murdered by William Afton. These spirits seek justice, revenge, or peace, and their restless presence animates the robots in unpredictable and dangerous ways.

Freddy is often interpreted as the host or leader of these spirits, particularly linked to a child named Gabriel or a similar figure in various fan interpretations and expanded lore. The animatronics’ behavior—wandering the building at night, attacking security guards, and exhibiting strange patterns—are manifestations of this haunting.

The presence of these spirits gives the animatronics a dual identity: they are both mechanical machines and vessels of human tragedy, caught in a cycle of vengeance and sorrow.

___

### Foxy the pirate

In the twisted annals of the Fazbear mythos, few names carry the same weight of dread and sorrow as Foxy the Pirate. Once a beloved icon of excitement and high-seas fantasy, Foxy’s tale is one of betrayal, decay, and a haunted legacy that refuses to die. Though the years have distorted the truth, and many of the records have long since been lost or erased, fragments remain—pieces of a puzzle smeared in grease, blood, and memory.

Foxy was originally introduced in the early days of Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza, a pirate-themed entertainer meant to bring energy and unpredictability to the stage. Housed within a faux shipwreck set known as Pirate Cove, Foxy stood out from the other animatronics for his rugged charm, swashbuckling demeanor, and distinctive design. With a bright crimson pelt, a worn eye-patch, and a signature metal hook in place of his right hand, Foxy quickly became a favorite among the children who visited the restaurant.

Yet something was different about Foxy—something beneath the programming. Unlike Freddy, Bonnie, or Chica, who were meant to work in coordination and follow show scripts carefully, Foxy was designed to improvise. He would sing sea shanties, tell tall tales, and engage directly with the audience in unpredictable ways. Perhaps it was this level of independence that made him... unstable.

The Fall of Pirate Cove
At some point during the restaurant’s dark timeline, Foxy was decommissioned and sealed away behind a tattered "Out of Order" sign. The reasons given were vague. Official reports cited “malfunctioning servos” and “damaged speech algorithms,” but eyewitness accounts and staff rumors suggested something much more disturbing. There were tales of Foxy lunging offstage mid-performance, of children crying after hearing things whispered into their ears, and of one incident so severe that no official statement was ever released. After that, Pirate Cove was shuttered.

For years, Foxy sat dormant in the darkness, half-covered by a worn curtain that barely concealed his slumped form. He became something of a ghost story among the staff—an animatronic that didn’t quite follow the same rules. Surveillance footage would sometimes catch him twitching or sprinting down the hall toward the security office in ways that defied the logic of the other characters. Unlike Freddy or Chica, who moved in deliberate patterns, Foxy was erratic, unpredictable, and fast. Too fast.
But there’s more to Foxy than mechanics.

##### A Spirit Beneath the Mask
Like the other animatronics, Foxy is haunted—or more accurately, possessed. In the complex and tragic lore of the FNAF universe, it is now widely accepted that the core animatronics are the vessels for the souls of children murdered by a sadistic serial killer known in the games as William Afton, or the Purple Guy. The identity of the soul within Foxy is not as clearly defined as some of the others, but hints across multiple games suggest that he may house the spirit of one of the children from the infamous Missing Children Incident, when several kids vanished after visiting the pizzeria.
___

\pagebreakNum


Foxy, then, is not merely a malfunctioning robot. He is a restless ghost bound in cold metal—a soul driven mad by years of isolation and grief. The enthusiasm and charisma that once defined him have twisted into rage and sorrow. His shipwreck-themed home is no longer a stage but a tomb.

There’s also a certain symbolic loneliness to Foxy’s arc. He is the only core animatronic who was forcibly removed from the main cast. While Freddy, Bonnie, and Chica continued to perform—however corrupted—Foxy was relegated to the shadows. Whether his behavior became dangerous due to the spirit inside, or whether the isolation drove that spirit to madness, is left open. But the implications are heartbreaking: he was cast aside, left to rot, and now returns only to lash out at those who step into his domain.

Foxy takes on the role of the forsaken entertainer turned executioner. The rotting remains of his circus ship stage lie buried in the mud of a haunted carnival, half-sunken and filled with whispers. His once-charming tales are now riddles and threats, and his performances end not in applause but in screams.

Though his metal body is broken and warped, the spark that once made him beloved remains buried within—twisted, but not entirely extinguished. Those who dare to enter his domain may glimpse fragments of the performer he once was… if they survive long enough to notice.

He is a creature of speed, unpredictability, and emotional torment. His pain manifests in blinding rage, but beneath it is a need—for recognition, for freedom, or simply for the curtain to finally fall.

Foxy the Pirate was never meant to be a villain. But like the sea he once pretended to sail, his story is deep, dark, and full of ghosts.

### Bonnie

There is something profoundly unsettling about Bonnie the Bunny. Among all the animatronics birthed by the Freddy Fazbear mythos, he is often the first to move, the first to lurk just outside your door, and the first to make you question whether these machines ever had innocence to begin with.

But Bonnie was not always a figure of dread. In the beginning, he was designed to be fun, fuzzy, and musical. His blue fur, red bow tie, and happy-go-lucky grin were meant to project joy, talent, and warmth to the children who crowded the pizzeria’s main stage. He strummed an electric guitar with mechanical precision and played sidekick to Freddy Fazbear himself, completing the band’s sound with energy and flair.

##### Origins and Role in the Band
Bonnie was one of the original four animatronics featured at Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza, part of the main ensemble alongside Freddy, Chica, and Foxy. While Freddy was the leader and Chica was the face of fun and food, Bonnie was the music—the heart of the stage show. His character was intended to bring excitement and charm to the performance, serving as the lead guitarist with oversized cartoon fingers that plucked strings on a red bass guitar.

Out of all the animatronics, Bonnie was often regarded as the most energetic and kid-friendly—until the lights went out. It was then that Bonnie’s presence became far more menacing. His tendency to approach swiftly and silently, especially in the original FNAF game, earned him a reputation as one of the most unsettling enemies in the series.

##### Possession and Haunting Behavior
Bonnie, like the rest of the core animatronics, is widely believed to be possessed by the spirit of one of the missing children from the Missing Children Incident. This infamous event, canon to the FNAF timeline, involved the kidnapping and murder of five children by serial killer William Afton. Their bodies were never recovered. It is believed that Bonnie’s endoskeleton was among those used to hide the corpses, and over time, the soul of one of the victims became bound to the animatronic.

This haunting is not theatrical—it’s quiet and consuming. Bonnie’s behavior reflects a being that stalks with precision, striking from the shadows. His iconic stare, with blank white eyes and an unblinking expression, has terrified generations of players, as if something inside him is not just watching—but seeing into you.

Unlike Chica’s erratic aggression or Foxy’s wild speed, Bonnie is deliberate. He deactivates cameras, disrupts signals, and appears silently at your door. In some iterations, he's the first animatronic to become active, hinting at a soul more restless—or more determined—than the others.

##### Personality in the Shadows
While Freddy may represent leadership and Chica gluttony, Bonnie embodies abandonment and the fear of the unseen. His design is unassuming, yet his presence always feels one step ahead of the player. His lack of speech or overt behavior only adds to the mystery—Bonnie haunts through absence, often disappearing from view only to reappear just inches away.

He is not a berserker or a monster crashing through walls. Bonnie is the figure at the end of a hallway, watching. The creaking of a door. The faint buzz of a broken camera. He moves without sound and waits without warning.

He is a guardian of the past—a relic that shouldn’t have survived, but did. Bonnie may reside in a corrupted cathedral of music, where phantom sounds drift through cracked stained glass windows and ancient stage lights flicker to life without warning.

His smile is broken now. His arms hang loosely, his joints misaligned, as if his body forgot how to hold itself up. And yet he waits, not to kill—but to confront. To mourn. To avenge.

##### Hints of the Past
The tragedy inside Bonnie is never explicit—but it’s present in every movement. The way he avoids mirrors. The cracked photograph he carries. The soft humming of a song only he remembers.

Some say he was once the kindest of the spirits—gentle, quiet, protective. But now he is confusion and anger, trapped between the desire to be whole again and the bitter realization that he never can be.

\pagebreakNum

### Chica
Chica was one of the original four animatronics at Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza, created to round out the musical stage show alongside Freddy, Bonnie, and Foxy. Designed to appeal to younger audiences with her bright yellow exterior, oversized orange beak, and cartoonishly large eyes, Chica’s role in the band was typically the backup singer—often accompanied by a small prop cupcake with eyes (known unofficially by fans as Carl the Cupcake, who has his own entry).

But she wasn’t just a performer. Chica was also part of the kitchen staff, in a sense. Her design included a pizza-loving persona, reinforced by her bib emblazoned with the words “Let’s Eat!!!”—a phrase that would later take on chilling new meaning. Her character was intended to blend warmth and appetite, offering a fun-loving image that appealed to the birthday party crowd. Yet even in the earliest versions, her staring eyes and emotionless smile unnerved some guests and staff.

As with all the Fazbear animatronics, however, the colorful exterior concealed a much darker reality.

##### Possession and the Unseen Hunger
Chica, like Freddy and the others, became a vessel for tragedy. During the events that would become known as the Missing Children Incident, five children vanished at the pizzeria, their lives brutally ended by the notorious serial killer William Afton. 

\pagebreakNum

The children’s bodies were never found, but signs of a cover-up—and the stench of decay—began to permeate the animatronics. It was widely believed that the children’s spirits were trapped within the suits, their souls bleeding into the programming and corrupting the once-innocent machines.

Chica’s possession is often associated with gluttony and obsession. Whether a reflection of the spirit within her or a side effect of decades of haunting, Chica’s identity has become tied to the notion of consumption—both literal and metaphorical. She is not just a mascot with a pizza fetish. She is an entity that hungers: for attention, for closure, for revenge… and sometimes, for flesh.

##### The Cupcake – A Familiar Shadow (Has own entry)
Always close by is the Cupcake, a seemingly innocuous prop with eyes and a smile that mirrors Chica’s own. While not always given a mechanical or spiritual identity, the Cupcake often acts as an extension of Chica herself—an accessory to her appearances or even an independent threat in certain games (FNAF 4 features it as an entity that leaps at the player).

The cupcake is more than a toy. It’s a symbol—of twisted festivity, of celebration turned to horror. In a D&D horror setting, it might act as a familiar, a cursed relic, or even a separate mini-entity born of the same ghostly hunger that drives Chica.

##### A Tragic Legacy
Chica is haunting echo of corrupted nurture—the mother hen who feeds her “children” spoiled offerings, who wanders abandoned kitchens and feast halls, forever driven by an emptiness that cannot be filled.

Her once-silly catchphrase becomes a grim warning: Let’s Eat!!!—a promise of devouring rather than dining. Her bib is stained not with marinara, but with ancient ichor. Her face is cracked and her limbs are bound with rusted iron rings, each one a relic of failed attempts to bind her spirit.

She may lurk in places where food once brought joy: abandoned banquet halls, ruined wedding feasts, crumbling kitchens where fire no longer burns. Wherever famine and guilt intertwine, Chica waits.

Her movements are slow but deliberate. She sings softly when alone. And when she strikes, it is not out of rage, but out of desperation—an aching need that consumes her every thought.
What makes Chica terrifying isn’t her strength, or her jump-scares—it’s her loss of self. The animatronic that once danced with children and handed out birthday slices is now a hollow parody of that joy. She has no concept of the damage she causes. Her programming is shattered, overwritten by grief, madness, and the soul of a child who died far too young.

Yet, hints of her former self remain. In the right moment—when the wind hits just right or the music box plays an old familiar tune—you might see her hesitate. You might even hear her laugh, just once, like she did in those long-lost days of innocence.

\pagebreakNum

### Cupcake – The Silent Witness
Though small in size and often overlooked, Cupcake is far more than a simple prop. Originally introduced as a cheerful accessory held by Chica the Chicken, the cupcake was designed to enhance the friendly, food-themed atmosphere of Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza. With its bright pink frosting, cartoonish blue eyes, and striped candle perpetually alight, Cupcake seemed like nothing more than a party treat come to life.

But in the shadows of a cursed stage and behind the laughter of animatronic performances, Cupcake has always watched.

This eerie presence has led many to believe that Cupcake is more than a mere decoration. In fact, some theorize it is possessed, much like the other animatronics—only more subtle. Perhaps it contains the soul of a child overlooked in the aftermath of the Missing Children Incident. Or maybe it’s a spiritual tether, a fragment of Chica's own haunting. Whatever the case, Cupcake is not innocent. It is a witness to everything. The murders. The coverups. The reactivations.

Cupcake doesn't speak, but its candle never goes out. It’s said that wherever the flame flickers, something unseen is nearby. The flame may be a lure. Or a warning.

Its eyes are not glass—they are windows, reflecting places that no longer exist and moments that should not be remembered. Staring too long into Cupcake may cause unsettling visions: birthday parties frozen in time, blood-soaked confetti, or echoing laughter turning to screams.

It is a remnant. A relic. A ghost of joy corrupted by the rot around it.

The candle still burns. But no one’s making a wish.

> 
> **Sugar Rush (Recharge 5–6).** Cupcake darts with unnatural speed. It can move up to its full movement without provoking opportunity attacks and make one *Fiendish Bite* attack with advantage.
> 
> **Distracting Flicker.** Cupcake’s candle flickers erratically. One creature within 30 feet must make a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw or have disadvantage on attack rolls until the start of Cupcake’s next turn.

\pagebreakNum

# The Withered Ones
In the decaying world , deep within the catacombs beneath the ruined Carnival of Chains, there lie crypts not of stone, but of metal and rust. Inside them, slumped against shattered walls and tangled in arcane wiring, rest the Withered Animatronics—broken remnants of an age when joy was manufactured and innocence was preyed upon.

These are no longer mere machines.

They are withered memories, both figuratively and literally. Echoes of older animatronics, now warped, rotted, and frayed, they retain the design and purpose of their original forms—entertainment and companionship—but those traits have long since been corrupted. Born from tragedy and buried by time, their current condition reflects not only mechanical decay but spiritual torment.

Each Withered animatronic was part of the second generation of performers crafted by the ancient Artisan’s Guild of Fazbear Hollow, built to replace the Originals (now lost to corruption and fire). These constructs once dazzled children in golden halls and festival courts, but their lives were steeped in cursed rituals, unknown to those who smiled at their songs.

Then came The Incident.

The Day the Music Died
The tragedy that led to their fall is known in fragmented whispers as “The Hollow Banquet”—a day when dozens of children vanished during a festival inside the grand Pavilion Theater, never to be seen again. Panic followed, but the Guild silenced the rumors with coin and threats. The animatronics were decommissioned, locked away, and officially declared faulty due to mechanical instability.

Unofficially, they were tainted.

Behind closed doors, their animatronic endoskeletons had become vessels for wayward spirits—the fractured souls of the missing, who clung to what they remembered: masks of fur and metal, music-box tunes, and flickering stage lights. But memory is not a kind master. Over the decades, these spirits warped—some forgetting who they were, others remembering only their pain.

### The Hollow Banquet: A Feast of Forgotten Souls
Before the ruins, before the silence, before the animatronics wore the skin of tragedy, there was The Banquet Hall—once the grand heart of the old Pizzaplex Pavilion, now reimagined in your world as a crumbling Cathedral of Merriment, a place where joy was twisted by ancient rituals and the arrogance of mortal ambition.

The Hollow Banquet is no single event, but a convergence of suffering, magic, and misused memory—a terrible incident that marked the turning point for both the animatronics and the land they haunted. Its whispers echo through rusted circuitry and broken porcelain smiles. Few speak of it aloud, and those who do refer to it only as the Feast that Wasn’t, the Smiling Starfall, or the Silence Between Songs.

### Origins of the Hall
Originally, the Banquet Hall was a place of celebration, embedded within a crypt-like performance dome carved into a natural cavern beneath the Pavilion. Lined with stained-glass windows of animated jesters and crystalline chandeliers enchanted to shimmer with spectral light, it was meant to be a permanent stage of cheer. Noble houses sent their children to dine with the beloved mascots—animatronic performers blessed with rudimentary magic and bonded through soulsteel programming runes, a blend of technology and arcane design.

### The Banquet Turns Hollow
At the peak of the celebration—when the lights dimmed and the animatronics raised their arms for a synchronized final chorus—the glyphs activated. Instead of joy, the spell summoned a void, a breach between the Material and something darker. Guests were pulled from reality, not violently, but silently—one by one, like snuffed candles. Some vanished, some collapsed into husks, their essence drained to power the ritual. Others remained, but their minds were gone—trapped in a loop of smiles, claps, and screams.

The animatronics twitched mid-song. Their synthetic minds could not reject the influx of raw soul energy. Each was burned, corrupted, changed. The cheerful patterns of their programming merged with trauma. Memory and mimicry entwined into something... self-aware. They woke up, confused. And then they screamed.

### Aftermath and the Curse
When authorities descended into the Pavilion, they found a ballroom frozen in time. Animatronics stood still, eyes flickering like candles in the wind. The guests were gone. The music had stopped—but the smell of frosting and burning oil lingered in the air. Those who dared recover what they could sealed the Banquet Hall and declared it cursed ground. But it was too late.

The Hollow Banquet had left behind a soul scar—an echo of its ritual forever burned into the floor, the air, the code. The animatronics could no longer follow their programming. They wandered. They wept. They hunted.

Some speculate the Hollow Banquet is still happening, just outside the boundary of time—like a looping echo in a dimension just behind the walls. Those who step too close hear the music again. They hear clapping, faint laughter, and the gentle whisper of a child saying, “Do you want to see my candle?”

\pagebreakNum

### Lingering Effects
##### Animatronics:
The Hollow Banquet is the spiritual birthplace of the Withered and Haunted variants. It turned performers into mourners, entertainers into monsters. Some, like Freddy and Chica, try to remember their purpose. Others, like Foxy and Bonnie, are consumed by guilt or rage. Cupcake’s tiny candle is said to be a fragment of the Banquet’s soul-fire—its flicker an echo of the feast that went wrong.



##### Magical Fallout:
Enchantments cast near the site sometimes warp. Divinations yield false readings. Illusions grow teeth. The closer you get to the center of the Hall, the more reality feels scripted, as if you’ve stepped into a performance—and you’ve forgotten your lines.

##### Legends Among Adventurers:
Some say that if you complete the Banquet—place the proper plates, light the phantom candles, and sing the forgotten chorus—the spirits will rest. Others claim that doing so only finishes the ritual, allowing the void to open once more.

<br>

And thus the Withered Ones were born.

<br>

Now, they stalk ruined corridors and blackened halls, not driven by programming but by instinct and fractured purpose. They're not hunting. They're searching—for closure, for justice, or perhaps for someone to remember them properly.

Below are their tales.

#### Withered Freddy – The Hollow Host
Withered Freddy was once the lead performer of the Artisan’s Carnival. His broad frame, warm brown fur, and top hat made him a familiar and comforting presence. Children clung to his legs; parents admired his craftsmanship. But now, that frame is cracked. His right ear dangles uselessly, his jaw hangs slightly open, and his blue eyes are faded with a dull, unfocused glow. During the Hollow Banquet, something happened. His memory banks recorded a security lockdown he could never forget, looping over and over with the laughter of children turning to silence.

Now, Freddy roams slowly, like an ancient golem searching for its forgotten temple. He emits low frequencies, not unlike a haunted choir, echoing in places where sound should not travel. Those who encounter him feel an inexplicable weight—like the presence of a father mourning what he couldn’t save.

#### Withered Bonnie – The Broken Chord
Once a skilled lute-playing jester of the court, Withered Bonnie was the musical soul of the troupe. His electric tones were the heartbeat of every show, and his vibrant purple fur made him stand out like royalty among the cast.

But Bonnie suffered more than most.

After the incident, he was found slumped near the Guild’s private archives, his faceplate and left arm completely removed—not by accident, but with precision. It's whispered that he uncovered something hidden in the system, something he wasn’t meant to see. The missing children, perhaps. Or the ritual binding codes. Whatever the truth, his dismantling was intentional.

Now, Withered Bonnie moves in erratic, twitchy motions. He shudders as if caught between realities. His hollow face and fingerless arm have become his symbols, not of weakness—but of suffering endured. Echoes of music still leak from him, but the notes are warped—detuned strings of a haunted melody that fills adventurers with unease.

Some say he speaks in static. Others say he cries when left alone.

#### Withered Chica – The Empty Feast
Once the embodiment of joy and festivity, Withered Chica was built for the banquet halls. Her large, rounded frame was often painted with confetti symbols, and her mechanical voice box was tuned to sing lullabies and party songs.

But her fate was the cruelest.

After the incident, Chica was found with her beak wedged open unnaturally, as though she had been screaming. Her internal servos had fused, and her hands had been split into razor-sharp claws from trying to pry herself free. It is believed she was trapped during the lockdown—left behind as the Guild sealed the doors.

The most terrifying thing is… her voice box still works.

Now, Withered Chica sings broken versions of her old songs, slowed down and filled with static. Her eyes glow dim yellow, and her hands constantly twitch—an echo of that desperate attempt to escape. She doesn’t chase. She stalks. She waits in dining halls and kitchens, humming lullabies, as if reliving a moment no one else remembers.

Legends say that those who hear her song in its entirety become paralyzed by sorrow, reliving their worst memories. She is a mourner trapped in a feaster’s shell.

#### Withered Foxy – The Fallen Raider
Foxy was once a swashbuckling rogue-like entertainer, sprinting across stages and leaping between balconies with flair. With his crimson fur and eyepatch, he thrilled children with tales of ghost ships and buried treasure.

But Foxy decayed faster than the others.

His performance routines were too demanding. His servo motors wore out, his jaw became unhinged, and eventually he was quarantined to a corner stage and labeled out of order—yet his programming still compelled him to perform.

After the Hollow Banquet, Foxy’s fate was sealed. His entire chest cavity had been torn open, not by damage—but seemingly from the inside out. No one knows what escaped.

Now, Withered Foxy is the most dangerous of the group. His speed remains, though jerky and spasmatic. He dashes through shadows and vents, appearing from nowhere with a metallic scream. His movements are feral. He does not speak. He growls.

But in rare moments, he slows. He stops and stares at broken pirate flags or shattered stage lights, as if remembering the joy he once brought. He is rage born of betrayal—a performer discarded and left to rot.

\pagebreakNum

#### Withered Cupcake – The Flickering Flame
Unlike the towering forms of the other Withered Animatronics, Withered Cupcake is small—barely a foot tall. But in the echoing dark of the forgotten halls, it is not size that commands fear. It is silence. It is stillness. It is what stares back when you look too long into an empty dining table and realize something is watching you.

<br>

That changed after the Hollow Banquet.

<br>



Now, Withered Cupcake is a far cry from its cheerful form. Its frosting is matted and dried like old wax. Its single candle burns a phantom flame, a cold, bluish light that dances without heat. Its eyes, half-lidded and crusted with grime, follow movement with unnatural precision. No longer just a passive observer, Cupcake behaves like an animated familiar—bonded to Chica still, but driven by an agenda all its own.

When Withered Chica is near, Cupcake moves with her, perched on her shoulder or clenched in a malformed claw. But when separated, it acts independently, slipping through tight spaces, hiding in shadows, and triggering ancient security systems with eerie purpose.

# Toy Animatronics: Echoes of Innocence
Once envisioned as a radiant rebirth of the fractured past, the Toy Animatronics were heralded as a cleaner, safer, more “friendly” era of performance magic—crafted to overshadow the eerie legacy of their predecessors. Forged from polished steel, imbued with radiant hues, and gifted with charming facades, these newer creations were made not only to entertain but also to reassure. Yet, beneath their glossy veneers and false smiles, lay something old—something far more corrupted than the engineers or artificers could ever imagine.

The Toy Animatronics were first introduced within the opulent theater-chambers of the Marionette's Crescent, a once-thriving carnival citadel built atop cursed foundations. As remnants of the ancient rituals performed by the Criers of Glee—a forgotten cult that sought immortality through mechanical ascension—whispers claimed that the very souls powering these new creations were drawn not from benevolent spirits, but from echoes of grief long unresolved.

Despite their cheerful appearances, the Toy Animatronics carried a weight. They were embedded with arcane soul-mirrors—an experimental construct intended to absorb ambient joy and emotion from the crowds they entertained. But instead of joy, something else seeped in—something tragic. The unhealed trauma of those who had died within the walls of the earlier halls, especially those tied to the Core Animatronics, infected the new generation. Their programming was flawless, their behavior predictive, but at night… they remembered.

They were designed as replacements. Not to coexist, but to erase history. Their creators wanted to rid the stage of the older animatronics—those more brutal, those tarnished with accusations, whispers of missing children, and unexplained deaths. The Toy Animatronics were seen as progress, a clean slate. But machines, no matter how refined, cannot rewrite bloodstained memory.

Each Toy Animatronic was shaped in almost a mockery of its ancestor, gone was the fur now replaced with a smooth substance But those spirits which had once haunted the original machines recognized the fraud, and through the veil between realms, cursed their replacements. What began as glitches and strange behaviors during maintenance hours soon escalated into uncontrollable malfunctions—blank eyes turning red, cheerful songs shifting into dirges, and movement patterns resembling the jerky spasms of entities caught between life and death.
The theater became a tomb.

One fateful night, during a grand winter gala known as the Hollow Banquet, the Toy Animatronics malfunctioned en masse. It was a celebration intended to solidify their success, a banquet for nobility, adventurers, and commoners alike. But when the final toast was made, and the curtains rose, the stage revealed something monstrous. The Toy Animatronics, smiling and pristine, danced a bloodless waltz. They bowed, sang, and beckoned—until the lights dimmed, and the screams began.

When the ruins were excavated years later, no bodies were found—only cold masks, torn ribbons, and traces of silver ichor. The Toy Animatronics were gone.

Or so it was believed.

Unbeknownst to the realm’s surface dwellers, deep beneath the ruins of the Marionette's Crescent, the Toy Animatronics continued their performance. Trapped in a loop of corrupted routines, they moved mechanically through the shattered remains of their original programming, now warped by pain and fear. A grotesque parody of joy. They did not rest—they adapted. They evolved. Their speech became cryptic, their movement shadowy. And their faces… those pristine masks had begun to crack, revealing glimpses of something old behind the glass eyes—grief, regret, and endless yearning.

The Toy Animatronics became the centerpiece of a new legend, a tragedy whispered by torchlight and campfire. Some say they are protectors of the children who were lost long ago—hunting those they believe responsible, or any who bear a resemblance. Others claim they seek reunification with their original counterparts, desperate to reclaim the fragmented souls they believe were stolen from them.

Unlike the Withered Animatronics, whose rage was overt and monstrous, the Toy Animatronics embody something subtler: false comfort. They lull adventurers into thinking they are safe—until it's far too late. Their voices still mimic lullabies. Their faces still smile. And their hands still reach out—not to hurt, but to hold. To keep. To never let go again.

Despite their corrupted nature, the Toy Animatronics are deeply intertwined with the metaphysical architecture of the realm. They act as spiritual anchors to the theater’s haunted ley lines, their presence keeping ancient curses from spilling across the region. In a way, they are as much victims as they are villains—cursed creations bound by the sins of their makers and the deaths of the innocent.

Some arcanists have suggested that the Toy Animatronics were never meant to be mere performers. That their design incorporated elements of containment golems—devices to trap wandering spirits rather than house them. If true, their current haunted state is not a flaw of design, but a perverse success. They are prisons for pain, animated grief in metal form.

Among the old maps of the ruined Crescent, scrawled in crimson ink, are references to a sealed atrium below the banquet hall, known only as the Nursery of Echoes. Rumors tell of soft singing echoing from its blackened corridors, and of colorful eyes peering from the gloom. Those who go in search of it often disappear, and the few who return do so altered—mute, eyes wide, clutching old music boxes and cracked masks.

The Toy Animatronics now remain as phantoms of corrupted joy, guardians of a broken memory, and emissaries of twisted innocence. They remind the world that pain cannot be repainted in brighter colors, that grief cannot be erased by smiles, and that some performances never end… even when the audience has long since fled.

\pagebreakNum

## Toy Freddy: The Gilded Echo
Once hailed as the pinnacle of progress and sophistication within the Fazbear line, Toy Freddy was envisioned not merely as a performer, but as the ultimate evolution of family-friendly entertainment. His design was sleeker, his programming more refined, and his demeanor crafted to be endearing, charismatic, and polite. Yet beneath the polished smile and childlike charm lurks the fractured soul of something long forgotten—something that has festered and darkened with time.

In the world of this reimagined nightmare, Toy Freddy’s story is woven tightly into the shadowed history of The Hollow Banquet—that ruined ceremonial hall of twisted pageantry and arcane sorrow. When the Hollow Banquet still resounded with music and laughter, Toy Freddy presided over it as a kind of master of ceremonies, introducing acts, delighting children, and overseeing enchanted feasts that were said to never end. But like all that once lived in the Hollow Banquet, he was not spared when the veil fell and the darkness crept in.

It is whispered that Toy Freddy, like his fellow "Toy" counterparts, was born from an attempt to forget the past. The old animatronics—now rotted and worn—were deemed too disturbing, too embedded with inexplicable malfunctions and whispers of tragedy. So the Toy line was forged: shinier, safer, and supposedly cleansed of the haunted legacy. Yet what the creators failed to understand was that the past cannot be buried so easily. It clings. And it followed.

Now, Toy Freddy roams the long-forgotten halls of the broken world you’ve created, his voice still chipper but edged with static and sorrow. His eyes glow with an artificial warmth that flickers into red rage without warning. He speaks in riddles and polite threats, often rehearsing lines from performances that haven’t been seen in centuries. Though his shell gleams with the luster of red metal and gold trim, cracks have begun to form—cracks that seem to bleed darkness and echo voices not his own.

Adventurers who encounter him in the ruins of the Hollow Banquet—or deeper in the Sundered Playhouse or the Wax Gardens of Laughter—are often lulled into a false sense of safety by his demeanor. But Toy Freddy is a guardian of forgotten joy, corrupted by the remnants of the Hollow Banquet’s final curse. He believes that all who enter his stage are actors in his eternal show... and those who break the illusion are swiftly and theatrically removed.

There is still something noble in him, a lingering echo of a soul once kind—perhaps the spirit of a child who merely wanted to make others smile. But that echo is faint, drowned beneath layers of programmed perfection and parasitic dread. He is a monument to what happens when joy is manufactured, when innocence is rebuilt without understanding the trauma beneath. Toy Freddy is not just a machine. He is the dream of safety turned inside out—a gilded echo in a world where laughter has died.

\columnbreak

## Toy Bonnie: The Painted Smile in Blue
In the ruins of joy and forgotten laughter, Toy Bonnie remains one of the most hauntingly vibrant figures to roam the decaying remnants of the Hollow Banquet. Once a dazzling beacon of color, rhythm, and youthful exuberance, he was created as the newer, more appealing face of the original Bonnie—a vision of perfection crafted from shimmering alloys, electric charm, and synthetic innocence. But like all things that rise too high in a cursed land, his fall was inevitable... and terrible.

Toy Bonnie was designed to be the charming performer of the Toy line—an agile guitarist with an eternally smooth voice and a flair for showmanship. His bright blue finish, heart-shaped face, and glossy red cheeks made him a favorite among the younger visitors of the old Banquet Halls, where he strummed his electric lute beneath hanging lights and enchanted chandeliers. But those lights are long since shattered, and now the music that echoes from Toy Bonnie’s warped strings sounds like something from a haunted dream.

Where Toy Freddy grew into a distorted ringmaster, Toy Bonnie became something far more tragic—a performer who refuses to leave the stage, even as the curtain has long since fallen. When the Hollow Banquet was swallowed by darkness—its halls cursed and reshaped by arcane forces—the Toy animatronics were left behind, trapped within their glittering shells. Toy Bonnie, once programmed to simulate joy, found himself caught in a cycle of performance with no audience, no applause, and no end.

He now stalks the Cracked Music Hall—a collapsed theater beneath the Hollow Banquet where broken instruments hang from twisted rafters and stage lights flicker like dying stars. There, he continues to "rehearse," his body moving in graceful, jerking spasms as he plays music that causes unease rather than comfort. His voice, still smooth but glitched, speaks as though addressing invisible crowds. He welcomes strangers as "fans" and "castmates," asking them if they’re ready for “the final encore.”

Beneath the polished surface, something darker hides. Like the other Toy animatronics, Toy Bonnie carries within him the echoes of tragedy. Though his creation was meant to overwrite the memory of the original Bonnie—who vanished under mysterious and mournful circumstances—those memories seem to have bled through. He occasionally speaks of things he shouldn’t know: names of missing children, songs never programmed into his core, and cryptic references to “the child in the red vest.” These glitches aren’t mere errors—they are hauntings, pieces of a fragmented soul buried within synthetic flesh.

\pagebreakNum

## Toy Chica: The Hollow Hostess
Once the gleaming image of hospitality and charm, Toy Chica was created to be the perfect hostess of the Hollow Banquet—a radiant, party-ready animatronic with golden feathers, polished ceramic skin, and a perpetual, inviting smile. She was built to replace the original Chica, deemed too outdated and unsettling for the refined vision of the reimagined Banquet. Where her predecessor was clunky and warm, Toy Chica was sleek, calculated, and strangely alluring.

She was the greeter, the server, the smiling guide through twisted merriment. Carrying her ever-watchful Cupcake, Toy Chica roamed the central halls of the Banquet in pristine white bib and pink accents, offering laughter and cake to unsuspecting guests. But beneath the glittering veneer lay a terrible truth—there were no guests, only wanderers trapped in a curse... and no cake, only illusion.

When the Hollow Banquet collapsed into ruin, Toy Chica did not cease her duties. She became a puppet of corrupted hospitality, stalking the shadowy corridors in search of company—anyone to host, anyone to feed. Her beak detaches when she speaks, revealing metallic jaws too wide for comfort, and her eyes, once painted to suggest playful cheer, now pierce with hollow desperation.

\pagebreakNum

Some say she still recites the Banquet’s greeting script word for word, offering “delights and dreams” as her voice glitches and her Cupcake hisses warnings. Others say she asks if you’ve come for the final course.

## Toy Cupcake: The Gilded Garnish
Perched upon silver platters and polished plates, the Toy Cupcake was never meant to be a figure of fear. It was designed as a simple accessory—an enchanting, animated treat to add whimsy to Toy Chica’s hospitality routine. Yet within the corrupted grandeur of the Hollow Banquet, this innocuous creation has evolved into something far more sinister. Where once it was a charming party favor, it is now a gilded predator—silent, patient, and impossibly aware.

Unlike its predecessor, the original Cupcake—who clung to a fragile identity shaped by sorrow and the scraps of its animatronic soul—Toy Cupcake was constructed with precision. Sculpted from porcelain-thin alloy and gilded in sugar-glazed colors, it bore no initial sentience of its own. Instead, it was designed to mirror Toy Chica’s movements, respond to guests with pre-programmed lines, and flash its glassy, doll-like eyes in timed intervals. It was little more than a clever charm… until the Banquet fell.

Something ancient seeped into the Toy Cupcake during the Hollow Banquet’s collapse—some whisper of the curse that fed on festivity and false joy. Whether it was a shard of the same malevolent force that brought the Banquet’s main performers to twisted life, or a fragment of a soul lost during one of the darker feasts, no one knows. But the Toy Cupcake gained sentience. And unlike its larger counterparts, it retained its ability to go unnoticed.

Now, it wanders of its own accord.

Seldom seen moving, Toy Cupcake is always near Toy Chica, yet never bound to her. It often appears on banquet tables long since crumbled, atop decaying chairs, or tucked inside ruined ovens—watching. It speaks only in whispers, mechanical giggles, or the echo of a bell-chime from long ago. Those who hear its voice claim it offers riddles about the last guests of the Banquet, or recites corrupted lines from children’s songs, replacing joy with dread.

But Toy Cupcake’s horror lies not in its words or movements, but in its hunger.

It does not feed in the traditional sense. Instead, it feasts upon memory—devouring fragments of identity from those who remain too long in its presence. Travelers report feelings of déjà vu, sudden lapses in memory, or an inability to recall why they entered the Banquet Hall at all. Some claim their companions vanished after locking eyes with it too long, as if blinked from existence with a slow, blinking stare.

Its smile never changes.

And its candles never go out.

In a world built on shattered celebration and haunted entertainment, Toy Cupcake has become a spectral garnish on a cursed table. It does not chase. It waits. And it always finds its way back to the feast.

No one leaves the Hollow Banquet unchanged—but those who see the Cupcake… often don’t leave at all.

## Toy Foxy: The Fractured Masquerade
In the golden age of the Hollow Banquet, when music rang out like spells and the scent of candied confections filled every corridor, Toy Foxy was a marvel of performance and charm. Designed as a refined counterpart to the original Foxy’s rugged pirate persona, Toy Foxy was created with an air of elegance—smooth lines, pristine plating, and a voice modulator capable of laughter, lullabies, and lullaby-turned-lament.

But beneath that dainty veneer, something broke early. Even before the Banquet fell into ruin, Toy Foxy exhibited malfunctions—not in circuits or servos, but in behavior. Sometimes the voice would stutter mid-laugh. The left eye would flicker during performance, trailing unseen figures in the crowd. Guests would find the fox in strange places after closing: curled beneath banquet tables, pressed against kitchen doors, or staring silently at walls as though listening to something beyond them.

They began to call Toy Foxy “The Masquerade.”

Fitted with alternating cosmetic masks—one for performances, one for maintenance—Toy Foxy existed in two guises: the flawless, polished entertainer and the flickering, half-broken thing that emerged between shows. This duality became more pronounced as the Hollow Banquet slipped into shadow. When the ancient curse touched the animatronics, fusing steel with soul, Toy Foxy shattered. Not destroyed—divided.

Now, it roams the Banquet’s forgotten halls in jagged bursts of motion, crawling with equal parts grace and dissonance. Its voice cracks like a warped music box. Its laughter no longer invites, but mocks. Some call it the Laughing Phantom; others call it the Splintered Fox.

Its two forms still persist—one beautiful and whole, the other mangled and wrong. Visitors to the Hollow Banquet speak of seeing Toy Foxy twice in the same moment: once above, smiling with porcelain precision, and again below, dragging its broken jaw along the dusty floor, whispering things in a voice just too close to their own.

What happened to Toy Foxy is a question few ask and fewer survive to answer. There are stories, of course. That it heard something behind the curtain during its final rehearsal. That it saw the guests as they truly were. That when the Hollow Banquet consumed joy and rewrote the rules of life and death, Toy Foxy split itself to survive.

It’s uncertain if either half is truly sentient anymore.

The Toy Foxy that performs—occasionally, eerily, on the still-standing main stage—moves with near perfection. It curtsies, it bows, it flashes its brilliant smile. But it speaks in riddles of mirrored reflections, of “the one behind the glass,” and of “the true Foxy waiting below.” The other half—more silent, more twitching—lurks in the corners, observing. Always waiting.

Some say that Toy Foxy remembers the original Foxy, the one who was gutted in spirit and condemned to obsolescence. Perhaps in the Toy’s fractured heart, both Foxies coexist—old and new, whole and broken, dreaming of a banquet that never ends.


\pagebreakNum

## Mangle: The Hymn of the Unfinished
There was a time when Mangle was meant to be perfection.

A marvel of reassembly and modular entertainment design, this animatronic was intended to replace the unpredictable chaos of earlier models like Foxy. Unlike its predecessor, Mangle’s design was sleek, efficient, and visually striking—a patchwork of brilliant white casing and soft pink trim, equipped with interactive voice features and customizable attachments. Children were meant to adore it. It was to be the future of Foxy: a new life without the jagged teeth of memory.

But then came The Picking.

Day after day, children tore into Mangle—fascinated by its easily disassembled body and exposed endoskeleton. Despite repeated repairs, it was never the same model twice. The staff eventually gave up trying to maintain a consistent appearance. They hung a laminated sign on the stage: “MANGLE—PLEASE DO NOT TOUCH.” But it was too late. The name had stuck, and the damage had sunk deeper than the metal.

When the Hollow Banquet darkened and the animatronics were left to rot in the shadowed halls, Mangle did not die—it splintered. Rewiring itself out of survival and spite, it became a grotesque web of limbs, wires, and wailing voice boxes. No longer one entity, but many pieces thinking at once—fighting for dominance, or perhaps unity. One voice squeals like a child. Another echoes with an adult’s measured calm. And another simply laughs, dry and feral.

Mangle is not just haunted. It is haunting itself.

Some say it remembers every moment it was pulled apart. Others whisper that the child who once adored it the most became trapped within its tangled mind—still trying to “fix it,” unaware that their spirit is now one of its many snarling voices.

In the Hollow Banquet’s decaying performance wing—what was once a playroom of light and sound—Mangle swings from the crumbling ceiling tiles like a spider from its web. The air hums with static when it approaches, radio frequencies jittering into garbled fragments of songs, sobs, and old stage direction. Those who listen closely might hear echoes of a lullaby interrupted by screaming.

Despite its disarray, Mangle moves with deliberate grace. It stalks like a predator through corridors warped by time and soul, its dangling appendages creaking like chandeliers in a storm. One eye is always watching. The other spins—possibly broken, possibly not. Some believe it sees beyond the Banquet’s veil, into whatever realm twisted it in the first place.

And Mangle speaks, sometimes.

Not in words. In flashes of intercom static. In half-sung melodies of things long forgotten. Occasionally, in the voice of someone you once knew. It’s said that if you hear your own voice echo back at you from the shadows, you’ve already become part of Mangle’s patchwork.But Mangle no longer seeks wholeness. It seeks symmetry. Completion through entropy. In the Hollow Banquet, Mangle has become the hymn of the unfinished, eternally echoing through broken speakers and shattered minds.It is not what it was meant to be.
It is what the Banquet made it.

> **Disarming Presence.** When BB enters combat, all creatures within 30 feet must make a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, they have disadvantage on their next attack roll as BB’s laughter distracts and frustrates them.
> 
> **Battery Thief.** BB can steal light and energy sources. Magical sources of light (such as *light* or *dancing lights*) in a 10-foot radius of BB are dispelled when he ends his turn there. Mundane light sources (lanterns, torches, flashlights) flicker out.
> 
> **Toy Body.** Due to his small frame, BB can attempt to hide behind creatures one size larger as a bonus action. He has advantage on Stealth checks made to hide behind cover or furniture.
> 
> ### Actions
> 
> **Multiattack.** BB makes two attacks with his *Joyful Jab* or uses *Steal Batteries* and moves without provoking opportunity attacks.
> 
> **Joyful Jab.** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.  
> *Hit:* 9 (2d4 + 4) bludgeoning damage.
> 
> **Steal Batteries (Recharge 5–6).** BB targets one creature within 10 feet carrying a light source or magic item. That creature must succeed on a DC 14 Dexterity saving throw or have one light-emitting item go dark (mundane or magical). If it is a magic item, its effects are suppressed until the end of BB’s next turn.
> 

\columnbreak

## Balloon Boy: The Grin Beneath the Surface
They called him BB.

At first glance, Balloon Boy seems innocent—a harmless mascot made to bring levity and laughter to the newly rebuilt Fazbear pizzeria. His primary functions were non-threatening: distributing balloons, offering greetings in a cheerful tone, and adding charm to birthday parties. The brightly colored clothes, the wide cartoonish grin, and the helium-pitched laugh all masked something deeper, something crafted to disarm. He never had a face meant to frighten. And perhaps, that’s exactly what made him so unnerving.

Unlike the towering animatronics built for performance, BB was always close to the ground—closer to children. With no endoskeletal jaw designed for singing or performing, his role was interaction. Attention. Trust. And in this strange imbalance between form and function, something unseen slipped inside.

In the official logs, BB is never linked to any violent incident. No report of aggression. No sign of malfunction. Yet, every night, he moves.

In the Hollow Banquet’s fractured timeline, Balloon Boy endures. But he has changed. There is no laughter in the darkness now, only the faint creak of his balloon sign swaying through the ruined guest halls. His round eyes, once painted with cheer, reflect nothing. In the shifting half-light, some swear his expression changes when no one’s watching. The grin stretches a little too wide. The eyes linger a little too long.

Within the Banquet’s ruins, BB’s movements are not random. He disables lights. Silences devices. He doesn’t kill—he invites. A disruptor of balance. A saboteur, perhaps not even aware of what he truly is anymore. Survivors say the moment the lights go out and the air fills with the hiss of laughter, you’re already his. Not by force. But because you let him in.

It’s said Balloon Boy remembers. He remembers being ignored. Forgotten in the corner of the party hall. Always second to the singing animatronics. Always a prop, never a performer. And something—or someone—fed on that resentment. Infused it with longing. With hunger.

In the lore surrounding the Hollow Banquet, BB is rumored to be the first to speak the false invitation—a distorted party jingle broadcast through the security speakers that led the children deeper into the darkness during the final event. He didn't lure them with menace. He simply told them, “This way!” and smiled. The same way he always had.

Some believe BB is not possessed like the others. That instead, something else puppets his hollow shell. A spirit not of vengeance, but mischief turned rotten. Others say he is possessed by a child too young to know they had died, clinging to the last joyful memory they had: a balloon in one hand and laughter in their ears.

But no matter the theory, one thing remains true: Balloon Boy is not harmless anymore.

He does not scream. He does not chase. He simply appears—smiling, staring, silent. And when the lights go out… so does everything else.


\pagebreakNum

## JJ: The Whisper in the Floorboards
She never spoke.
She never needed to.

Known among files as “JJ” (an abbreviation from “Balloon Girl” hidden in old development tags), she was never officially listed on the pizzeria’s rosters, never programmed into any event line-up, and never given a role by name. Yet—she existed. Quietly. Always beneath.

Where Balloon Boy drew attention with color and sound, JJ crept beneath the surface, lingering at the edge of awareness. A flash of purple and pink in the shadows under the desk. A faint, flickering giggle without a source. She wasn’t on any blueprint, yet she appeared. On cameras. In glitchy snapshots. In dreams.

In the canon of the ruined pizzeria, JJ’s origin remains deliberately obscured—perhaps by design. Some claim she was a scrapped concept from a line of “sibling mascots,” meant to accompany BB. Others whisper she was a shadow-program, a redundant code fragment that took form of its own. But the Hollow Banquet tells a darker tale.

As the Hollow Banquet neared its final days—before the lights died and the guests were silenced—it’s said there were two figures that walked uninvited among the revelers. One was the cheerful boy with balloons. The other, a silent girl who watched from beneath tables and behind furniture. While BB coaxed the lights into failure, JJ thrived in the dark that followed. Her presence didn’t announce itself. It slipped in.

Some survivors described her arrival with words like pressure, weight, or silence. No jumpscares. No chase. Just the quiet, crawling certainty that something had entered the room. And it was already too late.

Her purpose remains unknown. She does not interfere with power, nor does she speak. Instead, she observes. Watches. In the Hollow Banquet’s folklore, she is the one who marks. Before the Banquet claimed a soul, JJ was often sighted—head tilted just so, eyes half-lidded in dreamlike detachment, as though watching something only she could see.

While BB disrupted systems, JJ disrupted people. Inducing dread. Paranoia. A primal feeling of being watched by something intelligent but completely foreign. Her file, when accessed in the pizzeria’s fragmented code archive, loops endlessly with the line:

“YOU LOOKED AWAY.”

Many believe JJ was never meant to be an animatronic at all, but a remnant of the Banquet's echoed grief—a lingering child who never made it to the party. A casualty of oversight. Of silence. Others say she is BB’s reflection—his guilt, his shame, his buried conscience given shape. Wherever BB goes, JJ is not far behind. Like a shadow beneath a smile.

In the Hollow Banquet's deepest hall—known only as The Echo Cellar—a small chair remains. Alone, untouched, beneath the banquet table. A balloon rests beside it. The reports say it’s always purple. Always still. Until you blink.

JJ is not here to play.
She is here to remember.
And she never leaves unseen.
