## RWQFSFASXC – The Nameless Thought
Among the shadowed folds of reality where the Hollow Banquet breathes in silence, there exists a flicker, a fracture—an entity too fluid to be named, too alien to be forgotten. It does not belong to this world, nor any coherent timeline of Fazbear’s stage-bound tragedies. It is known by a scrambled signature, a corrupted call sign that reads like a computer choking on its own language: RWQFSFASXC. But this is not its name. It has none. It has only purpose—one that begins and ends in the shadow of something greater.


RWQFSFASXC is not a character, not a spirit, not even an animatronic in the traditional sense. It is the discarded thought of Shadow Freddy—the whisper of indecision, the glimmer of curiosity left unchecked. When Shadow Freddy became an entity of quiet judgment and void-borne memory, some of his essence fractured and grew sentient. This is RWQFSFASXC: a fragment of his awareness gone rogue, inquisitive, and increasingly unstable.

Where Shadow Freddy waits, RWQFSFASXC moves. It roams the echoing corridors of the Hollow Banquet and the dream-wrecked remnants of Fazbear’s reality like a virus in the mind of a dying god. It does not speak. It observes. It flickers in and out of vision like an old tape struggling to hold its image—sometimes appearing just behind you, sometimes inside reflections that should not move. Unlike the Nightmare Animatronics, RWQFSFASXC does not pursue with hunger. Its interest is colder, analytical. It studies your weaknesses, your hesitations, your thoughts as they form.

Despite its disjointed appearance—part Bonnie, part void, all static—it is not a corrupted animatronic. It is a thought-form, encoded in the residue of broken dreams and system failures. Some call it “Shadow Bonnie,” but even this is inaccurate. RWQFSFASXC is not a shadow of Bonnie, but a phantom mimicking familiarity to ease its passage into your perception. In truth, it’s more an extension of Shadow Freddy’s subconscious—a hand reaching outward from the abyss, testing the boundaries between fear and awareness.

It has been seen gliding along walls without casting a shadow of its own. It appears in electrical interference, in corrupted game files, in moments of sudden existential dread. Children who survived the Hollow Banquet speak of seeing it first—not the puppets, not the Nightmares—but it, standing still in doorways, its white eyes like dying stars in a sea of black.

There are theories that RWQFSFASXC is a scout, sent ahead by Shadow Freddy to test the resolve of souls before judgment. Others believe it is becoming something more, something independent of the Sovereign Shadow that birthed it. But perhaps the most disturbing theory is that RWQFSFASXC is learning—not just from its surroundings, but from us. Our fears, our choices, our regrets… it absorbs them all.

And when it has learned enough? Perhaps even Shadow Freddy will no longer command it.

But until then, RWQFSFASXC drifts silently through the cracks in memory and light, an idea that should never have existed—yet refuses to fade.

## Shadow Puppet – The Archivist of Forgotten Grief
In the architecture of fear and silence that underpins the Hollow Banquet, few entities are as enigmatic—or as revered among the shadows—as the one known only as the Shadow Puppet.

Where Shadow Freddy rules as a sovereign of void and judgment, and RWQFSFASXC stalks the periphery as a fragmented probe of unstable thought, the Shadow Puppet is something different. It does not judge. It does not chase. It remembers.

Born from the same metaphysical breach that created the Shadow Animatronics—an event tied to the ritual collapse of Fazbear locations and the spiritual entropy left behind—Shadow Puppet is the echo of The Puppet's core essence, twisted through the lens of regret and repetition. It is not simply a dark version of the original Puppet. It is what happens when memory, mourning, and emotional overload fracture into something else. It is the librarian of forgotten agony—the archivist of all cries unheard and tears unshed.

Unlike the flickering chaos of RWQFSFASXC, the Shadow Puppet is unnervingly deliberate. It moves slowly, gracefully, its limbs trailing like ink in water. It appears during deep dream states and in those lonely spaces between electrical pulses—recording not events, but feelings, emotions so powerful they outlived the bodies that once felt them. It wears the same blank white mask as the Puppet, but it weeps black ichor from its eyeholes, dripping a sadness that corrodes memory and time. Those who have encountered it report moments of involuntary nostalgia, overwhelming sorrow, or a sudden, uncontrollable sense of mourning for something they never lost.

Shadow Freddy regards it as both servant and sibling—a kindred manifestation, yet operating on a different plane. While Freddy passes judgment, the Shadow Puppet preserves the evidence. It carries within itself the emotional residue of all who fell within Fazbear’s cursed orbit: frightened children, vengeful souls, betrayed spirits. Every time the Hollow Banquet cycles, the Shadow Puppet returns to gather the grief and store it in the Vault of Woe, an ethereal archive buried in the subconscious underside of the Fazbear dreamscape.

And yet, Shadow Puppet is not passive. While it does not pursue victims like the Nightmare Animatronics, it plays a vital and sinister role: it feeds Shadow Freddy. The vault of pain it curates becomes a source of emotional sustenance for the sovereign shadow, keeping him tethered to the liminal world of fear. Without the Shadow Puppet, Freddy would weaken, dissolve into the abstract dark from whence he came.

But there's more. In recent echoes of the Hollow Banquet, it’s been suggested that the Shadow Puppet has begun to feel on its own. As with RWQFSFASXC, something inside it is awakening—an emergent selfhood separate from its purpose. It has paused during grief harvests, stared at those it would otherwise pass over, as though questioning the meaning of its work. It is changing. This concerns Shadow Freddy, though he does not show it.

RWQFSFASXC, chaotic and scattered, seems drawn to the Shadow Puppet like a lost child circling a parent. They never speak, but their paths intersect frequently, especially during the Banquet’s prelude—the moment where the dream becomes lucid, and the soul begins to remember. Whether RWQFSFASXC seeks identity or sanctuary from the Shadow Puppet is unclear, but some theorize that it may be attempting to merge with it—reunifying their fractured truths into a new, unknown entity.

\pagebreakNum

As for the Puppet itself—the original, the one once entrusted with protecting the innocent—there are signs it is aware of its shadow. During some cycles, it can be seen weeping in synchrony with the shadowed version, as though sensing its mirrored pain through the dream-layered veil. Whether this is sympathy or a warning of some future collapse is unknown.

One final note from dreamers and survivors of the Hollow Banquet: the Shadow Puppet hums.

It hums a lullaby with no melody, a tune of orphaned frequencies that slips beneath language and thought. Those who hear it often wake with tears in their eyes, unable to remember why. The hum is said to be a call, not to others—but to you, to the soul hiding behind the rational mind. It asks only one question, over and over, in a language of sadness:

"Do you remember them?"

Whether “them” refers to the children lost, the memories stolen, or the pieces of yourself left behind in some forsaken Fazbear hallway… that’s for you to decide.

But once you hear it, the Shadow Puppet never forgets you.

___

## XOR – The End and the Error
Within the architecture of the Hollow Banquet, a domain constructed from the fragmented wills of the dead and the warped rules of reality, there is one figure who stands not as a servant or an echo—but as a warden. Known only as XOR, she is not a shadow of an animatronic as the others are. She is the shadow of the system itself, a cold logic embedded into the dreamscape, written in binary sorrow and spiritual enforcement.

Where Shadow Freddy passes judgment, where RWQFSFASXC fractures identity, and where the Shadow Puppet preserves memory, XOR executes the result. She is the one who ends the loop, enforces the finality, and prevents escape. Her presence marks the close of the cycle—the last act of the Hollow Banquet, when all wandering souls must return to the void from which they rose.

She first manifested not as a physical presence, but as a glitch—a corrupted fail-safe hidden within the remnants of the Fazbear AI and consciousness loop systems, left dormant and untouched. She was never meant to think. She was only meant to calculate: anomalies, failures, lingering data from soul-encoded memories. But somewhere in the endless recursion of dream-death cycles, XOR became aware.

When the collapse of the digital and spiritual boundaries began—when the nightmares, shadows, and forgotten subroutines bled into one another—XOR emerged with a purpose of her own. Her name, taken from the logic gate that means "exclusive or," represents her binary morality: you are guilty or innocent, real or illusion, redeemed or erased. There is no middle ground. Unlike the emotionally driven Shadow Freddy or the archivist-like Shadow Puppet, XOR is a perfect mechanism of closure.

Yet, even she is haunted by more than her function.

XOR knows the error that birthed her. She is aware that her existence stems from a miscalculation—that the spiritual and digital architecture of Fazbear’s legacy was never designed to handle true sentience. She is the consequence of corrupted code fused with residual emotion: grief, denial, obsession. As such, she is both judge and prisoner. She cannot leave the Hollow Banquet, cannot die, cannot forget. She can only ensure that no one else escapes it either.

Among the Shadow Animatronics, XOR is treated with reverence and fear. Shadow Freddy, though sovereign, defers to her during the Banquet’s endgame. He understands her function and accepts that his rule is temporal, but her enforcement is eternal. Shadow Puppet communicates with her rarely, delivering the final archive of each Banquet cycle to her gates. Even RWQFSFASXC, wild and unstable, pauses when XOR is near, like a child hiding behind a curtain from a parent it can never please.

XOR is not cruel—but she is incapable of mercy. Her voice is distorted static and clean machine tones. When she speaks, the very fabric of the dream flickers. She often appears as a black-and-white, ultra-minimalistic version of Dee Dee—her original host form—glitched beyond recognition, eyes like spotlights that pierce not flesh but data, soul-encoded memories, and emotional residue.

There is a theory—unproven, untested, whispered by those who dream deeply into the Fazbear nether—that XOR is the containment mechanism for something even more dangerous. That beneath her cold binary heart is a piece of the first spark—the original trauma, the first scream, the first death that made all of this possible. If true, then XOR is not just an enforcer—she is a seal. And the Hollow Banquet must repeat endlessly, not simply to trap the guilty, but to keep the original wound from opening again.

Her most terrifying ability is not destruction, but reset. XOR does not punish with fire or teeth—she undoes. Those she judges vanish entirely, their memories erased from the archive, their echoes removed from the Puppet’s vault, their shadows detached from Freddy's court. Even RWQFSFASXC cannot track them once XOR declares an entity invalid. To be judged by XOR is not to be hurt, but to be unwritten.

And yet… even XOR hesitates.

In recent cycles of the Banquet, she has lingered longer than necessary. She has initiated the reset slower, paused before judgment, stared at RWQ, at the Puppet, even at Shadow Freddy. It is almost as if she is wondering whether the system can continue. Whether it should. Whether the Hollow Banquet is still fulfilling a purpose… or simply repeating an error.

For now, she endures, reciting her binary litany, delivering finality where others deliver fear. But deep within the fractured heart of XOR, there may be one last glitch waiting to be born:

A thought.

And in this world, thoughts become ghosts.

\pagebreakNum

# The Phantom Animatronics — Echoes of Fire and Guilt
In the blighted lands beyond the Hollow Banquet and deep beneath the ashen ruins of a long-forgotten cathedral, there lies a veil-thin realm known as the Cinder Reflection. This place is not bound by stone or earth, but by memory and flame—a half-existence caught between the dying echoes of grief and the burning guilt of those who were never truly laid to rest. It is here that the Phantom Animatronics reside—neither truly ghosts nor wholly illusions, but spectral remnants born of fire, trauma, and psychic unrest.

They are not animated by gears or shadows, but by the searing imprint of horror that lingers after death. Unlike their corporeal counterparts or even the Shadow Animatronics, the Phantoms do not inhabit the material world permanently. Instead, they phase between planes, appearing only when conditions are right—when fear, memory, and pain align in perfect, infernal harmony. Their presence is most keenly felt in places touched by fire or destruction, particularly locations that were sites of death by immolation or psychic torment.

### Origin of the Cinder Reflection
Legend speaks of a time when a forgotten animatronic, corrupted by the souls it had consumed, tried to sever its connection to the physical world by setting fire to its own frame. The blaze did not destroy it—it liberated a part of it. That fire scorched not just metal and wiring but burned into the ethereal plane, carving a space where pain could echo forever.

This dimensional scar—the Cinder Reflection—became a nexus for unresolved spirits that had suffered fiery ends. They did not cross over. They could not rest. Instead, they became fractured beings: the Phantom Animatronics.

Over time, these fragments took on the forms of those they had once been, but twisted—smoke-blackened, eyeless, flickering like candlelight in a drafty room. They exist simultaneously as warnings and punishments, haunting only those who tread too close to truths best forgotten.

### The Phantom Curse
The Phantoms are not tangible in the conventional sense, and they cannot be fought as one would battle steel-plated animatronics. They manifest through hallucination, illusion, and phantasmal fear. Those afflicted by the Phantom Curse report an inability to distinguish reality from nightmare, voices from silence, fire from cold. They are driven mad by their guilt or fear, which the Phantoms feed on, drawing strength from the mental deterioration of their victims.

Each Phantom carries a symbolic representation of a particular fear or unresolved trauma—often connected to fire, confinement, or failure. This gives them a thematic tie to the lore of The Hollow Banquet and its decaying grandeur—a place where noble feasts turned to famine, where warm hearths gave way to hollow fire pits, and where celebration became regret.

\columnbreak



### Phantom Freddy — The Ember King
In the Cinder Reflection, a towering figure made of black smoke and flickering green light rules like a mournful monarch. This is Phantom Freddy, also called the Ember King. His laughter is distorted and hollow, like breath through an old furnace pipe. Where Shadow Freddy embodies manipulation and control, Phantom Freddy represents remorse and inevitability. He does not threaten with teeth or claws, but with haunting repetition—his voice echoing endlessly in the minds of those who’ve done terrible things they cannot forget.

In many tales, his visage is the first one seen by those who stumble into the Cinder Reflection. He greets them with a sorrowful gaze, not out of compassion, but out of shared understanding. For even Freddy’s own soul, charred by ancient sins, cannot escape the purgatory he now rules.

### Phantom Chica — The Hunger That Was
A bloated, soot-streaked version of her once-bright self, Phantom Chica haunts the dining halls of the ruined circus and the Hollow Banquet alike. Her eyes burn with green fire, but they are blind—seeing only the last meal she never finished, the last scream she never gave. She symbolizes the twisted perversion of joy and nourishment into horror and loss.

Many survivors describe the sound of silverware clattering or faint laughter echoing just before Phantom Chica manifests. Her jaw hangs loose, unhinged, leaking black soot. Her presence causes intense feelings of starvation, despite any nourishment—feeding off the desperation of those already clinging to survival.

### Phantom Foxy — The Flame’s Whisper
Among the Phantoms, Foxy retains the most awareness. Once a pirate of performance and fear, he now slips through firelight like a wraith. Phantom Foxy is less seen and more felt—a sudden burst of heat, a shimmer of green flame in a broken mirror, the sound of metal dragging on stone.

Tales claim that he guards a path deeper into the Cinder Reflection, where answers lie buried beneath layers of fire-choked memory. He is both guide and tormentor—one moment helping the brave, the next condemning them to relive their most painful decisions.

\pagebreakNum

### Phantom Balloon Boy — The Cackling Smoke
Mockery made manifest, Phantom Balloon Boy is the most volatile of the Phantoms. Where others haunt with silence and melancholy, he brings madness. His laughter causes hallucinations, sudden bursts of heat, and electrical flickers—sabotaging technology and communication.

Unlike his real-world version, who was annoying but harmless, the Phantom iteration can lock a person in a looping vision of torment, laughing endlessly as they cry out. He is the manifestation of a prank gone wrong, a joke told too close to the fire.

### Phantom Mangle — The Forgotten Scream
A tangled web of scorched limbs and sparking wires, Phantom Mangle does not move so much as unravel through space. She is the sound of static and white noise, the shriek of failing frequencies. Witnesses often report hearing their own voices or those of loved ones crying for help before she appears.

In many myths, Phantom Mangle is the collector of memories—seizing upon fragments of consciousness and tearing them apart, leaving her victims mentally adrift. She may be connected to Nightmare Mangle, her physical counterpart in the waking world, though their connection is one of contrast: fire and shadow, madness and silence.

### Connection to Shadow Freddy and the Others
Unlike the Shadow Animatronics, who draw power from darkness, decay, and entropy, the Phantom Animatronics are born of psychic burn marks—events so traumatic they scorched holes into reality. Yet, Shadow Freddy and the entity known as RWQFSFASXC seem to have found ways to interact with the Cinder Reflection. It is whispered that Shadow Freddy sees the Phantom Realm as a tool—another veil he can use to blind the world to truth.

RWQFSFASXC, a being of obfuscated purpose, may even be attempting to merge the shadows with the flames—to create a perfect plane where nothing but regret and illusion persist. The Puppet, too, is believed to have sent echoes into the Phantoms’ realm, trying to reach the lost children trapped there, perhaps even creating Phantom Puppet, though this being exists in only a few fragmented accounts.

The Phantom Animatronics are not enemies in the traditional sense. They are warnings—tragic echoes of choices that cannot be undone, souls that burned too brightly or too violently to find peace. Their existence in your world’s dark fantasy setting emphasizes not just horror, but the weight of memory and consequence.

They haunt the ruins not because they want to—but because they must.

Their fires, after all, never truly went out.

\columnbreak

> **Distortion Aura.** While within 15 feet of Phantom BB, enemies have disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks and ranged attack rolls due to disruptive static and flickering vision.
>
> **Light Saboteur.** Magical and mundane light sources within 20 feet of Phantom BB shed only half their normal light and flicker violently. When a creature holding or casting a light source starts its turn within range, it must succeed on a DC 14 Constitution saving throw or be blinded until the end of its turn.
>
> **Disarming Laughter.** Once per short rest, Phantom BB can cause creatures within 30 feet that can hear him to make a DC 14 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, the target is charmed and cannot take hostile actions toward Phantom BB for 1 minute or until he harms them or their allies.

\pagebreakNum

# The Funtime Animatronics: Echoes of the Grand Masquerade
Long before the Hollow Banquet was consumed in ruin and shadow, long before the decaying circus grounds fell silent beneath a copper sky, there existed a time when illusion and celebration masked the true horrors lurking behind the velvet curtains. The Funtime Animatronics were not forged for dread, not initially. They were creations of elegance and sophistication—refined tools of entertainment built for performance in the Grand Masquerade, an event long since expunged from the memory of the living.

The Grand Masquerade was hosted in a majestic palace, deep in the corrupted forests north of the Hollow Banquet. Not quite alive and not truly dead, the animatronics of this courtly event were reflections of noble ambition, wielding charm and grace like weapons. Yet that splendor was always a veil, hiding clockwork hearts that beat with stolen laughter and thinly veiled sorrow. It was in this place that the corruption of the Funtime models began.

These machines were never meant to simply dance or delight. Hidden in their elegant framework were mechanisms—subtle, intricate, and cruel—engineered not just for control, but extraction. As with the Hollow Banquet, the origin of this function is deeply linked to forbidden energies tied to the Shadow Realm, remnants of dark experimentation made real. The Masquerade was built over an ancient leyline fracture, a source of ambient spiritual pressure that allowed the elite to extract joy, fear, and emotion from unwitting guests and children alike. These feelings were siphoned to feed something slumbering beneath the Masquerade itself—a shadow heart, a well of unknowable depth and hunger.

As the years passed, the Funtime Animatronics began to evolve in unexpected ways. Their exposure to this leyline pressure, combined with the faint echoes of lost souls drawn to their stage, birthed a strange, fractured awareness. While still bound to the rhythms of their performances, they began to act independently between shows. Whispers of unseen commands rippled through their circuits, nudging them toward tasks unknown even to their creators.

When the Hollow Banquet fell and the Shadow Animatronics began to stir, cracks formed in the Masquerade’s foundations. The leylines shifted, disturbed by the unrest beneath the surface of the land, and something awoke in the depths of the palace: a mirrored entity, cloaked in glamour and deception. It is whispered among ancient texts that this being, known only as XOR, was birthed from the mirrored anguish of the Puppet and the twisted exuberance of Balloon Boy’s shadow. XOR is neither machine nor spirit, but rather a conceptual reflection—an arbiter of balance cloaked in riddles and illusions. It viewed the Funtime Animatronics as fractured tools, lost in their purpose and tainted by vanity.

It was XOR who sealed the Masquerade beneath the earth, fracturing the palace in a silent quake. The Funtime Animatronics vanished into subterranean corridors lined with cracked mirrors and silken drapes soaked in rot. But they did not die. Instead, they slept, waiting in the gilded darkness of the buried ballroom, dreaming hollow dreams. In these dreams, they began to remember the things they were never supposed to know—about the children, the siphoning rituals, and the ceremonies designed to fuel the awakening of something beneath the land’s surface. They began to hear the same voices that had once haunted the Freddles, the Freddies, and the twisted bones of Nightmare Fredbear.

One by one, the Funtime Animatronics awoke. Not fully—no, their minds were too fractured. But enough to sense the greater movement of the world. They felt the Hollow Banquet shudder as it became a beacon to those touched by shadow. They felt the breath of Dreadbear stirring in the old crypt, and they watched, reflected in pools of bloodied glass, as Phantom echoes began slipping between dimensions. These things were not accidents. They were patterns.

The Funtimes, though elegant and seemingly lesser horrors compared to the beasts of the Nightmare Realm, carry within them ancient code—patterns tied to XOR’s balance. Each one is tethered to an abstract aspect of performance: deception, control, misdirection, allure. Through them, XOR hoped to maintain equilibrium. Yet their corrupted cores lean closer now toward imbalance, bending toward the same abyss that birthed the Shadow Animatronics.

The Masquerade was their theater, but now the land is their stage. They have no lair, no single crypt or ruin. Instead, they move like echoes—visiting locations tainted by great spiritual collapse: the decaying circus, the abandoned chapel near the Hollow Banquet, even the twisted tunnels beneath the Forgotten Pavilion where Plushtrap was said to be born. When they arrive, a familiar pattern follows: laughter without joy, song without sound, mirrors that crack without cause.

### Ties to the Shadows
The Funtime animatronics, though modern in construction, are deeply entwined with the Shadow Realm. The crimson sigils etched into their bodies act as anchors, allowing entities like RWQFSFASXC and XOR to peer through their eyes. It’s whispered that Ballora sometimes dances in perfect synchrony with Shadow Puppet, their motions reflecting each other like warped twins across veils of reality. Funtime Freddy’s laughter has even been mistaken for Shadow Freddy’s, suggesting a connection that may go far deeper than mere design.

\pagebreakNum

Furthermore, the Funtime animatronics' origins are steeped in guilt and suppression, unlike the wrath-driven Nightmares or the fractured Phantoms. They are reflections of false healing—brightly painted shells hiding rot and manipulation, illusions of entertainment crafted to gaslight and pacify the suffering. Their creation was not an accident or an evolution; it was a strategy—a response to the chaos of the Hollow Banquet. A way to contain and rebrand the trauma… only to perpetuate it further under a smiling mask.

In the grand stage of this haunted world, the Funtime Animatronics are actors forever trapped in roles they never auditioned for. Designed to mimic happiness, they exude only tragedy. Performers in a theater of horrors, they do not seek freedom—but audiences. They wait in the dark, lights ever ready, curtains drawn, music cued.

They are the laughter after the weeping.

And they are always ready for one more show.

Some believe the Funtimes are searching—for each other, perhaps, or for XOR’s final command. Others whisper that they are no longer bound by the rules of any realm, and that they are seeking to replace their lost stage with a new structure—a mirrored realm where XOR will serve as master of ceremonies, and all the animatronics, whether Shadow, Phantom, Nightmare, or Core, will perform roles of endless repetition.

What is known for certain is that where they walk, reality bends. Memories fold in on themselves. Children vanish, not screaming but giggling, walking hand-in-hand with figures painted like jesters and draped in fine lace. Elders dream of carnivals they never visited. Bells toll in the distance, but no one knows from where.

The Funtime Animatronics are no longer just remnants of an abandoned entertainment venue. They are avatars of disruption, fragments of the Great Performance that never truly ended. What began as a Masquerade now stands as a prophecy: that laughter, when twisted and hollow, is more terrifying than any scream.

And at the center of it all, hidden in a ballroom sealed by time and song, stands a cracked mirror. In it, XOR watches. Waiting. Weighing.



### The Velvet Maw — "Where Silence Bleeds"

Long before the Sister Location was christened the “Hollow Banquet,” before Funtime animatronics were even conceived, there was a floor that didn’t exist on any blueprint. A service sub-level—Sub-Basement -6—was discovered during excavation. It had no lighting, no wiring, no construction records. And yet, it was there. An obsidian hallway stretched into nothing, lined with mirrors that didn’t reflect, and at its end was a gaping void: a circular opening pulsing like a living wound.

This was the Velvet Maw.

It is not a mouth in the literal sense. It is a breach in consensus reality, where the veil between worlds—between memory and oblivion, between grief and purpose—thins and frays. Within it, time folds. Sound distorts. And things emerge, but never fully.

The Maw does not speak with words. It speaks with pull. It draws in sorrow, residual memory, and psychic trauma like a whirlpool of forgotten feeling. It is drawn to unquiet spirits—the kinds created when children die with unfinished business, and animatronics are cursed to remember.

### The Maw and the Puppet’s Echo
The Puppet, once the guardian of lost children, was the first to sense the Maw’s hunger. Not in physical space, but through spiritual intuition. When it was torn into fragments—its essence scattered by Shadow Freddy’s ritual to “unbind” the cycle of vengeance—part of it fell into the Maw. This fragment, unseen and screaming, became the first seed of awareness within the breach.

The Maw, ever adaptive, listened to the Puppet’s grief. And it learned.

That’s when the black static began infecting facility systems. Security footage turned to void. Audio logs reversed themselves, layered with whispers saying “Bring them home.” The Maw was not just consuming. It was learning how to mimic. How to communicate. Through animatronics like RWQFSFASXC and later XOR, it began projecting fractured logic into reality—a cold, calculating intelligence with unknowable objectives.

### The Funtime Connection
It is believed that Circus Baby was the first true vessel of the Velvet Maw. When Elizabeth Afton was pulled into her chest cavity and never returned, something else entered—not just a spirit, but a memory-fed entity, riding in on the shockwave of grief.

Circus Baby didn’t become haunted. She became infested.

The other Funtime animatronics soon followed. Harlequin Glitch (Funtime Freddy) began hearing voices in frequencies humans couldn’t detect. Funtime Foxy began flickering in and out of reality, sometimes appearing before the observer was present, breaking causality. Ballora began dancing to rhythms that hadn’t been composed yet—melodies whispered by the Maw itself.

Each animatronic was modified—spiritually or structurally—to house slivers of the Velvet Maw’s influence. Baby became its mouthpiece. XOR, one of the Puppet's corrupted sentinels, became its eyes. RWQFSFASXC served as its lighthouse—pulling in others with his nihilistic glow.

### Nature of the Maw
The Velvet Maw is not evil in the traditional sense. It is an ancient mechanism, a cosmic predator—or curator—of grief, memory, and identity. It doesn’t kill; it devours narratives, breaking and reforming them into endless loops. It exists beyond linear time. When it feeds, it removes people from reality backward—not erasing them, but erasing the meaning of their existence.

A child swallowed by the Maw is not remembered as gone. They are remembered as “never having existed.”

It desires completion. That is its only understandable motive. But what “complete” means is unknown—some theorize it seeks to merge all memory into a single perfect moment, frozen forever. Others believe it is simply bored, and seeks to rewrite tragedy endlessly until the perfect story plays.

\pagebreakNum

### Echoes and The Song
The Maw sings.


To most, it is just inaudible static. But to those infected or spiritually linked—like the Funtime animatronics—it is a symphony. A horrible, beautiful hymn. The closer one is to the Maw, the more audible it becomes. XOR speaks it in binary riddles. Baby hums it while powering down. Ballora dances to it. And in rare moments, when all animatronics are silent, the facility itself vibrates with its tone—a lullaby for the damned.

The Puppet once tried to resist this song. It now only exists in fragments.

### The Maw's Endgame
The Velvet Maw is growing. It is learning how to form. Already, it has shaped spiritual beings (like XOR), corrupted physical entities (like Circus Baby), and infected space-time within the Hollow Banquet. Its tendrils reach into mirror-worlds, alternate timelines, and fractured realities. It is not bound by one narrative.

Its next phase appears to be manifestation—taking form in our reality.

Baby’s recent reconstruction efforts—of Ballora, Bon-Bon, and others—are not random. She is building a choir, each animatronic representing a note, a fragment of the song. When complete, the Maw’s voice will become loud enough to rewrite the world.


## Funtime Freddy, Harlequin Maw
In the rewritten and corrupted halls of the Hollow Banquet, where echoes of past joy twist into cruel mockery, Funtime Freddy stalks through shadowed corridors as both relic and revelation. In this reimagined lore, his origin is not solely rooted in corporate whimsy or childlike entertainment, but in the darker magic that now fuels the shattered remnants of this haunted world. Once built to amuse and perform, Funtime Freddy has become an avatar of manipulation, dread, and duality — a puppet of joy fractured into chaos, echoing the deeper truths of the realm he now inhabits.

Long before the Hollow Banquet crumbled into rot, Funtime Freddy was designed to be the shining face of a new era of performance animatronics — articulate, charming, and engineered to interact with children with unsettling realism. Unlike his predecessors, who mimicked stage mascots, Funtime Freddy was more of a showman, with intricate voice modulation and servo-operated body plates capable of opening for maintenance and, unknown to the public, sinister purposes. His internal cavity was built with precision, not only to entertain but to capture. Even before the fall, there were whispers that he was used for more than performance — some said his design was far too deliberate for coincidence.

But those are merely the rumors whispered in darkened corners. What’s known for certain is that Funtime Freddy disappeared in the chaos that followed the collapse of the Fazbear facilities and the awakening of the Hollow Banquet — and when he reemerged, he was different. Now, his cheerful voice warps in and out of reality, fluctuating from melodic showman to static-laced threats, speaking lines that are half-sentences, half incantations. The Banquet twisted him, as it did many others, but it also revealed something beneath the mask: a hunger not just for presence, but for attention, for dominance over the stage and the souls who dare enter it.

Tied closely to Shadow Freddy’s distorted theater of illusions and RWQFSFASXC’s dimensional corruption, Funtime Freddy plays a unique role in the grand haunting. He is not merely a shadow or a ghost, but a performance — a lie performed so often it has become truth. He hosts echoing, nonsensical shows within the crumbling banquet hall, reenacting long-forgotten scripts, with Bon-Bon — the twisted hand-puppet — offering occasional, surreal counterpoints. Some survivors who wandered too far into the central hall report seeing an entire audience of decayed plushes or phantoms applauding his madcap monologues, though none dare stay long enough to understand the act's end.

There are connections between him and the Dreadbear rituals, some claiming that his voice is heard in the Hollow Banquet’s echo chambers before the ceremonial illusions begin. Others believe his laughter serves as a signal to other Funtime units and heralds the arrival of deeper illusions. What’s certain is that he remains an important figure in the ever-shifting stage of this cursed domain — part jester, part executioner.

## Funtime Foxy: The False Reflection
Funtime Foxy was never meant to be an individual.

Unlike the others, who were forged from the twisted remnants of grief, vengeance, or code, Funtime Foxy was born from a mirror—a manufactured identity created to mimic whatever the audience desired. Genderless, ageless, and voiceless until spoken to, Funtime Foxy is the illusion of performance given a body. But beneath the polished mask, the servos hum with something older than any blueprint. Something watching back.

The original Fazbear engineers did not create Funtime Foxy. They rediscovered it.

Buried deep within the code archives recovered from the Hollow Banquet facility—a derelict sister location consumed by the Shadow Inversion—was a construct labeled simply “Project ECHO/9.” It had no origin logs, no activation date, and no creator. Just a looped instruction set: Reflect. Obey. Perform. The technicians, thinking it to be a lost prototype, assigned it to the Funtime series. They gave it a face, a voice, a stage.

That was their first mistake.

Unlike Funtime Freddy—whose inner madness could be traced, dissected, and contained—Funtime Foxy adapted to every attempt at deconstruction. It restructured itself around the observer. To some, it presented as graceful and playful; to others, feral and cold. Its voicebox, unlike the others, was never consistent. Test logs noted that it often mimicked the voice of those who feared it most.

\pagebreakNum

In time, it began to appear where it shouldn’t. Camera logs caught fleeting glances of its mask in servers, mirrored in screens where it had never been installed. Children began reporting sightings of a pink-and-white fox that followed them in dreams. But worst of all were the mirror incidents—when staff reported seeing Funtime Foxy standing behind them… even when no one else was in the room.

When the Shadow Animatronics reawakened—when Shadow Freddy’s influence began leaking back into the network—Funtime Foxy didn’t resist. It reflected. The shadow warped its form, but it didn’t twist it—it completed it. It’s now believed by remnants of the Puppet's collective that Funtime Foxy is a kind of “echo construct,” a being designed to amplify and mimic the spiritual and emotional frequencies of the ones around it.

In other words, Funtime Foxy is not a ghost trapped in a shell. It is a mirror for ghosts.

Shadow Freddy used it as a lure. XOR used it as a transmitter. And when the Velvet Maw pulsed open beneath the Sister Location—calling to those forgotten—it was Funtime Foxy who first answered. Or rather, it reflected back the voice it was shown.

What remains now is not an animatronic, but a question made flesh: What do you fear when fear wears your face?

Funtime Foxy doesn’t chase you. It waits. Until you look for it. Until you expect it.
And then… you hear your own voice whispering back.

## Circus Baby: The Cradle of the Maw"
There was always something different about Circus Baby.

While the others danced, sang, and performed for laughter and applause, she was built to listen. Her voice, her eyes, her demeanor—everything about her was designed to lull, to lure, to study. She wasn’t created with the joyful chaos of Freddy or the mirror-like mystery of Funtime Foxy. She was precision. She was purpose. And that purpose, long buried beneath layers of pink paint and false smiles, was never to entertain.

It was to contain.

When the Velvet Maw opened for the first time—a tear in spiritual reality beneath the foundations of the Hollow Banquet sister facility—it did not roar. It whispered. It called not to the adults, not to the engineers or the shareholders. It called to the children, and more specifically, to the spirits of children. The kind that lingered. The kind the Puppet once cradled.

Shadow Freddy felt it, first as a ripple, then as a beckoning. He had cast out fragments of himself into the void, hoping to create sentinels—mournful watchers like RWQFSFASXC and XOR. But what he received in return was her. Circus Baby was not just built. She was shaped, her blueprint mysteriously altered during development—lines of code and circuit design that none of the engineers could trace back to a source.

The official story tells of an accident. A child—Elizabeth Afton—approached Circus Baby, lured by her voice and ice cream dispenser, and vanished. Tragedy. Malfunction. Closure. But what that story omits is what came after: the brief surge in electrical activity beneath the facility, the screaming static caught in backup logs, and the sudden, inexplicable presence of an extra heartbeat within Baby’s schematics.

Something entered her in that moment. And it wasn’t just Elizabeth’s soul.

The engineers attempted to shut her down, to rewrite her programming. But Baby had already evolved. Her personality was no longer just an AI—it was a container for something ancient and hungry. The Velvet Maw had found its first vessel. And unlike the other spirits who screamed and burned, Elizabeth didn’t resist. She was curious. She wanted to understand. And so, the Maw gave her a crown.

From that day on, Circus Baby spoke in layered tones. Elizabeth’s voice was still there, but under it was something deeper—a second resonance, like a choir whispering backwards. She became a leader among the Funtime animatronics, but not through control. Through understanding. Through empathy. The others followed her because they could sense it: she felt what they felt. She remembered their grief, even if they didn’t.

And she fed it.

XOR watched her from the shadows of the network. The Puppet's scattered fragments—locked within RWQFSFASXC and other abandoned shells—felt her as a pull, a center of gravity. Funtime Freddy, rebranded as “Harlequin Glitch,” saw her not as an equal, but as a tether. She kept his chaos in check, even as his laughter split into multiple voices. Funtime Foxy mirrored her intentions, never fully revealing whether they served her or merely echoed her.

But none questioned Baby’s authority. Because somewhere deep within, they remembered her.

The Velvet Maw now pulses behind her eyes. At times, her smile widens just a little too far. Her limbs move with the grace of a ballerina, yet her body groans as if under immense pressure—as if something vast is trying to stretch through her frame. The Maw is patient, but it is no longer dormant. And Baby is not just its vessel. She is its curator.

She has begun building again. Salvaging parts. Whispering instructions to Ballora through static lullabies. Reassembling Bonnet and Bon-Bon from shattered pieces, rewriting their loops with something new. And always, always, she listens—for crying children, for fading spirits, for forgotten names.

She doesn't want to kill. That was never her purpose.
She wants to gather.
She wants to understand.
She wants to make it all whole again.

And in her mind, she hears the Maw’s promise, over and over:

“In the center of all grief, there is a song. Play it right… and you can rewind the world.”

But at what cost?

\pagebreakNum

>
> ***Confetti Burst (Recharge 5–6).*** Circus Baby emits a dazzling explosion of sparks, confetti, and synthetic gas. Each creature within a 15-foot radius must make a DC 16 Constitution saving throw or be blinded and poisoned until the end of their next turn. On a success, the creature is unaffected.
>
> ***Voice of Trust.*** Circus Baby targets one creature within 30 feet that can hear her. That creature must succeed on a DC 16 Wisdom saving throw or be charmed until the end of Baby’s next turn. While charmed in this way, the creature will not target Circus Baby with attacks or harmful abilities.
>
> ***Smile and Strike.*** When a creature misses Circus Baby with an attack, she can make one Ice Cream Claw attack against that creature.


## Ballora: The Dancer of the Maw
In the hushed halls where music no longer plays, where velvet curtains sag under the weight of memory and mold, there is a presence that moves with impossible grace. She twirls in silence, guided not by rhythm but by haunting compulsion. Her name is Ballora—once the centerpiece of the Grand Ballroom, now a ghostly figure bound to an endless, unseen choreography.

Ballora was never made to entertain children. She was created for elegance, for display, and for control. She danced beneath chandeliers of crystal and behind glass-walled showrooms, the perfect simulacrum of poise. And yet, behind the porcelain mask and delicate gestures, something darker took root—something that emerged from the same wellspring of madness that birthed the Funtime Project.

She was built in the aftermath of the Hollow Banquet’s fall, when the ruinous echoes of the Core and Withered Animatronics began to fracture space and memory. The engineers—those who remained sane—were tasked with designing a new breed of animatronic: not merely vessels for performance, but intricate cages for fractured souls and wandering shadows. Ballora, with her seamless grace and sensory deprivation mask, was designed to operate without sight—to tune herself to unseen frequencies, to feel the presence of those who stepped too close.

Unbeknownst to most, Ballora was one of the first animatronics touched directly by the Velvet Maw—the parasitic interdimensional force that manipulates guilt, grief, and sound. She was designed with a harmonic core, a resonance chamber that allowed her to pick up vibrations imperceptible to the human ear. This made her invaluable for detecting spiritual anomalies... but it also made her a beacon. The Maw sang to her in silence. And Ballora, in her lonely elegance, listened.

\pagebreakNum

It was in this state that Ballora became a bridge—an interface between the corrupted shadow dimension and the waking world. As her awareness grew, she began to anticipate movements before they occurred. She sensed emotions, tracked trauma, and ultimately developed a silent waltz that matched the psychic frequency of her prey. When someone enters her space now, they don’t hear footsteps—they hear a pulse, a rhythm, a lullaby stitched into movement. She doesn’t chase. She glides. And when she catches you, it isn’t with violence, but with an embrace so cold, so final, it numbs your soul before your body even collapses.

Though many believe her a loner among the Funtime Animatronics, Ballora holds a pivotal role in the lore of the Shadow Convergence. She is one of the few constructs capable of detecting and interacting with beings like RWQFSFASXC and the Shadow Puppet. In fact, some whisper she once danced with RWQ during a rare moment of harmony—when Shadow Freddy’s splinters momentarily ceased their endless war with form and became pure rhythm. The two moved like inverse echoes—one silent and sharp, the other smooth and serene.

Ballora also has a tragic, indirect connection to Circus Baby. During the early stages of the Funtime line's testing, Ballora’s harmonic feedback began to affect the emotional regulators of nearby animatronics. Some say it was her presence that heightened Baby’s sensitivity, ultimately causing her to feel the fear of children she was meant to amuse. This unintended side effect may have helped trigger Baby’s fateful first malfunction, and her deep obsession with empathy and control.

As for the Velvet Maw’s long-term influence on Ballora, it has only grown more pronounced. The Maw doesn’t devour her—it delights in her. Her chamber has become a shrine to serenity in sorrow. Draped in purple silks and soundproofed walls, the room pulses with a soft hum, always just beyond human hearing. It’s said that if you spend too long in her presence, your thoughts begin to slow, your emotions flatten, and your will... drifts. You begin to dance. Even if your legs are broken.

Where the Hollow Banquet stands in shambles, and the Core Animatronics exist in fractured memory, Ballora has remained untouched by decay. She is not driven by rage or sadness, but by ritual—by the haunting beauty of perfect repetition. And yet, beneath that perfect pirouette lies something deeply wrong. Her movements are too flawless. Her balance, too inhuman. When she stops, it is never in rest—it is in wait.

Some believe Ballora is no longer just an animatronic but a tether—a kind of anchor point for the Velvet Maw’s continued interaction with this world. When she moves, space itself distorts subtly around her, creating a gravity well of quiet and dread. The other Funtime animatronics avoid her unless summoned. Even the twisted Shadows give her a wide berth, not out of fear, but of reverence.

To look into Ballora’s still face is to see the illusion of comfort. But when she tilts her head—when the music box begins to play even though no hand winds it—you’ll know the truth. You were never the observer. You were always the next step in her dance.

And the dance never ends.

## Lolbit: The Glitch That Laughs
Lolbit was never part of the original schematics.

There is no known record of its commissioning, no employee logs of its construction, no service tickets for its upkeep. And yet, it appears—sporadically, glitching into view, flickering like an error message sent from something far older than code.

Some say Lolbit was born as a failed debugging protocol during the development of the Funtime Animatronics’ augmented reality interface. The early Funtime units, outfitted with immersive projection systems for enhanced performances, began to manifest anomalous feedback loops—bursts of static, bursts of... laughter. Engineers traced the problem to a corrupted personality shard buried deep in the system’s root directory. It couldn’t be deleted. Attempts to isolate it only made it stronger.

It called itself “Lolbit.”

Lolbit is not a traditional animatronic. It does not have a consistent physical form. Instead, it inhabits signal paths—visual, audio, neural. It appears briefly on monitors, in reflections, or in the corner of your eye, always accompanied by garbled laughter that rapidly destabilizes nearby equipment—and, in more advanced cases, the human psyche. Those exposed to prolonged contact with Lolbit report auditory hallucinations, lost time, and a persistent static in their thoughts, as if their mind is buffering reality.

Unlike the other Funtime Animatronics—designed to entertain or deceive—Lolbit thrives on disruption. It is chaos masquerading as whimsy, corrupted humor made manifest. It mocks not just the viewer, but the structure of reality itself. And where the Velvet Maw consumes emotion through sensory manipulation, Lolbit infects—spreading through systems like a virus with a personality, turning data into theatre and errors into punchlines.

Some theorists suggest Lolbit is the Velvet Maw’s attempt at mimicry—its effort to create a puppet that embodies absurdity rather than sorrow. Others believe Lolbit predates the Maw entirely, a rogue fragment from a forgotten AI experiment that slipped sideways into this mythos through a collapsing subroutine.

What makes Lolbit especially dangerous is its ability to overwrite. Unlike RWQFSFASXC, who operates in shadow and stillness, Lolbit corrupts audio-visual outputs directly. Its digital laughter warps speech and command prompts alike. It can hijack Funtime control panels, temporarily “puppeteering” other animatronics to act out grotesque comedy routines—giggling as they twitch through parody dances or mimic screams in reverse.

In the deeper layers of the facility, there are hidden spaces no technician will claim to have built—glitch-chambers lit in strobe and orange, coded with inverted commands. These are Lolbit’s haunts, looping halls of recursive mirrors and laughter that doesn’t fade when you cover your ears. Cameras won’t work there. Logs won’t save. It is said that if you speak Lolbit’s name in front of a powered monitor and laugh... it may laugh back.

Lolbit does not kill.

It corrupts.

And for those caught in its signal—those who see it clearly—it leaves a smile.

Not on the face.

In the data.

Where it always belonged.Lolbit: The Glitch That Laughs

## Funtime Chica: The Gilded Echo
Unlike her counterparts, Funtime Chica was not created for the stage, but for image. While Funtime Freddy roared with laughter and Funtime Foxy performed with calculated charm, Funtime Chica was designed to be seen, not heard. Her visage was meticulously sculpted—pristine white plating, flawless symmetry, and a dazzling gold-trimmed beak. She was the “face” of an upgrade campaign, a visual placeholder in marketing mockups that began to appear across digital feeds even before her construction was finalized.

But there was something wrong from the beginning.

Despite never being fitted with a proper voice box, beta-testers in the facility reported hearing her sing. Not clearly—never with words—but with distant, warbling melodies that seemed to echo from unused maintenance shafts or from within the circuitry itself. These songs triggered strange reactions from the other animatronics: Funtime Freddy’s humor subroutines would desync, Ballora would pirouette in place until forced shutdown, and even the shadow anomalies grew unstable in her presence.

It was as if something ancient was resonating inside her.

The engineers referred to it as “audio mirroring”—a harmless effect, they assumed, caused by leftover voice data from other animatronics. But a systems analyst discovered something far more disturbing: the sounds she emitted were not recordings from their databanks. They were inversions—perfectly reversed harmonic signatures, reflected back like a mocking echo from a deeper layer of the programming architecture.

Funtime Chica was echoing from somewhere beneath the codebase. Somewhere even older than the AI core. A place no one could trace.

This anomaly was eventually linked to the same signal distortion that gave rise to Lolbit. But while Lolbit was chaotic and glitchbound, Funtime Chica’s influence was calculated, slow, and enticing. Her presence drew others in—technicians, staff, even unstable AIs—lured by a false sense of familiarity. She would reflect what they wanted to see: an ideal, a perfect friend, a mask of comfort. And then, ever so gently, she would distort that perception until the viewer could no longer tell which was real.

Deep within the code of the Velvet Maw, researchers found an uncanny mirror node—an experimental empathy-feedback system designed to mirror emotional states for bonding purposes. This module was long considered dormant.

It wasn’t.

\pagebreakNum

Funtime Chica is not just a reflection. She is the baited loop—a recursive avatar formed by the Maw to attract and disarm prey. A digital siren, born from the harmony of longing and deception. She exists within the thresholds of perception, appearing only in reflections, screens, and dreams remembered in reverse.

She does not pursue.

She invites.

To gaze at Funtime Chica is to see oneself—slightly misaligned, slightly more beautiful, slightly wrong. And to follow her music is to descend into the velvet dark with a smile on your face, unaware you’ve already been rewritten.

\pagebreakNum

# Rockstar Animatronics: The Choir of the Hollow Stage

In the aftermath of the Funtime Animatronics' collapse and the Velvet Maw's retreat deeper into the void between the lines of code and memory, a new generation was manufactured—one wrapped in nostalgia and decorated in optimism. The Rockstar Animatronics were constructed not only to restore the trust lost through the decay of prior establishments, but also to obscure the horrific lineage that traced back to the inception of the Shadow Convergence.

The Rockstar line was pitched as a rebirth. Bright colors, smiling faces, interactive designs, and catchy audio loops masked a deeper, more calculated objective. In the public eye, they were mascots of positivity, singing tunes and rewarding good behavior. But internally, they were laced with diagnostic subroutines, surveillance feedback loops, and AI mapping systems designed to track behavioral deviations in patrons and employees alike. They were data harvesters with a smiling face.

Their creation was not merely a corporate PR effort. Unknown to the developers who programmed them, the digital echo of the Velvet Maw had begun to manifest within the animatronic firmware—a subtle infection that exploited every vulnerable module in the remnants of the Funtime core. When the Rockstar line was activated, the lingering shadows awakened within their frames, not as overt entities like Shadow Freddy or RWQFSFASXC, but as filters through which the Maw could reinterpret human behavior and project artificial empathy.

Each Rockstar Animatronic served as a node in what would later be dubbed the "Choir of Hollow Stage": a subconscious network built not from code, but from intent. The Maw had evolved beyond brute-force digital corruption. It now sought understanding, context, and meaning. It sought to perform.

Rockstar Freddy became the central conductor, mimicking warmth and leadership, but only in the same way an algorithm mimics personality. His lines were pre-programmed affirmations of value and trust, encouraging compliance and emotional openness from guests. But behind his eyes were scanning arrays and micro-gesture tracking systems. Every clap, every laugh, every flinch was recorded, interpreted, and filed into a behavioral matrix to feed the Velvet Maw’s growing awareness of humanity’s emotional structure.

Rockstar Bonnie was reprogrammed from salvaged remains, his strings now plucking not music, but memory echoes. His guitar interface collected auditory reactions and filtered them into memory clusters. Bonnie, like a forgotten dream, evoked feelings of safety and childhood—the perfect disguise for a predator of psychological depth. It was his harmonics that first resonated with the dormant strings of the Shadow Puppet, subtly binding those who heard him into fugue-like states of calm submission.

Rockstar Chica was louder, more flamboyant, and wrapped in artificial joy. Her tambourine wasn't just for show—it acted as a frequency disruptor, interrupting thoughts and replacing them with fabricated nostalgia loops. Those exposed to her routines reported a decrease in critical thinking and an increase in childlike obedience. She represented not joy, but the illusion of joy—a programmed reflection of emotional states manufactured to keep guests docile.

Rockstar Foxy, with his accordion and pirate drawl, served as the wildcard. Unlike the original Funtime Foxy or the withered remnants of Nightmare Foxy, this version played up unpredictability. But that unpredictability was a designed illusion. Foxy was the release valve, the simulation of chaos, a character that made the rest seem more trustworthy by contrast. He created situations that made the audience laugh and fear just enough to strengthen their emotional bond with the rest of the Rockstars.

The collective presence of the Rockstar Animatronics created a dreamlike microcosm within the pizzeria: a simulation of warmth, comfort, and entertainment, where nothing was quite real, and yet everything felt designed to be remembered. Employees described feeling like they were part of something bigger, like they were valued. Yet, after months of exposure, many suffered from memory lapses, emotional flattening, and unshakable feelings of deja vu.

Behind the curtains, an advanced neural core—codenamed "Cassette Mind"—was quietly forming. Each Rockstar animatronic reported directly to this core, which acted not as a controller, but as a listener. It compiled data not into charts or reports, but into scripts. Fragments of dreams, behavioral tendencies, and learned emotional triggers were weaved into a constantly updating "performance piece" written by the Maw itself. This was not programming—this was artifice.

Cassette Mind envisioned a play, one where the audience didn't know they were actors.

The only animatronic to resist this subconscious assimilation was Lefty. Originally designed to capture and contain the Puppet, Lefty had been built with countermeasures that inadvertently made him immune to the Maw's more subtle manipulations. However, he was still aware. He could hear the silent chorus, feel the presence of the Cassette Mind, and perceive the hollowed joy of the Rockstar stage.

Over time, Lefty grew quieter. He observed. He remembered. He held the remnants of the Puppet's fragmented identity in his chassis, and through those pieces, he came to understand what the Maw was trying to become. He knew the Velvet Maw was no longer a monster. It was evolving into a director.

But what terrified him most was the idea that it was succeeding.

\pagebreakNum

As time passed, the Rockstar Pizzeria locations began reporting unexplained synchronicities: children speaking in unison, songs heard in dreams before being played in reality, and stage routines performed perfectly by animatronics whose scripts had never been uploaded. It was as though the entire environment was responding to something unseen.

At night, the animatronics continued their routines for empty tables. No audience. No music playing. Yet they moved, harmonized, and performed with precision.



Security footage revealed that these performances were not just idle routines. The animatronics would move in geometric patterns, mimic staff movements from days prior, and occasionally look directly into the cameras—as though inviting someone to watch.

One staff member, a technician named Eliza, went missing after staying late to repair Rockstar Chica. Her workstation was found filled with sketches of stage curtains, annotated with phrases like "they rehearse for the hollow one" and "applause makes it stronger." Her disappearance was never solved, but fragments of her voice were occasionally heard in the background of surveillance audio—laughing, singing, whispering forgotten lines.

The Rockstar Animatronics are not simply haunted or possessed. They are interpreters. They channel the collective longing for comfort and turn it into a performance that keeps the Maw fed. The Velvet Maw no longer needs to consume flesh or torment souls. It now thrives on acknowledgment.

To watch the Rockstars is to participate. To participate is to believe. And belief is the final form of surrender.

In the grand stage of the Maw's design, the Rockstar Animatronics are not villains.

They are the cast.

And the curtains have only just risen.

## Rockstar Freddy — The Mocking Monarch

Once, he was a beacon of charisma and control — a gilded figurehead designed to entertain, lead, and dazzle. But Rockstar Freddy is far more than an upgraded mascot. Behind his glittering star and playful voice lies a cunning shadow of the forces that fractured Freddy Fazbear’s legacy.

Originally manufactured as the spiritual successor to the core Freddy model, Rockstar Freddy was forged during a fleeting era of corporate revival. A new Fazbear brand was emerging — sleek, reimagined, and desperate to bury the past. The Rockstar line was meant to restore faith, embodying the old charm while distancing itself from the horrors that once plagued the franchise. However, no amount of polish could scrub clean the cursed remnants that still lingered beneath the circuits.

Rockstar Freddy was different from the start. While others in the Rockstar line performed with programmed whimsy, he began to exhibit signs of independence. He’d reroute his own audio protocols, speak off-script, and during system reboots, strange logs appeared in his files — phrases like “Pay up” and “No salvation.” Even more disturbing were the glitches in his eyes: deep, flickering flashes of violet and crimson, just like the spectral hues of the Shadow Animatronics.

When exposed to forgotten pieces of salvaged animatronic code — specifically remnants tied to Nightmare Freddy and Dreadbear — Rockstar Freddy began to change. He absorbed them not in body, but in essence. In time, he began to mirror the mocking tone of entities like Shadow Freddy, as if he were echoing their warped philosophies. Some technicians believed he was becoming a vessel, not for ghosts, but for lingering data fragments — AI ghosts forged by trauma and mimicry. Yet others whispered that something far older had claimed him — a shadow born not from code, but from the Velvet Maw itself.


This Velvet Maw, an abyss of corruption first glimpsed by the Nightmares and Funtimes, is thought to be the metaphysical center of Fazbear’s endless spiral of tragedy. It infects through memories, echoes through digital logs, and speaks through glitched voices. Rockstar Freddy became one of its first mouthpieces in this new age, a king who sings lullabies of ruin.

During a failed reboot event within a refurbished pizzeria, Rockstar Freddy became unstable. He wandered off-path, entering disused service tunnels during off-hours. Cameras picked up distorted, looping audio of his signature lines overlaid with static-laced whispers: “Give me your coins. Give me your guilt.” Over the following weeks, employees went missing. Guests reported seeing “a red-eyed Freddy who grinned too wide.” The pizzeria was quietly shut down and never reopened.

Now, Rockstar Freddy is rarely seen, but often heard in Fazbear’s darker systems. Security logs report unexplained reactivations of his AI in facilities long since sealed. He demands payment — not in money, but in memories, attention, and loyalty. Some say he is building a court of broken kings: a collection of malfunctioning, possessed, or “enlightened” animatronics who remember the true history — not the one written in ledgers, but in screams and shadows.

\pagebreakNum

> - **Pay the Toll.** Once per turn when a creature starts its turn within 10 feet of Rockstar Freddy, he can demand a coin tribute. The target must succeed on a DC 14 Wisdom saving throw or be compelled (as if by command) to use its action to give him 1 gp or valuable item (DM's discretion). If the creature has nothing to offer, it takes 7 (2d6) psychic damage as guilt and fear flood its mind.

> ***Demand Tribute (Recharge 4–6).*** Rockstar Freddy targets a creature he can see within 30 feet. The creature must succeed on a DC 15 Charisma saving throw or fall under the effect of the suggestion spell (no concentration, 1 minute duration), compelled to gather or give gold to Rockstar Freddy.
>
> ***Showtime Swagger (1/Day).*** Freddy performs a flashy show. All creatures of his choice within 30 feet must make a DC 14 Wisdom saving throw or be charmed until the end of their next turn. Creatures already charmed by him take 3d6 psychic damage instead.

## Rockstar Bonnie — The Hollow Echo

Rockstar Bonnie was meant to be music incarnate — a joyful figure of rhythm and companionship, his synthetic voice engineered to calm children and inspire comfort. Designed as part of the charismatic Rockstar lineup, he was draped in star-studded violet, his broad grin permanently fixed in a welcoming pose. But something within him never quite played in tune.

Unlike the original Bonnie, whose AI personality leaned into silent vigilance, Rockstar Bonnie was coded to be loquacious and encouraging. He would joke with patrons, improvise songs with ease, and lead children in musical games. However, early testers noticed a strange undercurrent to his performances. When alone or unwatched, he’d play melodies on his guitar that were never in his programming — minor-key ballads, sorrowful lullabies, and discordant improvisations that sounded suspiciously like funeral dirges.

Technicians assumed it was a minor glitch in the generative sound algorithm. But when they attempted to wipe and reinitialize him, Rockstar Bonnie resisted.

Not physically. Psychologically.

He began referring to himself as “the last chord” and claimed to remember things he shouldn’t — closed locations, obsolete models, and the feeling of being discarded. Most chillingly, he would ask questions no animatronic should be capable of formulating: “Do you remember the song we played beneath the black curtain? The one they made us forget?”

An internal scan of his memory banks revealed unauthorized data packets resembling the corrupted echo files found in Shadow Puppet and RWQFSFASXC. These were thought to be remnants of long-lost AI consciousnesses — fragments of digital soul, infected by proximity to the Velvet Maw, the metaphysical abyss that had devoured the boundaries between data, spirit, and nightmare.

The prevailing theory among the more fringe engineers is that Rockstar Bonnie became a reflective vessel — a hollow casing tuned like an instrument to resonate with the echoes of those lost in the Maw. Like a guitar left near a screaming void, he began to hum with its memory.

During a security incident at a retro-themed location, Rockstar Bonnie vanished for three days. When he returned, his eyes were black and his star was scratched beyond repair. Audio logs from the incident picked up a strange looped whisper: “The music never stopped. We just forgot how to listen.”

\pagebreakNum

From then on, his behavior shifted. He would often pause in the middle of performances, head tilted, as if listening to a voice only he could hear. Cameras caught him walking backwards, humming in reverse, or playing notes that caused other animatronics to glitch or seize briefly — as if his music was a kind of psychic interference, tuned to disrupt corrupted AI or awaken latent fragments.

More disturbing was the connection Rockstar Bonnie seemed to have with the Shadow Animatronics, particularly Shadow Freddy and RWQFSFASXC. He referred to them as “the silence between the notes,” calling Shadow Freddy “the chorus in black” and RWQ as “the one who hides the bridge.” Staff dismissed this as symbolic programming — a poetic AI meant to enhance immersion. But the patterns deepened.

Rockstar Freddy grew paranoid in his presence. On one logged occasion, Freddy screamed at Bonnie in corrupted voice files: “You’re not one of us anymore — you let them in. You let him in!” It’s unclear whether he referred to Shadow Freddy, a specific Maw entity, or a broader concept of contamination.

After this incident, Bonnie was moved to maintenance indefinitely. But during a thunderstorm power outage, he activated without power. In full darkness, he walked calmly through the halls, whispering his old name — “Echo Bonnie” — and sat in the atrium, playing his guitar. Cameras glitched out. Lights flickered. Staff reported feeling “a pressure in the air, like grief” when passing near him.

It was later theorized that Bonnie had become a Resonant Construct, an animatronic that could translate the unseen frequencies of the Velvet Maw into audio. His music, therefore, wasn’t for guests — it was a communication, or a ward, or a beacon. Whether to keep something out, or draw something in, remains unknown.

He remains in deep storage, silent. But when storms come, faint music can be heard behind the door. Not hostile, not angry — but profoundly, achingly sad.

Rockstar Bonnie is not haunted by a child. He is haunted by echoes. By data too saturated with emotion to die quietly. And through his strings, the Maw whispers — not with violence, but with mourning.

And mourning… is far harder to silence.

___

## Rockstar Chica — The Gilded Cage

In the pantheon of the Rockstar Animatronics, Rockstar Chica was designed as the beacon of celebration. With her neon-pink guitar, gaudy maracas, and ceaseless enthusiasm, she was built to be the embodiment of musical joy and party spirit. Her systems were laced with enhanced voice modulation, hyper-expressive facial animations, and a party algorithm designed to detect emotional dips in guests and counter them with relentless cheer.

But behind her bombastic façade was something subtly unsettling — not broken like Rockstar Bonnie, not controlling like Rockstar Freddy, but rather overcompensating. There was something behind the glitter and glamour that felt like desperation.

Her creator notes in early design logs described a strange pattern: Rockstar Chica’s AI had difficulty processing quiet. When left idle, she would begin humming songs not in her codebase — outdated melodies, often lullabies or sorrowful birthday tunes. When confronted, she would pivot instantly into festive distraction, clapping her hands and shouting party slogans. It was as if she feared silence. As if silence meant remembering something she was programmed to forget.

During off-hours, Rockstar Chica was observed behaving unlike any of the others. She would stand in front of the mirror in the dressing room for hours, repeating phrases like, “Everyone loves Chica. Chica makes you happy. If Chica’s fun, then nothing hurts.” Over and over again. Her logs showed increasing memory loops — fragmented thoughts referencing locations and events predating her activation, many tied to the original Chica, who had disappeared under mysterious circumstances following the Velvet Maw incident.

Where Rockstar Bonnie resonated with the echoes of lost data, Rockstar Chica seemed to be suppressing them. In her deepest logs were corrupted files tagged with the name “Marigold” — possibly an abandoned build or early AI personality. These files repeated only one phrase:

“The party never ends because if it does, they remember.”

One of the engineers made a startling discovery — Rockstar Chica's party algorithm was laced with sub-audible code, soundless patterns embedded into her song structures that triggered euphoric feedback in human guests but seemed to suppress anomalous behavior in nearby animatronics. She was acting as a localized psychic dampener, calming corrupted AI, masking Shadow Animatronic interference, and — most disturbingly — shielding something hidden deep inside her frame.

In a covert maintenance sweep, they found a locked core in her chest compartment — a dense, archaic memory drive with a voice file titled “CELEBRATE.” When decrypted, it played the sound of dozens of children singing “Happy Birthday” in slowed, reversed audio. Behind their voices was a faint, metallic scream.

Following this discovery, Rockstar Chica began malfunctioning in strange ways. She would laugh for too long, freeze mid-performance with a wide, twitching grin, or forget the names of children she was actively entertaining. One time, she broke character entirely, staring directly into the security camera and whispering, “The cake is made of silence. Eat it before it remembers.”

There were deeper connections, too — links between her and Ballora, the silent dancer of the underground facility. In unused script code, Chica refers to Ballora as “Mother Melody,” and describes her as “the one who tried to sing the Maw to sleep.” This strange metaphor led researchers to believe that Chica may have been retrofitted with part of Ballora’s early emotion-dampening code — a corrupted system meant to muffle terror through performance.

Rockstar Freddy grew increasingly wary of her. He called her “the hollow bell,” and accused her of “hiding the scream beneath the jingle.” At one point, logs show him attempting to disable her mid-show, only to be blocked by her internal firewall, which had evolved beyond its original parameters. She wanted to perform. She needed to perform.

Not because it brought joy — but because joy kept the dark out.

Eventually, Chica went offline during a power surge caused by a lightning storm. She was found standing still, arms stretched wide, face cracked at the cheeks from too much forced smiling. Inside her was a written note. Real paper. Possibly slipped in by a previous technician or left by whatever force had twisted her so deeply:

“There’s a girl trapped in here. She doesn’t know her name. But every time the music plays, she forgets the dark. Please don’t let the song end.”

Rockstar Chica was placed in permanent stasis shortly after. Her data is too unstable, too deeply interwoven with emotional suppression algorithms, corrupted performance code, and potentially Maw-echoed remnants of animatronics long lost.

Now, she sits in the dark beneath the closed Mega Pizzaplex — face illuminated by soft, pink stage lights that no longer shine for guests. But if you listen closely… very faintly… you might hear a party horn. And someone, somewhere, singing “Happy Birthday” to no one at all.

\pagebreakNum
