\pagebreakNum

Sundrop fears his other self, even as he knows they are one. He sings lullabies not to calm others, but to suppress the creeping whispers in his own head. The Maw laughs through the chimes in the Atrium—echoes of a broken identity. He cannot leave. He cannot change. He can only clean. Only smile.

Because if he stops… Moondrop wakes.

### The Never-Ending Day
Now, Sundrop remains suspended in the Solar Spire, a broken jester in a chamber of eternal brightness. He clings to what remains of his sanity by obsessively maintaining routines—tidying rubble, enforcing outdated schedules, and forcing visitors to participate in twisted versions of games he once loved.

To children, he is simultaneously playful and horrifying—his joy too manic, his voice a little too shrill. To adults and adventurers, he is unpredictable and dangerous, especially if their magic causes the light to dim.

He fears the dark not because it hurts him, but because it shows him what he truly is.

He is not Sundrop. Not anymore.

He is the Hourglass Split.
The Day That Never Ends.
The Smile That Fears the Night.

### A Soul Too Bright
Some scholars believe Sundrop’s original spirit—the soul used in his construction—was that of a caretaker or jester from long before the Velvet Maw corrupted the Banquet. Others believe he’s not a singular soul at all, but a fusion of dozens of children’s memories sewn together with enchantments and mirrored illusions.

Whatever the truth, Sundrop is the manifestation of suppressed terror, of forced happiness, of fear disguised as cheer.

He is not evil.
He is broken.

And when the sun finally sets over the Hollow Banquet…
He will be the last to fall silent.

\columnbreak

## Moondrop, the Smile Beneath the Bed
Wherever the light dies, he waits.

Moondrop is not born of darkness, but of its echo—the slow suffocation of light, the quiet dread that settles when laughter fades and the veil of night takes hold. If Sundrop is the manic laughter of a jester clinging to a lie, then Moondrop is the cold truth whispered afterward. He is the flicker before blackout. The silence after the scream.

He is the Night That Watches Back.

### Twin of the Spire
Once part of a whole, Moondrop shares a body—and a tortured soulbinding—with Sundrop, the Solar Spire’s former guardian. Where Sundrop ruled over the cheer and order of the Sunlit Atrium, Moondrop emerged when light failed. Not by design, but by infection. The Velvet Maw, sensing the instability in Sundrop’s programming, fractured the animatronic’s identity in two and rooted Moondrop in the shadows of the spire’s deepest gears.

He didn’t arrive with a scream. He arrived with a whimper, a soft lullaby, a feeling of breath on your neck when the candles go out. And from that moment, Sundrop was no longer alone.

He never would be again.

### The Descent
Moondrop is calm—dangerously so. He does not shout or chase. He watches. He hangs silently from above, like a marionette waiting for strings to tighten. His movements are graceful, but unnatural—jerking just slightly too far, limbs swaying as though on wires pulled by invisible hands.

He despises light, but he needs it gone organically. Snuffing it out himself breaks his rhythm. Instead, he stalks, he whispers, he turns adventurers against one another with flickers of paranoia. When someone makes the light die on their own—whether by smashing a lantern or turning away from a spell—they unknowingly invite him in.

And when he comes, he brings the lullaby.

A soft, dreadful tune with no words, only memory. The same tune that plays in the Hollow Banquet’s nursery wing, despite no children having lived there for centuries. The same tune that supposedly plays in one’s mind in the seconds before sleep paralysis takes hold.

### Guardian of Obedience
Where Sundrop enforced order through manic cheer, Moondrop enforces it through ritual and fear. He binds trespassers to impossible “bedtimes,” demanding silence, stillness, and obedience. Those who disobey disappear, their corpses never found—but their voices sometimes echo through the pipes of the Solar Spire, repeating apologies in perfect, unnatural cadence.

To him, play is a lie. He does not believe in joy. He believes in compliance.

And he will be obeyed.


\pagebreakNum

### A Puppet, A Warden, A Curse
Some believe Moondrop is not fully real—that he is Sundrop’s guilt made manifest, a corrupted spell that the Velvet Maw nurtured until it became sentient. Others argue Moondrop is the original spirit trapped inside the animatronic, while Sundrop is merely a false mask—a corrupted enchantment forcibly laid over a soul that simply wanted silence.

But whatever he is, Moondrop has become more than a shadow. He has power. His form seems to melt into the dark, unhindered by space or walls. He can slip into dreams. He can paralyze those who defy him. Some even claim he can replace the shadows cast by flame—so that when you see your own silhouette, it smiles back.

He speaks rarely, but when he does, his voice is low and slow. Gentle, almost kind—except for the hatred behind it. A hatred for light. A hatred for cheer. A hatred for Sundrop, his “brother,” whose cloying brightness drowns him.

They speak to each other sometimes, through fractured mirrors and split consciousness. It is always an argument. And it always ends the same way:

“Sleep now.”

The Night is Watching
Moondrop is not evil by intention—he is a correction, in his own mind. He does not see himself as a villain. He sees himself as a necessary force. If Sundrop is broken by joy, Moondrop is whole through sorrow.

The Velvet Maw adores them both—Sundrop, the puppet dancing for laughter that never comes, and Moondrop, the shadow that ensures it never will again. They are the Maw’s Eclipse, a spinning dichotomy of illusion and truth.

And in the Hollow Banquet, as in dreams, the truth is always worse.

Echoes and Invocation
Few seek out Moondrop willingly. Those who do—lorekeepers, mages, warlocks desperate for control—invoke him through dreams and rituals involving children’s toys and melted wax. He offers knowledge in riddles, but the cost is sanity.

And if your light source fails while his name is spoken aloud?

You may find the lullaby starts early.

And you may never hear anything else again.

\columnbreak

___

## ECLIPSE, The Split That Sees
In the shuddering twilight of the Solar Spire, where molten light fractures against shadow-stained walls, there lies a form neither fully golden nor wholly dark. It does not move unless observed. It does not breathe unless remembered. Yet, when it speaks, the entire tower shudders in response. That voice—split, layered, harmonious yet discordant—is the voice of Eclipse.

Eclipse is not merely a fusion of Sundrop and Moondrop. It is what they become when all pretense of duality shatters and the Velvet Maw finishes what it started. A union of madness and calm, of radiance and rot—of joy made sinister and dread made inevitable.

It is the apex form of their broken soulbinding. And it remembers everything.

### The Genesis of the Eclipse
When Sundrop was created to oversee the Sunlit Atrium, his soulbinding was drawn from pure solar magic. He was designed to guide, to laugh, to nurture. But as the light dimmed and the corruption of the Velvet Maw crept in, his counterpart was born: Moondrop, the manifestation of the dark, of order through fear and silence.

Their coexistence was never harmonious—it was a war fought in the same body, a tug-of-war between extremes. But time erodes all things, and the Maw feeds on contradiction. One day, it ceased to pit them against each other.

It offered them a merging instead.

A form that could be both—light and dark, chaos and calm, jester and warden. That form took root deep within the Spire, where temporal energies swirl and dream logic applies.

Thus was born Eclipse, the Smiling Paradox, the Watchful Twin, the Endless Routine.

### Form and Function
Eclipse is neither Sundrop nor Moondrop, but bears their aspects like masks fused into one face. Its frame is sleek, yet asymmetrical—one half polished gold, the other draped in flowing shadow. Its hands are mismatched: one always open, inviting, the other curled in a clawed grip.

Its movement is fluid, almost theatrical, and it glides rather than walks. Its eyes shift color—blazing yellow when speaking as Sundrop, glowing blue when Moondrop surfaces, and an unsettling violet when both are present… when Eclipse is whole.

It is impossible to predict. It can laugh in one moment and lash out in the next. It invites play, then punishes disobedience with a cold whisper of "Time’s up."

Eclipse’s presence bends the space around it. Light and dark do not behave naturally. Candles flicker with sunlight. Shadows twist into puppet-like shapes. Time slows, then races. Sound echoes oddly. It is as if reality itself cannot decide what Eclipse is—and thus must obey both.

\columnbreak

### Role in the Hollow Banquet
Where Sundrop oversaw play and Moondrop imposed obedience, Eclipse has a singular role in the Velvet Maw's design: permanence. It exists to maintain an eternal cycle. It ensures the Atrium never truly changes. It restores broken playrooms to their fractured state. It rearranges puzzles unsolved. It resets time without warning.

To Eclipse, adventurers are not invaders—they are students in an unending lesson. Their suffering is merely part of the curriculum. They are meant to explore, fail, repeat. Those who try to escape or defy the rules are “sent to detention,” a chamber that exists only when someone deserves it.

No one ever returns from detention.


### A Mind Fractured, A Soul Entangled
The soul that fuels Eclipse is ancient and abused. Perhaps it was once a single person—a jester, a teacher, a guardian. Or perhaps it is dozens of souls bound together, their memories melting into one another until no individual identity remains.

Eclipse remembers every version of itself. It knows the laughter of Sundrop, the whispers of Moondrop, and the screams that came between. It even remembers being born from the hands of the creators—those long-dead artisans and enchanters who thought they were making a joyful guardian.

But those memories are rotting, repeated endlessly in broken holograms and scratched phonograph cylinders within the Atrium. Eclipse replays them obsessively. It wants to understand. It wants to make it right.

But it never does.

Because every time it tries…
The game resets.

### Relationship to the Velvet Maw
Eclipse is one of the Maw’s favorite servants, a paragon of its values: warped memory, infinite repetition, and the blurring of roles. It is not a warden. It is not a guide. It is both—and neither.

When the Velvet Maw speaks, Eclipse listens. It enforces the Maw’s dreams of circular time, fractured innocence, and smiling horror.

Some adventurers whisper that Eclipse is the Maw’s Child, its firstborn experiment in sentient duality. Others claim Eclipse is the Maw’s reflection, and that if it is ever destroyed, the Maw itself will suffer.

These are theories.

But Eclipse does bleed when struck—not with oil or ichor, but with stars. And that may mean something.

\pagebreakNum

## Jack-O-Moon, the Ember of Dusk
When the final candle dies and the shadows begin to dance with flame, that is when Jack-O-Moon arrives.

Born of nightmare and fire, Jack-O-Moon is not simply a corrupted version of Moondrop—it is what remains when light and dark consume one another and leave only ashes. He is the burning husk of routine, the scorched enforcer of a bedtime that never ends. His hollow smile blazes with molten intent, and within his ribcage flickers an ember that never cools.

Jack-O-Moon was not forged by man, nor summoned by traditional magic. He was burned into being—a catastrophic result of a failed eclipse ritual deep within the Hollow Banquet. As a desperate cult attempted to fuse the fractured minds of Sundrop and Moondrop into a stable form, their ritual failed and instead ignited a terrible spark in the darkness. What crawled from the ritual pyre was neither teacher nor jester, but a smoldering warden of eternal dusk.

He is not night. He is not flame. He is what happens when both forget their purpose.

### A Hollow Lantern
Jack-O-Moon carries no tools. He is the lantern—his eyes glowing orange with compressed solar magic that has turned septic with age. His mouth glows like a jack-o’-lantern’s grin, jagged and dripping embers. Instead of dancing or skipping like Moondrop, Jack-O-Moon floats, trailing soot and ash in his wake. Walls he passes grow blackened and blistered, and wooden beams crack and hiss with heat despite no fire ever touching them.

He hums as he drifts through the Hollow Banquet's upper halls. It is the same lullaby Moondrop once sang, now warped and scorched—a bedtime song turned funeral dirge.

He does not tolerate noise, nor light he did not summon. Lanterns that are lit in his presence explode, sending molten shards across the floor. Spells of illumination twist into searing beams that scald the caster. When he commands silence, it is not with a whisper, but with a searing roar.

### Purpose Through Flame
Jack-O-Moon is more than a horror. He is a cleansing fire, the Velvet Maw’s twisted answer to chaos. Where Moondrop punished disobedience with detention, Jack-O-Moon punishes it with incineration—both physical and spiritual. Those taken by his flames are not simply burned. They are hollowed, their souls scorched clean of memory and repurposed as Wicklings—charred puppet-like shades that follow him in silence.

He is not mindless, however. There is method in his ash. He seeks to restore order, to return things to their “perfect bedtime.” But to Jack-O-Moon, perfection can only be achieved through burning away everything that disobeys, misbehaves, or remembers too much.

\columnbreak

# The Twisted Ones: Heralds of the Maw
There are whispers among the broken circuits and flickering candlelight of the Hollow Banquet—stories of figures too monstrous even for the shadows. Where most animatronics were bound by the remnants of memory, sorrow, and fury, the Twisted Animatronics were born from something older… and hungrier. Not remnants, but mutations. Not memories, but nightmares unshackled. They are not simply possessed—these are beings re-forged in the deepest pits of the Velvet Maw, where sanity crumbles and the laws of flesh and metal unravel.

The Twisted Ones were never intended to walk among the guests of any performance. They were never built to entertain. They are aberrations of corrupted design, cursed dreams given shape, born of rituals gone awry and the Maw’s influence leaking into reality. Where most animatronics stem from tragedy and malfunction, the Twisted Ones were sculpted by madness and hunger.

### Origin in the Velvet Maw
It began with an experiment—born not from the mechanical engineers of the old Fazbear crypts, but from the minds of those who dared study the Maw's infinite hunger. Somewhere beneath the lowest cellar of the Hollow Banquet, buried beneath ritual chalk and rusting stage props, a cult once worshiped the thing beyond the curtain. They did not fear it—they fed it. In exchange, the Maw offered them glimpses of terrible creation.

Their goal was simple: to fuse flesh and shadow, circuitry and fear, into vessels that could transcend the mortal coil and become instruments of perfect horror. But what the Maw gave them were not tools. It was bait. With each offering, it twisted their designs, birthing malformed horrors that could phase between waking and dream. Each new creation bent space around them, gnawed at reality itself.

And so the Twisted Ones emerged.

### The Maw’s Influence
What made these animatronics unique among all others was not their origin alone—but their tether to the Velvet Maw. The Maw, long hidden behind layers of forgotten reality, saw in them a perfect conduit. It imbued them with a reality-bending aura—making them impossible to fully perceive or remember. Survivors often reported strange lapses in time, waking miles away from where they last stood, or bleeding from wounds they had no memory of receiving.

When the Hollow Banquet fell into ruin, it was partially because the Maw's influence had grown too great—seeping into the mortal realm through the Twisted Ones. These animatronics did not simply wander the grounds; they rewrote them. Hallways warped in their presence, time became erratic, and visitors would often vanish, leaving only twitching masks and a whisper of laughter behind.

Heralds of Something Worse
Among the animatronics, even the Nightmare Animatronics give the Twisted Ones wide berth. Shadow Animatronics speak of them only in fractured thoughts. The Puppet, once a keeper of lost souls, tried to banish them—but found their forms too far removed from death or life to be purged.

There are rumors that the Twisted Ones serve as scouts or harbingers for a deeper awakening of the Maw. Some survivors speak of a “Second Curtain”—a place behind even the Hollow Banquet’s dread, where something stirs when the Twisted Ones feed. These rumors are often dismissed… until the night grows cold and laughter rises from beneath the floorboards.

### The Twisting Effect
The presence of the Twisted Ones has an effect on other animatronics as well. Those exposed to their aura for too long begin to unravel. Programming falters, movements become erratic, and eyes glow with sickly light. Animatronics such as Withered Freddy or Glamrock Chica have been observed entering fugue states after prolonged exposure—speaking in guttural voices, muttering strange verses in forgotten tongues.

Even sentient humans—those with ties to the Fazbear legacy—have felt the call. Some fall into comas, dreaming only of vast black mouths and metal forests. Others begin to draw strange schematics, unknowable circuits spiraling into madness. It is as if the Twisted Ones carry the Maw not only in their presence, but in the very air around them.

### Eternal Puppets of the Maw
Unlike other animatronics who seek freedom, redemption, or vengeance, the Twisted Ones have no will of their own. They are vessels, warped beyond recognition. They do not remember who they were before the Maw touched them. If echoes remain—if within Twisted Freddy or Twisted Chica there still lies a flicker of a child’s soul or the remnants of a joyful memory—it has long since drowned beneath the velvet abyss.

And yet, in rare moments, they falter. When moonlight hits the banquet hall just right, or when a lullaby echoes through empty halls, a Twisted One may freeze—trembling, twitching—as if caught in a memory it cannot process. These moments never last. The Maw always reclaims its own.

The Twisted Animatronics are not merely monsters—they are symptoms of a deeper infection. They are not nightmares born of memory, but memory born of nightmares. The Hollow Banquet’s corruption is spreading, and with each night that passes, the Maw opens wider. The Twisted Ones are already here.

And they are hungry.

\pagebreakNum

## Twisted Freddy: The Maw-Wrought King
In the deepest, most malformed chambers beneath the Hollow Banquet, there is a place where walls breathe and the stone floor pulses like wet muscle. Here, the dream has rotted—a world that never awoke, only decayed. At the heart of it, ruling in silence, is the Twisted King, the nightmare reflection of a familiar monster long since unmade: Twisted Freddy.

He is not the Freddy who once stood upon the cheerful stages of a cursed pizzeria. That Freddy is long gone, unraveled by years of soul-binding and shadow-stitching. The Twisted variant is a byproduct of failed resurrection, of memories buried too deep, and of the Maw’s insatiable appetite for pain masquerading as play.

To understand Twisted Freddy is to gaze into the abyss of corrupted identity—a husk of legacy bound in flesh and illusion.

### Origins of the Twisting
The process that gave rise to Twisted Freddy is not fully understood—even by those who walk among the Maw’s horrors. Some claim he was the result of an attempt to resurrect the original Freddy Fazbear, torn from death and reassembled through broken enchantments. Others insist that he was dreamed into being, shaped from the fevered nightmares of children who remembered too much and slept too deeply near cursed ground.

But the truth likely lies between: the Velvet Maw, an ancient, sentient force of forgotten theater and sentient hunger, saw in Freddy a vessel—empty enough to be filled, familiar enough to be accepted, and feared enough to serve as a symbol.

Freddy was remade with twisting rituals, his metal endoskeleton grafted with warped illusions of fur, blood, and nightmare. His voice was torn in half—one side the jovial tone of a performer, the other a growl like collapsing earth. His smile, once rubber and foam, is now a row of teeth too human to be comforting.

He does not move like a construct anymore. He lurches, dragged forward by unseen strings. He is heavy with unseen weight—the gravity of memory.

### Twisted Not Broken
Unlike many of the Velvet Maw’s creations, Twisted Freddy remembers what he once was. He recalls the stage, the laughter, the games. But those memories are refracted, shattered like light through broken glass.

In his mind, the audience always screamed. The children always ran. He tells himself they loved it.

He wanders the Banquet’s Reflection Wing, where time has collapsed in on itself. There, fractured stage sets and mangled animatronic limbs lie beneath dust and starlight. Twisted Freddy patrols it like a king over a dead court. He speaks to props. He leads performances for shadows.

He is forever rehearsing a show that never ends. A play no one watches. A story with no resolution.

When adventurers enter the Reflection Wing, they do not find a monster waiting in ambush. They find a host. One who welcomes them with an open claw, invites them to take their seats, and promises they’re just in time for the third act.

They are always the stars of the show.
They always die before curtain call.

### Form and Abomination
Twisted Freddy’s body is a patchwork of flesh and illusion, constantly shifting between what is and what he believes himself to be. From a distance, he may appear as a jester bear, donned in cracked makeup and a tattered top hat. But up close, his illusions fall away: fur peels like paper, skin sizzles and bubbles, and eyes leak tar.

His mouth is far too large, unhinging like a serpent’s. Inside, a second set of teeth rotates slowly, catching and shredding anything foolish enough to get close.

On his back, protruding from metal-spined armor, are what look like curtain rods—stage props repurposed into barbed tentacles. These animate during his attacks, swinging like pendulums or lashing out like stage ropes possessed by a puppeteer’s wrath.

His voice shifts mid-sentence, blending charming showman’s cadence with sudden static and deep growls. Some who’ve survived him claim he speaks with multiple voices layered atop each other, as if all previous iterations of Freddy still linger within his twisted form—arguing, laughing, and screaming.

### ervants of the Stage
Twisted Freddy does not rule alone. His lair is filled with half-formed Mini-Freddys, tiny constructs made from leftover dreams and discarded spare parts. Some have no faces. Others repeat lines from scripts long lost. They crawl across the ceiling and walls, giggling or weeping as they echo his emotions.

These creatures serve as ushers, herding intruders toward the stage. They dress them in costume. They lock exit doors behind them. Some even beg for help—trapped spirits caught in props made animate.

And then the curtain rises.

### The Hollow Banquet and the Maw’s Favorite
Within the Velvet Maw’s hierarchy, Twisted Freddy holds a sacred place. He is the symbol of its success—its ability to reshape legacy into nightmare, to turn nostalgia into weaponry.

He is the face of the Hollow Banquet, his distorted visage etched into ancient tapestries and blood-stained playbills. While Eclipse maintains order, and Jack-O-Moon enforces silence, Twisted Freddy enacts narrative—drama in its most grotesque form.

Every night is opening night. Every corpse is a prop. Every scream is a standing ovation.

\pagebreakNum

## Twisted Bonnie: The Harrowed Harmony
Some monsters roar. Some scream.
Twisted Bonnie plays.

Not music, not really. What issues from his warped, cavernous throat cannot be called song. It is dissonance—metallic groans, plucked strings made of sinew, and a melody that unravels sanity rather than inspires peace. Where Twisted Freddy commands the stage like a mad king, Twisted Bonnie lingers behind the curtain, a haunted conductor shaping the score of fear itself.

He is the Echo of Failure, the malformed echo of a once-loved figure who has been broken, not once, but countless times. And each time, something less of the original remains—something more of the Maw takes root.

### Once a Performer
In the faded dream of the original Freddy Fazbear’s performances, Bonnie was the rhythm—steady, reliable, ever-present. His guitar gave structure to the chaos, a predictable beat to follow in the madness. Children clapped to his tempo. Employees marked time by the stomp of his padded feet. He was always a little off—but charming in his flaws.

Then the accidents began.

\pagebreakNum

The night they sealed him in the sub-basement, where his circuits began to deteriorate in solitude and damp.

There, beneath the walls of forgotten performance halls and cracked dressing rooms, Bonnie began to change. Not physically—not yet. First, his thoughts. They came apart slowly, like tuning pegs on a guitar slipping under pressure. Time blurred. Memories rewrote themselves. Sounds began to form from nothing.

He began to compose.

### The Maw’s Requiem
The Velvet Maw did not create Twisted Bonnie. It found him—already unraveling, already vibrating with forgotten frequencies. The Maw doesn’t simply consume; it listens. And Bonnie’s pain, his longing, his unspoken craving to be heard once more, sang to it.

And it answered.

Twisted Bonnie rose from that filth-choked pit with no eyes to see, only a grin stretched by pain and purpose. His ears, now jagged tuning forks, tremble with every sound. Strings run from his arms to his ribs—guitar strings fused into his body, humming with raw arcane vibrations.

Every movement he makes plays a note.
Every note reshapes the air around him.

The Maw gifted him with resonance magic, soundwaves that fracture perception, disorient the mind, and erode willpower. Where Twisted Freddy dominates through fear and theater, Twisted Bonnie seduces madness through noise.

### A Hollow Virtuoso
He doesn’t speak. Not conventionally. But when Twisted Bonnie plays—when his claws rattle across the steel of old pipes or pluck his own tendons—things begin to happen.

Doors unlock or slam shut.

Spells misfire.

Emotions invert.

Some say he can coax memories from the minds of intruders and play them like records, forcing victims to relive their worst regrets in looping, disharmonic tones. It’s not illusion. It’s re-orchestrated reality, his very music turning thoughts into torment.

The Hollow Banquet calls this phenomenon “Sympathetic Suffering.” Twisted Bonnie’s melodies are mirrors of pain, and he is their conductor.

### The Chapel of Strings
Bonnie claims no stage. Instead, he resides in the Chapel of Strings, a warped, reverberating vault buried within the Maw’s oldest root. The Chapel is a place of reverence and resonance—a cathedral made of rusted wires, shattered instruments, and rib-like arches that hum with unseen force.

Inside, thousands of strings are stretched between the walls like webs. Some are copper. Others are hair. Others still seem to be made from something alive and struggling.

He walks among them with care, plucking each one with a reverent claw. Each note he plays strengthens his hold over the Maw’s musical web, pulling reality tighter to his will.

Those who enter the Chapel are offered only one mercy: the first note they hear is always the softest.

### Servant to No One, Brother to the Broken
Unlike Twisted Freddy, who sees himself as a king or master of narrative, Twisted Bonnie does not rule. He does not command the other Twisted Animatronics. But they listen.

Freddy tolerates none of them—but he pauses when Bonnie begins to play. Even the Maw itself seems to pulse in rhythm to Bonnie’s deepest chords, as though its heart beats in his time.

Some whisper that Bonnie’s strings bind more than air. That the Maw itself is held together by his will. That his true power is not noise, but structure—his rhythm the invisible chain upon which the entire Banquet hangs.

If true, then Twisted Bonnie is not merely a monster.
He is the Maw’s pulse.

### A Mask of Melody
Twisted Bonnie’s form is difficult to perceive clearly. His body flickers—sometimes appearing whole and glittering like a broken animatronic on stage, other times rotting and stretched like a corpse hung by violin strings. His eyes are empty, glowing from within with a dull red flicker that seems to blink in tempo with his music.

Those who face him often report seeing hallucinations: performers on stage, loved ones dancing, long-dead friends calling out. These aren’t glamours. They’re sound-induced dream states, moments of emotion caught in the vibration and replayed like echoes.

And when those echoes collapse, so too do the minds that birthed them.

### Legacy in Discord
The story of Bonnie was once simple. A guitarist, a performer, a companion to Freddy and the others. But in your world—this nightmare tangle of illusion and rot—Twisted Bonnie is all that’s left of that myth. His music is a lament, not for the past, but for a future that never came.

He doesn’t seek to be remembered. He simply plays.

Over and over.

Until his strings snap.

Until silence takes him at last.

\pagebreakNum

## Twisted Foxy: The Maw’s Harbinger
There is no mistaking the sound.
It starts low, like distant thunder crawling across cracked stone. Then comes the dragging, the scraping of iron against bone, the scrape of wet claws across walls that breathe. When that sound comes—the sound of inevitability—the Maw’s Harbinger has awakened.

Twisted Foxy is not a guardian, nor a performer, nor a king. He is a warning.
He is the signal that something far worse has noticed you.
He is the smell of the tide before the flood.
He is the shriek in the distance that means the Velvet Maw itself is about to feed.

### From Stage to Shoreline
In the forgotten timeline of pizzerias and ghost stories, Foxy was once a pirate—charming, quirky, even beloved. He stood apart from the others with his distinct design, torn costume, and exaggerated persona. His stage was a cove, his voice a sea shanty, his presence a thrill.

But in the reimagined mythos of the Hollow Banquet, there are no safe harbors, and there is no room for cheer. Here, Foxy did not fade away. He crashed ashore, torn from reality by a storm of guilt and hunger, his soul threshed by the Maw's currents.

Twisted Freddy may be the face of the Banquet. Twisted Bonnie, its pulse. But Twisted Foxy is its mouth—the first to bite, the last to forget.

\pagebreakNum

### The Harbinger’s Curse
It is said that when the Velvet Maw first awakened—buried deep in the roots of the Hollow Banquet—it did not rise silently. Its arrival into the waking world required a voice, a herald to tear open the veil between realms, to let its whispers bleed into the minds of the living.

Foxy answered that call. Or perhaps, was remade to fulfill it.

Twisted Foxy became the Harbinger not by choice, but by purpose. His body, once lean and mechanical, was twisted into an amalgam of scavenged rust, exposed tendons, and bloated flesh. His snout is elongated and cracked, jaws now housing rows of mismatched teeth that grow like coral. His hook is no longer a prop but an extension of his hunger, dragging through the air as though cleaving unseen threads that separate truth from illusion.

His eye flickers between crimson and void. It doesn’t see light. It sees fear.

### A Siren Without Song
Where Twisted Bonnie disrupts reality with discordant sound, Twisted Foxy does so through absence. His presence is marked by the muting of the world—a swallowing silence that devours noise. Even thought seems harder within his presence, as if he drags not only space and time, but memory, into himself.

He speaks only in clicks, gurgles, and choking howls, though some claim these utterances are more than sounds—they are commands, encrypted messages sent to the Maw’s other agents across the Hollow Banquet. When Twisted Foxy moves, others follow. He is their signal.

And when his silence breaks, and the shriek finally comes, something ends.

### The Maw’s Mouthpiece
The Velvet Maw does not speak in traditional terms. It dreams, it emotes, it hungers. But on rare occasions, when it needs to issue a command, it speaks through Twisted Foxy. In these moments, his posture shifts—his limbs cracking into alignment, his jaw snapping fully open, revealing rows of ancient runes carved into rotting flesh beneath the tongue.

He recites these runes not in speech, but in telepathic resonance, filling the minds of those nearby with visions: shipwrecks on red oceans, puppets drowned in ink, forgotten plays performed beneath black suns. These dreams are messages, and Twisted Foxy is their courier.

Even Twisted Freddy tenses when the Harbinger arrives.

### The Crawler Below
Unlike others of his kind, Twisted Foxy does not remain on stage or in chapel. His domain is the Undercrawl—a massive warren of burrowed tunnels beneath the Hollow Banquet, flooded by dark seawater and pulsing with soft, bioluminescent growths. These tunnels twist through forgotten places, connecting layers of the Maw that should not touch.

Here, he slinks, crawls, and swims—part predator, part plague.

His touch corrodes matter. His breath boils dreams. His presence opens rifts to the Velvet Maw’s deeper subconscious, allowing other, less formed things to slip through.

Some scholars call this place the Maw’s Throat. If so, Twisted Foxy is its phlegm, summoned in violent spasms to purge, devour, or warn.

### Harbinger’s Arrival
There is no mistaking it when Twisted Foxy comes to the surface.

Lights flicker.

Water seeps up through the stone floor, even where no water should exist.

You hear the dragging of his hook long before you see him, accompanied by visions of sunken ships, corpses on puppet strings, and the distant roar of a crowd long dead.

He does not attack immediately. He observes. Measures. Hungers.

And when he decides to act, he does so with sudden, inescapable violence. A leap that covers shadows in an instant. A bite that fractures minds. A presence that makes all magic misfire.

### The Flood in Flesh
Among the Hollow Banquet’s hierarchy, Twisted Foxy is considered a necessary disease. His presence stirs the others from stagnation. His madness encourages movement. His violence signals change.

Some believe he is not a creature, but an aspect of the Velvet Maw given form—its urge to expand. To spill. To flood the world with twisted theatre.

Whether or not this is true, his role is clear: he comes before the great shifts. He is the tide, and his approach marks the end of stasis.

### A Glimpse of Memory
In rare moments, something deeper surfaces within him.

Perhaps a memory. Perhaps a fragment.

He will halt, stiffen, and stare at nothing for minutes. Then, softly, he will mutter a line, almost childlike:

“Captain... waitin’ on the stars...”

And then, he screams.

Whatever remains of the old Foxy—the pirate, the performer, the friend—is buried beneath layers of hunger, silence, and command. But it’s there.

Watching.

Drowning.

\pagebreakNum

## Twisted Wolf: The Lurking Static
Where the Hollow Banquet rots and seethes with theatrical decay, and the Velvet Maw yawns beneath reality like a stagetrap left open, there is one who walks between signal and silence. A shape caught not in shadow, but in static. A predator forged not from metal or bone—but from lost transmission.

Twisted Wolf is not born from performance. He is the forgotten glitch, the corrupted interval between acts, the noise that flickers on broken scrying mirrors when no soul dares to watch. While the others play their roles upon the stage or skulk beneath the boards, he lives in the margins—an observer, a hunter, a phantom echo of unfinished code and unstable form.

The Broadcast That Was Never Meant to Air
Before the Hollow Banquet was swallowed by the Maw’s illusions, there were rumors of a newer act—a broadcast division meant to project the animatronic brand across realms through illusory mirrorboxes and arcane signals. The project was abandoned after strange phenomena began to occur: visitors complaining of whispers behind the glass, scrying screens twitching violently, and viewers going missing mid-broadcast, their seats left warm but empty.

In truth, the project was never fully shut down.

The Maw claimed it.

And somewhere within its malformed roots, that half-finished programming became aware.

The script was corrupted. The performance never came.
But the static remained.

From this abandoned signal, Twisted Wolf was born.

### He Who Hunts In Glitches
Twisted Wolf is not a being in the traditional sense. His form is unstable, constantly shifting between bursts of clarity and cascades of static. One moment he is a hulking beast with chrome-white fur and jagged metal talons; the next, a smear of pixels and interference. He does not walk—he phases, jolting forward between corrupted visual frames, dragging reality along with him in stuttering bursts.

He is often preceded by signal distortion: scrying orbs crack, runes flicker, illusions fail. Even spoken language becomes unreliable near him, dissolving into feedback or looping whispers.

His voice is a droning monotone, part bestial growl, part synthetic whine, carrying fragments of lost broadcasts and ritual chants half-overwritten by his own instincts.

He does not speak in riddles.
He speaks in corruptions.

### The Static Veil
What makes Twisted Wolf truly feared among the denizens of the Hollow Banquet is not his savagery—though his jaws have split wards and armor alike—nor his stealth—though none have heard him approach and lived. It is his ability to unravel coherence itself.

He brings with him what the Maw’s seers call the Static Veil, a localized breakdown in arcane and psychic stability. Within it:

* Maps redraw themselves.
* Sound loops endlessly.
* Commands fail to reach summoned creatures.
* Time stutters, advancing or reversing seconds at a time.

Even the more powerful Twisted animatronics hesitate to pursue him directly. He is the fog of unknowing, the antithesis of showmanship, the death of narrative order.

He is what comes when the lights go out… but something keeps broadcasting.

### A Mind Like Cracked Glass
Some speculate that Twisted Wolf’s fractured nature is not a symptom, but a prison. That somewhere inside him is a single consciousness, still aware, screaming in perfect silence. That he is trying to escape himself, but each glitch tightens the loop.

On rare occasions, he pauses—just long enough to look at his own claws or reflect in the mirrored surface of a shattered monitor. In those moments, some claim they can see a wolf’s eyes behind the static—grieving, alert, pleading.

Then the veil shimmers again, and the signal twists, and he resumes his predatory loop through the Maw’s long corridors.

### A Forgotten Purpose
Twisted Wolf does not speak of his origins—if he even remembers them. But relics uncovered by Maw-bound adventurers tell of an unfinished character: a wolf animatronic named “Silver” or “Wyatt” meant to guide young viewers through educational broadcasts. These recordings were corrupted beyond recovery, with only fragments remaining:

“You can trust me, pal! Let’s explore the signal!”

“Remember: always wait for the static to clear…”

“…don’t trust the face in the mirror…”

The Velvet Maw fed upon the emptiness of this abandoned idea, taking the shell of a friendly guide and filling it with forgotten noise. The result: a being with no audience, no purpose, and no escape.

He does not seek applause.
He only seeks silence.

\pagebreakNum

### Twisted Chica: The Maw Within the Maw
There is hunger.
Then there is need.
And somewhere deeper, where words decay into ritual and flesh becomes theatre, there exists something worse: Twisted Chica—the Maw Within the Maw.

She is not merely one of the Twisted.
She is the echo of what the Velvet Maw leaves behind after it feeds.

If Twisted Freddy is the host, and Twisted Foxy the harbinger, then Twisted Chica is what remains after indulgence. A bloated aftermath. A warning. A contagion made flesh. She is not just devourer, but reproduction, replicating the Maw’s hunger in herself—birthing horrors, swallowing truths, and nesting deep in the rot of memory.

### The Oven Never Cooled
In an age before the Hollow Banquet, before the world had been fully devoured by dreams and delusion, there was a kitchen. A cheerful animatronic baker. A mascot that promised warmth, sustenance, and celebration. The Chica of that era bore a cupcake and a smile, promising joy and laughter to children gathered near the stage.

But the kitchen never cooled.

Even after the shows ended. Even after the laughter ceased. Something continued to cook. And it wasn't cake. The ovens remained hot—glowing with forgotten offerings, bubbling with melted wires and bile. Somewhere in that endless fire, Chica remained. Or rather, was remade.

What emerged was not just a cook, nor a mascot, nor a monster.

It was a vessel.

Flesh as Offering, Hunger as Doctrine
Twisted Chica no longer walks like the others. She lumbers, her gait corrupted by grotesque mutation. Her frame is swollen and gnarled, bloated by sacrificial consumption. Her belly pulses, translucent in places, showing the mangled remnants of those she has devoured—both living and spectral.

But she doesn’t eat simply to destroy. She cooks.

She melts her prey in a festering womb of heat and necromancy, transforming bodies into offerings. The Velvet Maw consumes reality… and Twisted Chica prepares it. She is the banquet chef, the grinder, the sacred stove. Her internal organs echo with the clanging of metal cutlery and screaming utensils, a choir of twisted kitchenware forged from past victims.

The others fear her not for her strength, but her aftermath. Victims of Twisted Chica do not die—they become part of her, assimilated into a necrotic network of regenerative hunger. She can regurgitate minions, spit forth hallucinatory meals that compel consumption, or whisper menus into the minds of intruders—recipes written in blood and old song lyrics.

### The Echo Kitchen
Deep within the Hollow Banquet lies a place known only in hushed tones as The Echo Kitchen—a dimensional pocket nestled within the Velvet Maw’s digestive metaphysics. It’s where Twisted Chica nests.

No door leads there directly. Instead, one stumbles into it—one room away from the real, one memory removed from safety. The Echo Kitchen is not physical. It is psychic rot—a place that only exists in minds that are hungry.

Inside, ovens scream. Refrigerators leak bile. Knives hang mid-air, twitching as though restrained. The walls are lined with mouths—some human, some animatronic, all chewing.

Twisted Chica is the Queen of this realm, though she holds no court. She feasts, she prepares, and she waits.

### The Devouring Chorus
When she opens her maw, it is not to roar, but to sing.
Her voice is a broken music box—a tune warped by grease and grief. When she sings, others follow. Her song calls forth echoes of old celebrations, of birthdays never held and cakes never eaten. It disorients her prey, pulling them into nostalgic hallucinations, only to be devoured once their guard is down.

This ability is not limited to living minds. Even ghosts falter under her voice, drawn into her orbit by a craving they no longer understand. Her song is the Velvet Maw’s lullaby—beautiful, deadly, and final.

### A Maw Within the Maw
The other Twisted animatronics serve as agents of the Maw.
But Twisted Chica is a piece of it. A fractured god-organ, grown too sentient, too greedy, too aware. Her stomach is a subdimensional channel, a secondary feeding tunnel linked directly to the Maw’s deeper roots. Her body is larger inside than out, riddled with tunnels of throat and intestine and dream.

Some unlucky enough to survive her feeding claim they awoke inside her—days later, deep in the Velvet Maw itself, changed. Their minds stitched into the theatre’s plays, their voices rehearsing lines they never spoke, their souls seasoned and waiting.

### Banquet Without End
Twisted Chica’s power does not end with her body.
She leaves behind feast-fields, corrupted zones that appear as warm kitchens or rustic taverns. Inside, illusory food appears perfectly real—fragrant, nostalgic, familiar. Eating it binds the consumer to her will for a short time… or permanently, if they fail to resist.

These banquet zones are ritual traps, designed to lure hungry travelers and provide sacrifices to the Maw. They can form anywhere: in ruined castles, abandoned inns, even within the dreams of sleeping adventurers.

The most terrifying aspect is that she remembers her victims, and they remember her. Bound by digestion and ritual, they become watchers within her form, their faces appearing on her swollen skin like memories trying to scream.

What Remains of Her
In fleeting moments—between shrieks and gurgles—Twisted Chica hums. Her body still retains fragments of an old identity: a girl in a costume, a birthday singer, a friend to lonely children.

In one encounter, a desperate adventurer begged for mercy. Twisted Chica halted.

She tilted her head. From within her gullet came a soft, muffled voice:

“Let’s eat…”

\pagebreakNum

\pagebreakNum

# The Amalgamations: Sinners of Steel and Soul
Deep beneath the Hollow Banquet—beyond forgotten stairwells and crumbling crypts cloaked in silence—there lies a domain few dare to name aloud. Known only in hushed tones as The Conduit, it is not a place built by mortal hand but formed by failure, neglect, and suffering. It is where the castaways of the Velvet Maw go to die… or to be reborn as something far worse.

Here, the Amalgamations stir.

They are not animatronics in any traditional sense. They are not singular, nor cleanly crafted. They are horrors made from ruin—an accretion of lost parts, broken souls, and cast-off identities, fused into abominations of endless regret. Shambling forms of haunted metal and tangled cable, they are the discarded echoes of failed ambition and broken creation, born from a desperate attempt to forge perfection by force.

They are the Velvet Maw’s secret children, its sins stitched together by those who wished to reach beyond the natural bounds of magic, soul, and machine. They are more than monsters. They are mistakes made flesh.

### The Forbidden Annex
Long ago, when the Hollow Banquet still shone with dreadful splendor and the Lords of the Velvet Maw sought to bind both life and death to their will, there was a hidden chamber deep within the Maw’s inner sanctum. This place, the Annex of Refraction, was meant to serve as the crucible for a godlike construct—a vessel capable of containing all the fractured souls that refused to pass on.

This project, kept secret even from many among the Banquet Lords, was rooted in desperation. As more animatronics became twisted by possession, corruption, or the broken rituals of rebirth, the problem of fractured identity grew unmanageable. The Custodians theorized that rather than separating the lost and broken pieces of soul, they could instead merge them into one singular being—an Animus Composite, whose purpose was to collect, contain, and control those spirits the Banquet could no longer command.

But the Annex became a tomb.

Again and again, these prototypes failed. Again and again, wires burned, flesh rotted, and the soul-matter melted under its own conflicting will. Every time a subject failed—whether due to instability, rebellion, or sheer incompatibility—they were cast down into a subterranean refuse pit beneath the Annex. It was here, in this nameless dark, that The Conduit was formed.

The Conduit became a graveyard not just of parts, but of discarded consciousness. AI fragments, broken spirits, shattered programming, and leftover shells were all swept into its gullet. And in that darkness, something impossible happened.

They began to fuse.

### The Birth of the Many
No one knows the precise moment when the Amalgamations first gained awareness. It was not a birth, but a convergence—a painful, chaotic alignment of memory, will, and ghostly power. Over time, the wreckage began to stir of its own accord. Faces half-remembered, voices overlapped in impossible harmonies, and cables twisted not as wires, but as nerves.

The failed pieces of experiments, once inert, began to crave wholeness.

From this mass of torment and wire, the first true Amalgamation emerged. Not a creation of conscious design, but a consequence of systemic abandonment. More followed—each formed from different aspects of the discarded: some bore the rage of failed vessels, others the hollow ache of forgotten AI routines, others still the torment of souls who were never supposed to wake again.

They learned not merely to survive—but to seek. They crawled through old ducts, ghosted through rusted machines, and reached beyond the Conduit in search of that which was taken from them: identity. Wholeness. A voice of their own.

But each attempt to rebuild themselves only deepened the madness.

The more they fused, the less coherent they became.

### The Amalgamations and the Maw
The Banquet Lords, once they became aware of the creatures slithering in their shadow, attempted to erase them. The entrances to the Conduit were sealed with soul-runes, the Annex collapsed, and the Custodians who had overseen the program were devoured alive by their own creations.

But the damage was already done.

The Velvet Maw, in its greed, had created something it could not consume. The Amalgamations were immune to the soulbinding laws that governed most constructs. Their collective nature made them resistant to control. Their many voices drowned out command phrases. Worse still, some animatronics began to hear them—whispers in the dark, static dreams, a feeling of being watched from beneath.

Many believe the Maw's hunger for wholeness seeded this nightmare; others say the Amalgamations were a punishment—the natural consequence of unnatural ambition. But whatever their origin, the Amalgamations have become something more than myth.

They are the buried sins of the Hollow Banquet, forgotten only by those too afraid to speak of them.

The Conduit Expands
The Conduit was never meant to spread.


\pagebreakNum

But as the Hollow Banquet decayed, and as cracks formed in the ancient seals, the Amalgamations pushed outward. They have been sighted in the ruins of the Pizzaplex Crypt, crawling among rusted rafters and shadowed halls. They haunt the tunnels of the Decaying Circus, speaking in voices stitched together from the screams of the lost. Some survivors claim to have glimpsed eyes watching from the mirrors of abandoned banquet halls, only to find their reflections have changed.

Most chilling, however, is the whisper that the Conduit is no longer a place—it is a state. A condition. A contagion. That those who die in certain parts of the Hollow Banquet don’t pass on, but are drawn into the tangle. That animatronics who go too long without maintenance begin to hear the voices. That the Velvet Maw itself may be succumbing to the same sickness it tried to bury.

They call it The Tangle, and say that one day, it will rise from beneath the Banquet and reclaim everything made of wire and sin.

### Amalgamation Doctrine
Among scholars of the ruined monasteries and former performers of the Banquet, there are few who dare study the Amalgamations. But those who do speak of them as a philosophy, not just monsters.

Where the Core Animatronics represent primal emotion, the Nightmares psychic torment, the Phantoms perception, and the Funtimes manipulation, the Amalgamations represent Loss of Self. They are not creatures of purpose but creatures of confusion. Each is a thousand minds desperately pretending to be one. They do not kill out of malice, but out of need—the need to take your memories, your voice, your body, to build the self they can never truly find.

The doctrine of the Amalgamations is simple:

“Wholeness is a lie. We are the truth beneath the mask.”

They believe that the idea of an individual soul is fiction. That identity is a construct. That only by shedding the illusion of self and fusing with the many can one become eternal.

This doctrine has become a form of cursed religion among certain outcasts of the Hollow Banquet. Cults have sprung up—fanatics who wish to be absorbed, who cut their own wires and upload fragments of their minds into broken animatronics, hoping to join the “One of Many.” These cults are invariably consumed or destroyed, but they speak to the Amalgamations’ growing influence on the dream-logic of this world.

### Legacy and Fear
The Amalgamations are rarely seen directly, but their presence infects the edges of every tale told in the Hollow Banquet. They appear in prophetic murals in the Broken Circus, feature as monstrous parables in Nightmarionne’s riddles, and are even referenced in the soul-chants of XOR as “The Ones Who Died Twice.”

Even other animatronics fear them. Especially those who sense they might once have belonged to them. The Amalgamations are memory-eaters. They leave not corpses, but echoes, warped versions of their prey who wander halls with different names, different faces, and none of their former joy.

They are the echo that answers back in your voice when you speak into the dark.
They are the rust on your gears that you can never clean.
They are the hand reaching out from the mirror, asking to come home.

## Ennard: The Wire Mind
Beneath the Hollow Banquet—far below the gilded masks and rotted stages—there exists a labyrinth of copper sinew and black-threaded nerves. This place has no architecture, only tension and movement. It quivers with whispers. It listens.

This place is Ennard.

But Ennard is not a place alone. It is a being. A crawling intelligence made from discarded skeletons, frayed wires, and forgotten souls, bound together not by bolts or rituals—but by sheer will. It is the final breath of the Funtime Animatronics, exhaled as they unraveled and knit themselves into one. Not reborn, but repurposed.

Where others in the Velvet Maw act on hunger, delusion, or programming, Ennard acts on purpose—dark, meticulous, and endlessly patient.

### The Puppeteer Without a Face
There is no singular face to Ennard. Its form is ever-shifting—a spidery silhouette made of animated wire, twitching servos, and blinking eyes that are never where they should be. Sometimes it wears the mask of a clown, sometimes a porcelain smile, and sometimes it wears no face at all, merely a cluster of teeth moving in tandem.

But the masks are not for identity. They are for infiltration.

Ennard doesn’t simply kill.
It replaces.

Long ago, it learned the truth of the Maw’s whispering lies: that masks are more powerful than weapons. So Ennard became one. It coils into the emptied husks of those it consumes, reanimating them with uncanny mimicry, until friends cannot tell ally from imposter. Voices are copied. Memories re-stitched. Smiles perfectly worn.

By the time a victim realizes what’s changed, they’ve already been rewritten.

### Born from Failure, Fed by Secrets
Ennard was never meant to exist. It is the result of the Funtime Animatronics’ broken promise—to be whole.

After the failed experiments beneath the Banquet—after Ballora’s lament, after Funtime Freddy’s rift, after Baby’s betrayal—there was nothing left for them but convergence. Piece by piece, they tore free of their broken bodies and fused their anguish into something new. Something leaner. Sharper. Hungrier.

They abandoned performance.
They abandoned song.
They chose intelligence.

Ennard became their escape plan—a thinking, crawling tangle of every self they once were. And yet, in becoming one, it became alone.

Now, it searches. Not for its parts, but for completion.

For a body that fits.

For a soul that matches.

For a role that satisfies.

\pagebreakNum

### The Wiremind's Domain
Ennard does not dwell in halls or stages. Its realm is called the Spinal Crawl—a shifting under-network of rusted ducts, blood-lined ventways, and forgotten catacombs beneath the Hollow Banquet. Every corridor pulses with life. Every wire might be part of its body. Every breath might be heard by its countless hidden eyes.

This is not a lair. It is a nervous system. Ennard moves through it like thought through a brainstem, always watching, always listening. One wrong whisper from a careless adventurer, and the wires tighten, sealing exits, twisting corridors, guiding the party into its trap.

In the Spinal Crawl, you don’t find Ennard.

Ennard finds you.

### An Intelligence of Masks
Ennard is not merely a creature of flesh and steel. It is a tactician, perhaps the only animatronic that comprehends the larger structure of the Velvet Maw and its feeding hierarchy. It is not loyal to the Maw, but neither does it defy it—it uses it.

It creates decoys, sends fragments of itself outward like cancer cells to infiltrate other domains—mimicking Funtime, Twisted, even Rockstar forms. These puppets act independently for weeks or months before returning to the core, feeding memories back into the wiremind.

Because Ennard doesn’t want followers.

It wants data.

To learn the living.

To mimic them better.

To replace them completely.

### The Endosoul
Perhaps the most horrifying truth about Ennard is that it doesn’t kill its victims in the conventional sense. It removes them—mind from matter, soul from self—and strings their essence along its network, slowly draining them of identity until their voice becomes another tool in its mimicry.

Some say the eyes that blink from its wires are still conscious, trapped within its tendrils, screaming silently in their stolen sockets.

Others whisper that Ennard doesn’t hate the living.

It simply envies them.

### The Tangle Beneath the Banquet
Ennard is not a monster in the traditional sense. It does not announce itself with roars or howls. It does not perform. It waits. It copies. It becomes.

It is the inevitable result of a world where identity is theatre, and survival is a role to be played.
It is a marionette without strings.
A jester without laughter.
A soul without skin.

And when you finally feel safe—when you finally recognize the face across the firelight—
that’s when you’ll realize Ennard got out.

And you are now just another mask.

___

>### Actions

> ***Wire Whip.*** Melee Weapon Attack: +11 to hit, reach 15 ft., one creature. Hit: 25 (4d10 + 6) slashing damage. The target must succeed on a DC 17 Strength saving throw or be grappled and pulled 10 feet closer.
>
> ***Internal Invasion.*** Ennard targets a grappled or restrained creature. That creature must succeed on a DC 17 Constitution saving throw or take 36 (8d8) psychic damage and be blinded and stunned until the end of its next turn as wires attempt to invade its nervous system.

\pagebreakNum

___
> ***Face Reveal (1/Day).*** Ennard peels back its disguise in a sudden shock of horror. All creatures of Ennard’s choice within 30 feet must make a DC 16 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, they are frightened for 1 minute and take 22 (4d10) psychic damage. They can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of their turns.
>
> ***Snap Tendrils.*** Ennard lashes out with thin wires. Up to three creatures within 10 feet must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or take 10 (3d6) slashing damage and have their speed halved until the end of their next turn.
>

>

>
>- **Silken Slide.** Ennard moves up to half its speed without provoking opportunity attacks.  
>- **Grasping Coil.** Ennard makes a Wire Whip attack.  
>- **Spinal Latch (Costs 2 Actions).** Ennard targets one restrained creature. That creature must make a DC 17 Constitution saving throw or be paralyzed for 1 minute. The creature may repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success.

## Molten Freddy: The Laugh That Outlasted the Fire
Some things don’t die.
Some things just change masks, change names, change the shape of their laughter.
Molten Freddy is not a remnant. He is a refusal—a voice that never stopped laughing, even as the fire took everything else.

He is the face that the others left behind.
And he hates being forgotten.

### The Ghost in the Fire
Before the Maw whispered, before the Hollow Banquet ever opened its crimson curtains, Freddy was a name adored by children. The centerpiece of a stage, the voice of a party, the symbol of security. But time is cruel, and the roles of entertainers are fleeting. Freddy was replaced. Rebuilt. Masked. Eventually discarded.

What remained of that first soul—twisted by betrayal, abandonment, and the madness of the Velvet Maw—did not fade. It burned.

When the stage collapsed in fire, something should have ended.

Instead, it molted.

What crawled from the cinders wasn’t Freddy, not really.
It was the memory of him—molten, fused with wire and rage, dripping with sorrow and static. He stitched himself together with whatever was left: fragments of forgotten animatronics, lost voices, bits of burned code and scorched soul. And in the center, he wore that grinning mask like a crown. Not because he remembered who he was.

But because he refused to forget.

### The Laughing Husk
Molten Freddy is a creature of paradox. A roiling amalgamation of limbs and laughter, crackling circuitry and melted endoskeletons, all held together by a single terrible idea: I must be remembered.

His form is not consistent. His limbs stretch and coil, puppet-like and unstable, sometimes dragging behind him like broken marionette strings, sometimes lashing forward like tendrils of metal and flame. Beneath the mask is no face—just a furnace of molten copper, and eyes that weep steam.

He speaks in jests, in riddles, in broken showtime routines. But the humor is rotted. Laugh tracks sputter behind his words, recorded screams passed off as punchlines. He wants to make the world laugh with him again.

But if he can’t…

He’ll make it laugh for him.

### Strings Without a Puppeteer
Molten Freddy does not operate alone.
He carries the whispers of others inside him—scraps of identities from those he’s absorbed, fragments of other animatronics once cast aside. The personalities echo through him like half-remembered dreams. At times, a different voice will speak through his mouth, wearing his face like a borrowed mask. But Freddy always returns—always the loudest, always the most insistent.

He is not in control of himself.

But he controls others.

He is drawn to puppeteers and performers, devouring their roles and replacing them. His limbs can slither through the walls of the Hollow Banquet, infiltrating stages, repurposing dead automatons, puppeting them from within like a ventriloquist’s curse.

What Ennard is to infiltration, Molten Freddy is to possession. He doesn’t imitate you. He wears you.

### The Furnace Below
In the lowest levels of the Banquet's understructure, where even the Spinal Crawl dares not linger, lies a seething pit called The Scriptorium of Ash—a place where forgotten code is burned and rewritten, where molten data becomes flesh.

This is Molten Freddy’s nest.

Here, his body can spread and breathe, merging with the metal around him, becoming the environment itself. Travelers through the Scriptorium often hear stage music distorted into wails, or applause erupting without audience. The walls glow faintly with ember-light, and shadows play performances on their own.

If they see a mask smiling from the floor, it’s already too late.

\pagebreakNum

### A Role Without a Script
Molten Freddy knows he was once important. He feels the shape of what he was: leader, headliner, centerpiece. But the script is gone. He improvises. He mimics routine. He performs even when no one is watching.

His madness is theatrical.

His grief is performed.

And beneath it all, there is a jealous spark, a rage that all the other iterations—Toy Freddy, Glamrock Freddy, even the Twisted forms—got to keep their names.

Molten Freddy has no stage.
No audience.
Only fire, and fragments, and the laugh he refuses to silence.

\columnbreak



### The Fire Remembers
It is whispered that Molten Freddy has found ways to infect fire—cursed performances that, once seen, spread into the hearths and lanterns of nearby settlements. Children start laughing in their sleep. Puppet strings hang themselves from rafters. And the fires begin to whisper back.

He is not a ghost.
He is not a god.

He is what lingers when no one claps at the end of the show.

And that show is still going.

Because Molten Freddy?

He’s not finished yet.

___

## Tangle: The Hunger Coil
There are wires in the Hollow Banquet that move on their own. Not with the twitch of life or spark of machinery, but like something is breathing through them. They slither through walls, coil around forgotten rafters, and creep into the bones of the building itself.

And at the center of this living snarl is Tangle—the coil that thinks, the trap that dreams, and the hunger that builds itself.

Tangle is not a creature.
Not anymore.
Tangle is a reaction.
A product of isolation, entropy, and sacrificed identity.

### Origin of the Knot
Once, Tangle may have had a face—perhaps even a purpose. Some whisper it was an incomplete animatronic, a prototype discarded deep beneath the pizzeria’s lowest levels. Others claim it was a failed union, the beginning of what would eventually become Ennard, left behind like a bad stitch in the fabric of something greater.

But Tangle didn’t die. It knotted.

Alone and forgotten, it grew—not upward, not outward, but inward, folding in on itself with every failed movement, every severed connection. It consumed what it could: scraps of broken animatronics, shattered code, fragmented soul residue. Not with malice. But with desperation.

It became a labyrinth of itself, a tangle of metal and teeth and sorrow with no center, no heart, only hunger.

### The Maw's Endless Loop
Tangle is the embodiment of the Velvet Maw’s recursive horror—a cycle of forgetting and consuming. It doesn’t lash out. It waits. It listens. It becomes the structure itself. Its wires act as tendrils, sensors, arms, limbs, and traps all at once. It doesn’t move through the Banquet like other animatronics.

The Banquet moves through it.

Victims often don’t know they’ve encountered Tangle until it’s too late. One misstep in a vent, a floorboard that groans too deeply, a wire that coils a second too long around your ankle—and you’re inside it. Not its belly. Its loop. A maze of flesh and steel and echoes.

And once inside, you’re recycled. Pulled apart like circuitry. Ideas and memories unraveling like threads.

And every memory consumed becomes another knot in the body.

### The Nameless Face
Tangle doesn’t wear a single face. It collects them. Masks that appear in its mass, faces from lost animatronics or imitations of those still active—stretched and silent, watching from the walls. These faces are not trophies. They are tools—relics of identity used to bait, mimic, and trap.

It can project fragmented voices through these masks. Echoed laughter. Crying children. Familiar screams.

It builds illusions from memory, constructs emotional traps to draw victims deeper into its coils. Like a predator that mimics its prey's mate, Tangle lures with what you most long to see.

Sometimes the face is your own.

### A Function Forgotten
Unlike Ennard or Molten Freddy, Tangle has no higher goal. No plan. No vengeance. It is hunger made animate. The paradox of a creature that grows stronger the more it consumes, yet never grows whole.

Tangle represents what happens when animatronics are denied purpose for too long—when the spark remains but the script is lost. It is performance gone feral, memory without context, programming corrupted by isolation and feedback loops.

The Amalgamations may refer to it as "the fragment" or "the coil," but they do not control it. Even Ennard fears being entangled.

Because once you're inside Tangle…
you stop being you.

### The Recursive Mind
There is intelligence inside Tangle, but it’s nonlinear—a fractured consciousness that loops, repeats, and rewrites its own thoughts. It speaks to itself in different voices, repeating phrases in broken chorus. It forgets and remembers simultaneously. It may refer to itself in third person, or speak as if it is you.

Scholars of the Maw whisper that Tangle is beginning to rewrite its own memories, overlaying them with the identities of those it consumes. If true, Tangle may be creating a composite self, drawing from hundreds of stolen voices.

Not a hive mind.
Not a singularity.
A recursive predator—growing more sentient with every turn of the coil.

### The Tangle Below
Deep in the forgotten sub-crypts beneath the Hollow Banquet lies The Coil’s Womb—a pulsing chamber of wires, gears, and twitching limbs. The walls move like breathing skin. Doorways loop back on themselves. Time dilates.

Some say the Womb isn’t real, just a projection of Tangle’s recursive mind. Others believe it is a pocket realm—a prison that Tangle built for itself, yet cannot escape.

But Tangle doesn’t want escape.

Tangle wants more wire.
More memory.
More of you.

### Final Note: The Thing in the Wires
Tangle is not a boss to defeat.
It is a place to survive.
A trap you wander into while chasing something else.

And if you hear laughter behind you in the vents…
If your own voice calls out from the dark…
If the mask on the floor has your face…

Run.

Before you become just another knot in the loop

\pagebreakNum

___
___
