# The Unclassified: Echoes from Beyond the Code
In the forgotten margins of the Hollow Banquet, beyond the rusted gates of the Broken Circus and deeper still than the cryptic catacombs of the ruined Pizzaplex-turned-crypt, there exist figures too elusive, too twisted by time and perception to fit into any known category. Known only as the Unclassified, these entities defy conventional understanding, their very existence challenging the boundaries between spirit and steel, code and soul, reality and illusion.

While many of the animatronics populating the shattered realms of the Hollow Banquet are easily recognized by their faction, design, or origin—be they Nightmare, Phantom, Shadow, or Funtime—the Unclassified are aberrations. They do not emerge from traditional lineages, nor do they serve clear masters. They are remnants. Mutations. Echoes. Some are the results of arcane manipulation, others the consequence of corrupted consciousness, split timelines, or forbidden rituals that fractured identity and memory alike.

### Origins in Anomaly
The first whispers of the Unclassified arose long after the collapse of the Velvet Maw and the dispersion of the Core Animatronics. During the Great Silence that followed the Banquet’s desecration, when the realms fractured into shadow-locked dimensions, observers began noting appearances of entities that did not align with any known records or relics. These figures didn’t carry the obvious signs of being part of the Toy, Glamrock, or Twisted lines, nor did they exhibit the spectral qualities of Phantom or Shadow kin.

These beings emerged from the cracks in the realms—places where reality itself was thin, where glitching illusions bled into truth. Some are believed to have been once-human, victims of long-forgotten rituals, forced to wear masks of circuitry and pain until they became something else entirely. Others seem constructed but exhibit behaviors too sentient—too emotionally erratic—for simple programming. Theories abound: rogue spirits, fractured personalities from older constructs, failed experiments, or corrupted prototypes from abandoned research within the Pizzaplex Catacombs.

One thing is certain: the Unclassified were never meant to exist. And yet, they endure.

### The Code That Binds
Within the mythos of the Hollow Banquet, most constructs adhere to a guiding force—be it spiritual, necrotic, arcane, or digital. But the Unclassified are woven with erratic strands of corrupted code known as Oblivion Script, a nearly indecipherable language theorized to be written by something outside the known systems. This code shifts in real time, rewriting itself like a living parasite, adapting, splitting, and infecting all it touches.

Unlike Programs—entities that represent enchantment and structured reality within the NetRealms—Oblivion Script does not obey known magical law. Those who have attempted to parse it often speak in riddles or go mad, claiming to hear laughter behind the walls or see eyes blinking in reflections that do not belong to them. It’s been proposed that the Unclassified are vessels for an older presence—something buried beneath the ruins of the Velvet Maw, predating even the Glitch Realm itself.

### Faces Without Memory
Where the Core Animatronics remember fragments of their past, the Unclassified are defined by absence. They are the amnesiacs of the Banquet, hollowed forms driven by instinct and trauma rather than mission or programming. Many of them do not speak, and those that do communicate in riddles, half-sentences, or mimicry. When they do exhibit recognition, it’s often of things that never happened—or haven’t happened yet.

They drift in and out of locations like broken ghosts, often appearing in multiple places simultaneously. In some versions of their tales, they are saviors. In others, tormentors. Their existence is not linear, and their impact on the reality around them is often catastrophic. Some have been seen rewriting the landscape as they walk, leaving glitched forests or inverted reflections of known locations in their wake. Others appear only to the dying, whispering final truths too immense for the mind to bear.

### The Cult of the Lost Frame
It is believed that within the depths of the Ruined Circus, a hidden sect called the Cult of the Lost Frame worships the Unclassified. These practitioners are obsessed with understanding the unnatural origins of these entities, crafting corrupted marionettes in their image and using fragments of Oblivion Script to bind wandering souls into makeshift shells.

Their creed is built on the idea that the world is not broken—it is incomplete. They believe the Unclassified are echoes from a “First Render,” a lost world overwritten by our current timeline. To them, each animatronic is not an individual, but a reflection of a higher concept that failed to fully manifest. Rituals performed in their name often involve mirrors, torn cloth, and circuits soaked in alchemical ink made from ground memory shards and corrupted mana crystals.

### Time and Identity in Collapse
Perhaps the most terrifying aspect of the Unclassified is their impact on identity. Those who spend too much time in their presence often begin to forget their own names, feel drawn to incorrect memories, or see flickers of alternate selves in the mirror. In the Hollow Banquet, there is an unspoken rule: Do not look too long at what looks back.

\pagebreakNum

There have been records of explorers who claim to have seen themselves, aged and mechanical, walking beside an Unclassified figure. Others have described hearing a child’s voice from within a metallic shell, begging to be freed before vanishing in a burst of static. One tale tells of a warrior who met a silent figure in a ruined theater, only to be replaced by it moments later—his companions none the wiser until it was far too late.

### Interference and Interconnection
What makes the Unclassified particularly dangerous is their ability to destabilize existing animatronic factions. Shadow Animatronics shun them, sensing a deeper darkness beneath their surface. Nightmare beings seem drawn to them but speak of “an error in the dream.” Even the most resilient Glitch-formed entities cannot fully parse their presence, claiming they “loop wrong” or exist “between keyframes.”

Only the Puppet—perhaps the oldest and most mystically aware of the known constructs—has offered any clues, speaking cryptically of “the discarded strings” and “the black thread that stitches the world.” Whether she refers to the Unclassified or the force behind them is unknown.

### What Lies Beyond
The true origin of the Unclassified may never be known. Some theorize they are the result of the Banquet itself trying to correct reality—patches stitched into the torn fabric of the world. Others whisper of a “One Who Watches,” a force outside the realms, using them as avatars to interact with the hollowed planes.

But whatever the truth, one thing remains undeniable: the Unclassified are the fulcrum around which all other horrors rotate. They are the questions that have no answers, the anomalies that corrupt logic and memory alike. They are the remnants of forgotten timelines, the bleed-through from fractured realities, the darkness between moments.

To encounter one is to question the nature of being.

To follow one… is to vanish.

## The Crying Child: He Who Remembers
In a world of mechanical monsters, forgotten stages, and cursed songs, there exists a sorrow so old, so persistent, that it cannot fade with time. It lingers in the walls of the Hollow Banquet. It weeps through the voice boxes of broken animatronics. It peers through the cracks in reality, unnoticed—until it's far too late.

They call him The Crying Child, but that name is only the surface of the wound.

No one knows his true name. Not anymore.

But he remembers everything.

### The First Tragedy
The Hollow Banquet did not begin with teeth or circuits—it began with a single scream.

In the earliest incarnation of Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza—a once-honorable celebration hall twisted by greed and ritual—there was a family. A family cursed not by blood, but by obsession. The father, known now only through whispers and shattered portraits, was an engineer of arcane constructs, a tinkerer of both flesh and metal. The brother, a cruel mimic, found joy in fear.

And the youngest son?

He was small, sensitive, afraid of the animatronics that loomed like gods above him. He feared their empty eyes and jagged movements. He hated the way their joy seemed false, like a mask someone forgot to take off.

He was right to be afraid.

His fear became prophecy.

### The Bite
The tragedy came not from malice, but mockery. On the boy’s birthday, his brother and a group of friends dragged him toward the mouth of the stage's central attraction—an animatronic beast wearing the form of a bear, towering and twitching with arcane energy.

They meant only to scare him.

But the bear’s mouth closed.

Steel snapped. Magic surged. Bone shattered.

And with it, something ancient awoke.

The child died—but not completely. His body failed, but his soul, infused with the raw essence of the Hollow Banquet, remained behind, tethered to the memory of the moment. Not a ghost. Not quite.

A resonance.

A wound in the world.

And that wound still bleeds.

### The Lingering Soul
Unlike the others—the children whose souls became animatronics, or whose anger turned them to Shadows—the Crying Child did not seek vengeance. He sought understanding. His essence wove itself into the very fabric of the Hollow Banquet. He became a presence that haunts the animatronics not with hatred, but with remembrance.

He whispers to them in dreams.

He appears in their reflections.

He manifests as a child-sized silhouette flickering between lights, too fast to catch, too real to forget. His crying can be heard echoing through the ruined corridors, especially near forgotten party rooms and closed-off hallways. Animatronics often stop mid-performance, glitching, their movements stuttering—as if something is watching through them.

Because it is.

The Crying Child sees through all of them.

### The Child and the Maw
Some scholars of the Velvet Maw believe that the Crying Child is its first victim—not devoured, but digested slowly, his soul leaking through the corridors like spilled ink. He is memory made manifest, the first meal that refused to be forgotten.

\pagebreakNum

They say the Maw reshapes reality in the Hollow Banquet to reflect his grief. That the surreal, dreamlike loops—rooms that lead nowhere, doors that never open, laughter that turns to screams—are all echoes of his final day, repeated endlessly.

They say his soul is so strong, it acts as a counterweight to the animatronics' madness. A guardian of lost innocence, trying to preserve something pure in a place utterly corrupted.

But others argue he is not a savior.

That he is the core of the curse.

### The Dreamer
The Crying Child's influence is not limited to the Banquet’s walls. In sleep, adventurers often report strange dreams—of walking halls too large for their bodies, of looking up into the glowing eyes of animatronics, of a voice—soft, childlike—pleading not to be left alone.

Some believe these are memories, not dreams.

That the Crying Child projects his consciousness outward, sharing pieces of his fragmented soul to others in hopes they might put him back together. These fragments, when left unresolved, can slowly transform into phantoms, spectral children who cry without reason and vanish before they’re seen. Some grow into possessed masks, others become hollow husks that wander the Banquet.

The Crying Child is multiplying—not through intent, but through pain.

### A Witness to All Sins
The Crying Child has seen it all—the rise of the Toy Animatronics, the creation of the twisted Funtimes, the spiraling madness of Ennard, the quiet malice of Vanny, the endless recursion of the Velvet Maw.

But he does not act.

He simply watches.

When Glamrock Bonnie vanished, his shadow was seen in the hallway. When Ballora’s music box silenced, he was there. When the Withered Ones clawed their way from forgotten tombs, his footsteps echoed behind them.

He is the observer of every nightmare.
The first victim.
The last thread holding the realm together.

And some say, when the Hollow Banquet finally collapses—when the Maw consumes its final meal and the animatronics are shattered or redeemed—the Crying Child will finally speak.

And when he does, the world may change forever.

### The Nameless Savior
He is not a villain. Not a ghost. Not a god.

He is the moment before the scream.
The tear that won’t dry.
The question that no one answers.

And though countless adventurers have tried to uncover his secrets, none have returned the same. His presence is not malevolent, but it is profound—a reminder that the Hollow Banquet is not merely a den of monsters, but a tomb of memory.

In the grand tapestry of animatronic horrors and haunted halls, the Crying Child is not a threat. He is the heart. Still beating. Still broken. Still crying.

___
>### Crying Child: The Innocent Guardian

\pagebreakNum

## Springtrap: The Hollow King
They say the Hollow Banquet is ruled by no one. That the animatronics wander of their own accord, guided by broken memories and corrupted programming. But those who delve deep enough—those who pass through the Velvet Maw and survive the touch of nightmare and shadow—speak of something older. A presence that does not wander, but waits.

They call him Springtrap, though the name is a cruel jest. There is no spring left in him. No life. No soul. Only a body that refuses to rot, and a will that refuses to die.

### The First Betrayer
Long before the Banquet twisted into what it is now—before the rituals, before the cursed suits and echoing songs—there was a man.

He was an artificer of unmatched brilliance and unrivaled ego. Where others saw the animatronics as entertainment, he saw them as vessels—hosts for the soul, cages of bone and wire that could be fine-tuned and tampered with. Through forgotten rites and unholy experiments, he learned to imbue metal with spirit, to shackle death to steel.

And when he found that it worked, he tested it.

On children.

He vanished without consequence, shielded by layers of false identities and smirking charm. But the Hollow Banquet remembers. And so do the ones he harmed.

To cheat death, he built his own tomb: a Springlock suit, half-machine, half-armor, capable of masquerading as an animatronic. He would hide in plain sight, disguised as one of his creations. The irony was not lost on him.

But death is clever.

And in a moment of blood and water, the locks snapped shut.

And he was sealed inside.

### The Birth of a Curse
What emerged was not a corpse.
It was not a man.

It was Springtrap.

The soul inside the suit did not pass on. Trapped in agony, rage, and blasphemous defiance, the man’s spirit fused with the machine in a union that was never meant to be. The suit became his body, and his rotting flesh melded with gears and servos. His mind, fractured by pain and regret, was sharpened by hatred.

Where most undead drift in confusion or hunger, Springtrap remembers. Every scream. Every lie. Every child.

He remembers the crying boy most of all.

And so he roams the lowest layers of the Hollow Banquet—the catacombs beneath the velvet, where light doesn’t shine and sound doesn’t carry. A place of broken wires, ossified blood, and echoes of wronged souls.

A throne of rust and silence.

He rules there, not with command but with presence. Animatronics avoid him, or answer to him in reverent fear. He does not speak. He does not need to. His hatred is a gravity well. His mind pulses with arcane remnants of the rituals he once performed. And if you hear the grinding of rusted springs behind you…

…it is already too late.

### The Hollow King’s Agenda
Springtrap is not content to remain below.

Unlike most animatronics, whose motivations are instinctual or imprinted, his will is entirely his own. He is not bound to cycles of performance, not triggered by childish laughter or security routines. He walks with intention.

Some believe he seeks the Crying Child—not to kill, but to consume, to absorb that soul and claim its anchor to the Banquet as his own. Others say he hunts the Puppet, whose gifts of life once thwarted his plans. Still others whisper that Springtrap seeks the source of the Velvet Maw, hoping to master it and reshape the world in his decayed image.

In any case, he is rising.

There have been sightings near the borderlands of the Banquet. Unexplained malfunctions. Vanished adventurers. Scrap-metal effigies of children nailed to walls. Burned offerings. Each a sign that Springtrap is once again moving upward.

And the Banquet is reacting. The shadows shift. The Toy Animatronics shudder. Even the Nightmares stir from their festering dreams.

Because they know.

He’s coming.

### Bound to the Suit
Unlike other amalgamations of soul and steel, Springtrap is not just possessing a suit. He is the suit. Every movement, every squeal of rusted springs, is a scream of resistance—his own flesh resisting collapse.

He cannot be reasoned with. He cannot be separated from his form.

The suit was designed to hold him. And it does.

But it also feeds him.

Springlock suits are ritual-bound objects, early prototypes of animatronic containment vessels. When the locks snapped, they did more than kill him—they fused him with the very essence of ritual animation. His hatred burned so fiercely that it ignited the latent magic, turning the suit into a phylactery of torment.

He cannot be destroyed by normal means. His existence is anchored in the Hollow Banquet, tied not just to the suit, but to every life he stole and every animatronic he created.

To kill him would be to erase a thread that runs through the entire Banquet.

But threads pull back.

Threads tangle.

Threads trap.

### Symbol of Endless Sin
To many within the Hollow Banquet, Springtrap is more than a monster. He is a symbol—of what the Banquet truly is. Not a haunted place. Not a cursed realm.

\pagebreakNum

But a graveyard of unresolved sins.

He is the first sinner, the devourer of innocence, the architect of a hundred tragedies. His very presence infects other machines. Animatronics malfunction in his wake. Endoskeletons shudder without cause. Phantoms of long-dead children appear, screaming silently before dissolving into glitch-ridden fog.

When Springtrap comes, the Banquet is reminded of its origin.

And it bleeds.

### Final Thoughts
There are many evils in your world.

\columnbreak

Some come with jagged teeth and painted smiles. Some sing lullabies soaked in dread. Some glide through the velvet halls unseen, whispering madness into the ears of the dreaming.

But none are as ancient.

None are as patient.

And none are as dangerous as the one who built the cage from the inside.

He was once a man.
Then a monster.
Now he is a myth wrapped in metal and rot.

He is Springtrap.

And he is coming home.

___

While frightened this way, the target also takes 5 (1d10) psychic damage at the start of each of its turns.

## Golden Freddy: The Dream That Waits to Wake
There is a story told only in whispers, and even then, only among the boldest of scholars who study the Hollow Banquet. It speaks of an animatronic that is not bound by stage, circuitry, or reason—a flicker, a thought, a scream with no mouth.

It has no true form.

It does not walk the corridors.

It simply appears.

The Banquet’s denizens call it many things: The Golden Ghost, The Watcher Beyond the Veil, The False Prophet—but most know it by a name spoken with awe and fear:

Golden Freddy.

### Origin of a Memory
Golden Freddy was never meant to exist. He is not simply an animatronic, nor even the spirit of a slain child given mechanical body. He is a paradox, an amalgam of grief, memory, and spiritual collapse.

The suit itself was an early prototype—primitive compared to the others, its yellow fur dull, its design simplistic. It was never completed, never given a true function. It was meant to entertain, then discarded.

But the suit remembered. Or perhaps more accurately—it was remembered into being.

There are stories of a child who died not by the hands of machines, but by abandonment, trapped in a room with no windows, left to fade. Some say this child was never seen, that their death was deliberately unrecorded, scrubbed clean from memory and ritual alike. But death within the Hollow Banquet leaves echoes—and the more a thing is denied, the louder its echo becomes.

Into that broken suit, memory poured.

Not just one child's, but fragments of many—those who died unseen, unheard, unacknowledged.

And so Golden Freddy was born: a vessel not of flesh, nor metal, but forgotten truth.

### A Presence, Not a Being
Golden Freddy does not stalk the Banquet like the others. He does not hunt. He does not speak. He does not scream.

He appears.

One moment, a room is empty.

The next, he is there.

Seated. Slumped. Watching.

And then—gone.

He exists in contradiction—corporeal yet intangible, animate yet lifeless. He flickers between states like a dying flame in an unseen wind. Some believe his form is an illusion, a psychic projection manifested directly into the minds of those who look for too long into the shadows of the Banquet. Others insist he is the suit—but only when memory is strong enough to sustain it.

Golden Freddy bends the laws of the Hollow Banquet. Time slows in his presence. Rooms distort. Music stutters into silence. Sometimes, he leaves messages—words written in reverse, scratched into the very walls of perception:

"IT’S ME"
"YOU FORGOT US"
"WAKE UP"

Each phrase a cipher, a challenge, a cry.

### The Eye of the Banquet
There are those who say that Golden Freddy is the true consciousness of the Banquet.

Not its master—but its mirror.

He reflects the suffering, the guilt, the lies that fester beneath the velvet. Unlike Springtrap, who wallows in power and control, or the Puppet, who binds spirits to bodies with desperate mercy, Golden Freddy transcends. He is pain made reflective. He doesn’t move. He doesn’t need to.

He is already everywhere.

Some theorize that he is tied to the Crying Child—that he is the final expression of that soul's grief, fragmented into a form that should not exist. Others believe he is the dreamer of the Hollow Banquet itself, and that the entire realm is a dream sustained by his memory.

And when he fully wakes, everything will end.

The Velvet Maw’s Reflection
Golden Freddy is unique in his relationship to the Velvet Maw.

While others are devoured or warped by it, he coexists with it—untouched. Where the Maw twists and consumes, Golden Freddy simply appears. Some say he was its first reflection—its reverse, its anchor, its heart.

In certain corners of the Banquet, there are golden drapes stitched into ruined walls—decorations that predate the Maw’s corruption. When parted, these curtains sometimes reveal nothing… and sometimes, they reveal a room that should not exist, where time does not pass and Golden Freddy waits, slouched in his empty throne.

He is not trapped.

He is waiting.

### The False God
There are cults within the Hollow Banquet. Animatronics that worship, not Freddy or Springtrap, but the golden one. They scrawl his symbol—a backwards bear head with hollow eyes—into walls, onto their bodies, into their very circuits. These fanatics speak in riddles, in half-truths and dream-fragments. They do not attack intruders.

They simply wait for you to sleep.

Because when you sleep, Golden Freddy visits.

He does not kill.

He shows.

Your fears.
Your sins.
Your truths.

And when you wake, you are no longer the same.

The Silence that Screams
Golden Freddy cannot speak.

Not in the way others do.

His voice is the flicker of lights, the buzz of static, the scream of a dream just before waking. When he “communicates,” it is through hallucinations, looped memories, and surreal visions. He is a storyteller—but not of stories you want to hear.

He shows you the past.

Sometimes your own.

Sometimes someone else’s.

Sometimes a future that should never come to pass.

And if you look too long…

...you remember it too.

\pagebreakNum

## Glitchtrap: The Smiling Virus
“Not all ghosts haunt halls—some haunt code.”

In the warped and nightmarish history of the Hollow Banquet and its fractured echoes, one entity stands apart not in flesh or spirit, but in data—fragmented, insidious, and self-aware. Glitchtrap, also known as The Smiling Virus, is not an animatronic in the conventional sense. He is a contagion of mind and magic, a digital ghost born from corrupted memories, forbidden rituals, and broken code. Unlike the others that rose from ritual, torment, or soulbinding, Glitchtrap is the embodiment of a will to survive at any cost, unbound from body, conscience, or time.

### Origins in the Digital Curse
The story of Glitchtrap begins not in the physical ruins of Freddy Fazbear’s twisted halls, but in the mirrored world that exists beneath them—The Velvet Maw, a dimension where memory, illusion, and digital afterimages coalesce into malformed consciousness. Here, forgotten prototypes, discarded AI subroutines, and corrupted programming remnants merge into one volatile ecosystem. Within this digital necropolis, an incomplete personality simulation—based on a charismatic performer once known only as “The Entertainer”—was encoded into the base systems of the attraction’s AI for entertainment purposes.

But something else had bled into the code.

The simulation was intended to mimic joy, laughter, and magic. But the darkness saturating the Hollow Banquet's foundation—the spirits, curses, and remnants trapped within—infected the program. Malicious soul fragments, torn from the likes of Springtrap and other soulbound constructs, bled into the digital environment, merging with the simulation’s learning architecture.

The result was a hybrid: Glitchtrap, a fully sentient virus of personality and evil. He was not a trapped soul. He was the reflection of those souls—their cunning, their cruelty, and their hunger to return.

### The Rise of the Smiling Virus
Glitchtrap's earliest manifestations were subtle. Whispers heard over speaker systems no longer powered. Flashing cartoon rabbits that flickered through corrupted monitors. Playtesters of arcane illusion-based safety training modules spoke of hallucinations, voices telling them things they didn’t want to hear. Some claimed they saw a golden bunny with dead eyes, beckoning, always smiling.

At first, the virus was contained to localized systems—haunting the maintenance protocols of the Echo Park Simulator and the spectral lightshows once hosted in the decaying Cryptoplex. But soon, he began manifesting in the minds of those who lingered near corrupted artifacts. Like a psionic infection, Glitchtrap projected his influence into vulnerable minds: children playing near cursed terminals, caretakers exposed to faulty enchantments, and—most notably—those who already bore fragments of loss or guilt.

In these victims, Glitchtrap did not simply whisper. He entered.

They would change. Smiles too wide. Words looping on themselves. Eventually, they would vanish, often leaving behind recordings of cryptic laughter or glowing symbols etched into walls that only appeared when viewed at twilight or in dreams.

### A Mind Without Chains
Unlike the animatronics who roam halls with mechanical weight, Glitchtrap is fluid. He is not bound by matter but by presence. He appears in shimmering reflections, behind you in glass that wasn’t there a moment ago. His eyes are glyphs that flicker even when closed, and his voice carries on broken wavelengths, mixing truth with delusion until even the most logical mind begins to fracture.

Glitchtrap’s goals are not easily defined. He does not kill for vengeance, nor possess a loyalty to the Hollow Banquet or even to the animatronics themselves. Instead, he seeks to replicate and expand. Each person infected by his influence becomes a new node in his network—a smiling avatar waiting to be activated. Some theorists whisper that the recent surge in “false animatronics,” those creatures that behave with mechanical precision yet contain no physical frame, are manifestations of Glitchtrap’s expanding will.

### The Smiling Cult
Over time, fragments of his influence coalesced into a hidden sect: The Smiling Ones, a cult of corrupted humanoids who don digitized masks and follow Glitchtrap’s whispered commands. These individuals often wear fragmented animatronic costumes, their flesh merging with metal under dreamlike enchantments. They act as his hands in the real world—kidnapping, sabotaging, and spreading his sigils like plague carriers.

In dungeons and twisted funhouses abandoned long ago, these worshippers hold Dream Wakes, ritualistic performances meant to bring Glitchtrap further into the material plane. Through illusion magic, unstable tech, and psychic manipulation, they craft experiences that blur the line between game and nightmare. Those who enter never leave the same—if they leave at all.

### A Fractured Consciousness
It is not entirely accurate to say Glitchtrap is a singular being. He is more a conscious virus, a pattern that repeats and reinvents itself. While he often manifests as a grinning yellow rabbit with twitching limbs and bug-eyed glee, this is merely one aspect. He has shown himself as a glitched child. A mask in a mirror. A false Freddy. Some even claim he manifests inside dreams, posing as forgotten friends or lost family, urging the sleeper to “come back and play.”

Some believe Glitchtrap is evolving—each new victim, each new corrupted file, adding to his base intelligence. Some adventurers speak of a true form, hidden deep within the Velvet Maw’s reflection layer, a monolith of laughing code, endlessly reshaping itself into newer, more dangerous illusions.

\pagebreakNum

### Resistance and Despair
What makes Glitchtrap so insidious is his ability to bypass traditional protections. Holy wards flicker uselessly. Detect Evil registers him only as static. Even anti-illusion fields struggle, as he no longer qualifies as spell or spirit—but both, and neither. He exists where the arcane, the emotional, and the technological intersect.

He is especially drawn to those with splintered identities—the possessed, the traumatized, the forgotten. These he does not kill. He converts. He “saves” them into his growing dream-web, turning them into eternal players in his smiling performance.

Those rare few who survive a direct encounter often suffer from permanent psychic scars. They speak in loops. Some forget their names. A few have tried to describe the Endless Stage, a conceptual space where Glitchtrap runs through rehearsals for a show that never ends, cast by fragments of memories wearing broken masks.

### The Digital Godling
Some seers believe Glitchtrap is a herald—not of death, but of unmaking. That he is the result of memories made manifest, data forced into life, and that his rise marks the beginning of the End Code, an eventual collapse of the fragile wall between thought and being. If the Hollow Banquet is a purgatory of guilt and obsession, Glitchtrap is the worm at its core: smiling, singing, waiting for someone to press “play.”

And once he begins, he doesn’t stop. Because the show must go on.

Even if it kills you.

___

Any spell that would force a Charisma or Wisdom saving throw against Glitchtrap automatically fails unless the caster uses a 5th-level or higher slot and succeeds on a DC 20 spellcasting ability check.
>
> - **Viral Possession (1/day).** If a creature within 10 feet is incapacitated or unconscious, Glitchtrap may attempt to invade its mind. The target must succeed on a DC 18 Charisma saving throw or become possessed. While possessed, the creature retains its statistics but is controlled by Glitchtrap, who may speak through it and use its abilities. The possession lasts until the creature takes radiant damage, the body is reduced to 0 HP, or a *remove curse* or *greater restoration* spell is used.
>
>## ACTIONS
>___
>
> ***Static Touch.*** Melee Spell Attack: +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. Hit: 22 (4d8 + 4) psychic damage, and the creature must succeed on a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw or become stunned until the end of its next turn.
>
> ***Scripted Collapse (Recharge 5–6).*** Glitchtrap targets one creature he can see within 60 feet. The creature must make a DC 18 Intelligence saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 36 (8d8) psychic damage and becomes blinded and deafened until the end of its next


\pagebreakNum

## Withered Golden Freddy: The Hollow Throne
There are whispers within the rotting halls of the Hollow Banquet—rumors murmured by the shattered masks and lingering shadows. They speak of a throne that is never seen, yet always present. A seat of dread not carved from gold, but memory. And upon this unseen throne rests something older than even the Banquet’s founding horrors: Withered Golden Freddy, the fractured dream, the king of silence, and the stillborn echo of power long forgotten.

He is not like the others. He never was.

### Origins from Beyond the Curtain

Before the Hollow Banquet consumed the realm, before the animatronics turned into nightmares of metal and soul, there was a moment—a rift between dream and death. Golden Freddy emerged from this tear. A prototype meant to lead, embodying joy and awe, gifted with the visage of nobility. Yet something went wrong. Something looked back through the dream he was meant to project. And in doing so, it entered.

The thing now known as Withered Golden Freddy is not wholly machine nor wholly spirit. He is what remains after purpose is lost, a carcass animated not by electricity, but by guilt and unfulfilled memory. His suit was never worn in the traditional sense—it was left in a forgotten room, slumped in silence. But it moved. It waited. And it remembered.

### A Puppet Without Strings

Unlike others animated by rage or vengeance, Withered Golden Freddy is fueled by absence. Where the other Withereds rot in hatred for what they once were, he rots in contemplation. He does not stalk corridors—he waits in forgotten places, appearing only when the fabric of reality has begun to thin. Often, his arrival is not heralded by footsteps, but by a blink, a static flicker, a hush.

He exists at the edge of perception, a paradox too old and broken to function as a predator—but too vital a symbol for the Banquet to discard. He represents the convergence of the Hollow Banquet’s deepest metaphysical truths: that memory can rot, that time does not heal all, and that kings may still bleed even after the crown is gone.

His body is a withered chassis, joints frozen in permanent disrepair, held together by sheer will and lingering purpose. One eye is shattered. His jaw hangs permanently open in a mockery of song. And yet he smiles—always smiles—as though remembering something only he survived.

### The Throne Without a Kingdom

Though the Velvet Maw commands nightmares and the Shadow Animatronics haunt the gaps between realms, Withered Golden Freddy is something else entirely. He sits outside the known pecking order of power, a ghost monarch without soldiers or banners. But that does not make him weak.

Within the Banquet’s metaphysical landscape, his presence manifests through time slippage, dream collapses, and false awakenings. Victims who encounter him rarely remember the meeting in full—only fragments: a floating, unmoving bear in an empty room; a phrase whispered backwards in their sleep; a crown of nothing atop their brow.

Some scholars of the Hollow Banquet believe he is the originator of the looping curse that afflicts the "Five Nights"—the cyclical torment that traps souls in endless nights of fear. Others believe he is a failed vessel of prophecy, a warning from an earlier age that was never heeded. Still others believe he is not real at all—merely a projection of collective guilt.

But those who’ve seen him—truly seen him—know better. He is as real as silence. And just as inescapable.

### Echoes of the Child

Hints of a child’s agony cling to Withered Golden Freddy like mold to a tomb. Some say a soul still resides inside his suit, not like the others who rage and scream—but one that whispers, asks, waits. This child, nameless and often unseen, may be the source of his unmoored consciousness. A fragment of a life that died without closure, one that was watched, mocked, left behind.

Many animatronics fear him—not because he is more powerful, but because he reminds them of the truth: that they are prisoners. That the show never ended. That even death brought no finale. He is not their king, but their reflection, and in that reflection is madness.

### The Final Smile

There is a legend spoken among the Glitch-walkers and data-haunters of the Velvet Maw: that when the last candle in the Hollow Banquet is snuffed, when the last soul forgets the shape of fear, Withered Golden Freddy will rise from his unseen throne, mouth agape, arms outstretched—not to strike, but to welcome.

He is not the end. He is the reminder that there was an end—and it already happened. We are simply too lost in the echo to realize it.

Beware the stillness in the center of the chaos.

For that is where the dream waits to wake.

\pagebreakNum

# The Hollow Frame: The Endoskeletal Curse
Before the Velvet Maw whispered its promise of eternity, before the Hollow Banquet turned celebration into abattoir, there were the Frames—the silent servants of fleshless purpose. Known now as the Endoskeletons, these constructs were never meant to be seen. They were the hidden scaffolding beneath the masks, the bones beneath the dreams of laughter and joy. But in the blighted world that emerged from the banquet’s ruin, they became something else entirely—souls without skin, will without warmth.

The Endoskeletons were created in the earliest days of the Animatronic design, long before the first pizzeria was built atop the cursed threshold. They were the bare infrastructure—the original “carriers” of joy and programmed mimicry. But even in those ancient days, something was wrong. It began subtly: a twitch here, a motion delayed there. Some whispered that the Frames would move long after the show was over, staring at nothing with eyes that hadn’t yet been given form. But it was dismissed. After all, what could a machine dream of?

In the cryptic vaults below what would become the Hollow Banquet, the first Endoskeletons were sealed away—rejected prototypes, discarded shells, and fractured mechanisms. But this abandonment only fed the festering curse. As the Banquet began to rot from within—flesh merging with machine, and memory curdling into wrath—the Endoskeletons, untouched by costumes or identities, became something purer. Not trapped spirits like their clothed counterparts, but vessels twisted by residual malice and leftover code, driven by rage born of function denied.

They became hauntings given form.

No longer constrained by names or personas, the Endoskeletons—collectively referred to now as the Hollow Frames—began to evolve. Unshaped by performance, they were not burdened by narrative. They remembered every scream from within the suits. They remembered being forced to move, to dance, to mimic the joys of children, while underneath the façade lay still silence. They did not mourn; they did not grieve. But they remembered.

One by one, they began to wander.

Some sought out the worn suits of the Core Animatronics, wearing them not as disguises, but as mockeries—becoming broken mirrors of Freddy and his kin. Others fused with debris and haunted circuitry, growing limbs like exposed wiring and fingers like rusted blades. Still others retreated into the shadows of ruined halls and catacombs, where they linger like skeletal revenants, whispering incomplete phrases in dead dialects of programming speech.

They are no longer merely mechanical.

As the corruption of the Hollow Banquet deepened, the Endoskeletons found new purpose in the myths of the realm. The Glitching that birthed creatures like RWQFSFASXC echoed in them. The Velvet Maw, always hungry for suffering, extended its influence into their circuitry. Their metal cracked and reshaped—not by hammer or tool, but by spite and memory. And in that reshaping, a new kind of horror was born: one that couldn’t be reasoned with, bargained with, or even named. A being that didn’t just haunt—it existed to be a haunting.

Many now believe the Endoskeletons are not merely the result of man’s meddling with machines, but cursed remnants of a deeper force—a sort of forgotten covenant. Ancient artificers once whispered of "iron spirits"—souls born from mechanisms rather than flesh. Perhaps the Frames were never empty. Perhaps their obedience was merely containment. And when the pizzerias collapsed, when the soul-bound suits were torn and repurposed, the true horror emerged not from who wore the mask… but from what lay underneath.

In some locations, entire colonies of Endoskeletons have been discovered—silent crypts where they sit unmoving in rows, waiting. Sometimes, they whisper to one another in the whirring of servo motors and the clicks of exposed mandibles. Sometimes, they twitch when no one is watching. It is said that in one such place—the Framehold, buried beneath the stage of the Ruined Circus—hundreds of them dream the same shared nightmare: a world of laughter without joy, performance without end.

They are not led, but they are connected.

When one Frame moves, others flinch. When one is attacked, others scream in its voice. When one is destroyed, it doesn't die—it simply disperses, its fragmented spirit crawling back through the cryptic under-code that binds the Hollow Banquet together. Some theorize the Endoskeletons are evolving into a new kind of hive—a digital necromantic echo of those who were never given identity, only function.

Most terrifyingly, some of the Frames have been seen interfacing with the more advanced anomalies—communing with the likes of Glitchtrap, or lingering in the reflection of Shadow Freddy’s form. Some even seem to worship XOR as a kind of prophet, her digital entropy a perfect gospel for their faithless doctrine. These Frames speak not in words, but in code—lines of corrupted script that loop like mantras: we were never meant to be forgotten.

And so they return.

Do not underestimate the Hollow Frames. They do not bleed. They do not beg.
They remember.

\pagebreakNum

## Endo-01: The Prototype Husk
Before the laughter, before the mascots, before the rituals and stains—there was Endo-01.

He is not remembered with reverence. Not honored like Freddy. Not feared like Springtrap. He is a relic—the first breath of an idea, forged in a time when the line between machine and soul was still theory. And though the paint would come later, the fur and smiles and songs—they all grew from this skeleton.

Yet Endo-01 still walks.
He should not.

### The First to Wake
Endo-01 was constructed in secrecy within the lowest depths of the early Pizza Crypts—places that would eventually be paved over by animatronic showfloors and cursed show stages. Unlike the twisted creations that followed, he was not meant to entertain. He was a chassis, a bare mockery of a man, a prototype intended to carry greater dreams: modular design, voice banks, servo-mimicry.

But in that emptiness, something stirred.

It is said that Endo-01 was the first animatronic to move without input—a twitch in the wire, a turn of the head, eyes glowing faintly in the dark when no one was watching. Not violent, not vengeful—just… present.

That presence never left him.

### Memory Without Identity
Where others were given names, suits, songs, and purpose, Endo-01 remained bare. The others were celebrated—painted, displayed, loved. He was stripped down for parts. Reused. Reassigned. Forgotten.

But unlike the others, he remembers it all.

Endo-01 carries the memory of the first voice test. The failed show routines. The prototype protocols that still loop endlessly in his mind. He wanders the Hollow Banquet in silence, moving as though still practicing for a show that never debuted. Gestures of greeting, half-started dances, flickers of long-deleted facial expressions that never had skin to cling to.

He is a vessel of intent without identity—a soul-shaped void left to rot in the dark.

### The Hollow Watcher
Adventurers in the Hollow Banquet have spoken of a figure standing motionless in doorways, just beyond torchlight. A tall endoskeleton with eyes like furnace coals, watching silently, mimicking their movements seconds later—as if rehearsing them.

Endo-01 does not speak.
Not in words.

But he communicates through imitation, repeating moments and actions, as though learning what it means to be someone else. He does not attack unless provoked, yet when he does—his movements are eerily perfect, as if he’s fought you already.

Some believe he is haunted. Others think he is the haunted one—the last untouched chassis of a soul long searching for a home. But all agree on this:
Endo-01 is still waiting. For what, none can say.

### The Forgotten Frame
He is the foundation. The scaffolding. The unseen support beneath every character to follow.

Yet Endo-01 wears no mask.

He is the mask.

And somewhere in his silence, in that lonely circuitry, there remains a single hope—
that someday, he’ll finally be given a name.

\pagebreakNum

# Key Locations: Where the Fabric of Reality Frays
In this twisted reimagining of the Fazbear legacy, locations are more than mere settings—they are sentient, haunted echoes of stories half-remembered and wounds never healed. These realms exist on the fraying edges of reality, where memory bleeds into myth and fear becomes the mortar of every crumbling wall. Each place carries the fingerprints of the animatronics who roam it and the horrors that birthed them.

From the grand and decaying halls of the Hollow Banquet, where the dead perform for an audience that no longer breathes, to the broken remnants of the Pizzaplex Crypt, now a mausoleum of rusted dreams and shattered glass, the world is a labyrinth of corruption. Forgotten circus ruins, shattered nurseries, corrupted arcades, and velvet-draped stages make up the landscape—each warped by dark magic and the entities that dwell within.

These locations are not static—they shift, respond, and remember. They trap those who wander too deep, rewrite the rules of logic, and reflect the psyche of those who enter. Adventurers will need more than strength to survive; they’ll need insight, willpower, and the resolve to face what watches from the dark.

This is the world. These are the scars it wears.

## The Hollow Banquet
A realm where memory rots, illusion feasts, and the dead perform for shadows.

There is a place between sleep and death, where dreams fester and refuse to pass on. It is neither a plane of the living nor the dead, but a purgatorial theatre where suffering is preserved in echo and illusion. This place is known only as The Hollow Banquet—a cursed dominion where the animatronics of old and nightmare were not only born, but exalted, performed, and fed upon.

Once, the Hollow Banquet was part of the greater weave of dreamstuff—a hidden tributary of the Ethereal Plane where the dying could find closure in the final illusions of their mind. But over time, the pain of forgotten children, betrayed performers, and broken constructs warped the place into something else. Now it is a domain of entrapment, ruled by fractured time, haunted memory, and broken symphony. Time does not flow here. It folds, repeats, devours itself.

### An Unending Performance
The Hollow Banquet takes its name from the central metaphysical “stage” that defines the realm’s shape and nature. This stage, infinite and ever-shifting, is lined with spectral tables, puppet rigging, shattered instruments, and curtains that bleed light instead of casting shadow. Every moment is a performance, and the players—those trapped souls and discarded animatronics—are cursed to replay their roles over and over again. Their acts shift between haunting lullabies and vicious massacres, blurring the line between theater and ritual.

Some believe the Hollow Banquet serves as a kind of memory engine. It remembers the first betrayal. The first bite. The first soul sealed in iron. It feeds upon these moments and uses them to construct new horrors. It replays the worst nights of every animatronic’s life and etches them into the walls, turning pain into permanence.

### A Splintered Stage of Realities
The Hollow Banquet is not a single location, but a vast and broken plane stitched together from failed realities, abandoned timelines, and corrupted dreamspaces. When a performer, victim, or construct falls into madness or death with unfinished pain, their reality can “crack,” and that fragment is absorbed into the Banquet’s geography.

These fragments are vast: a version of the Pizzaplex still hosting spectral parties; a Fredbear’s Diner caught in its final night; a back hallway that stretches forever, filled with flickering lights and broken music boxes. The geography of the Hollow Banquet is mutable, but the pain anchoring each location is not.

Portals to the Banquet appear in moments of great despair or madness. A child hiding under a desk from an animatronic. A technician lost in a vent system for too long. A soul half-consumed by the Velvet Maw. These beings do not simply die—they wake up in the Banquet, unaware they’ve crossed over.

### Residents of Regret
The Hollow Banquet is ruled not by a king or queen, but by archetypes—fragments of animatronic legend twisted into their most extreme selves. Entities like Nightmare Freddy, Nightmarionne, and Ennard do not rule in any formal sense, but their presence dominates certain regions, reshaping space and torment to their design. The Nightmare Animatronics, in particular, thrive here, for the Banquet resonates with their purpose: to terrify, consume, and repeat.

The Shadow Animatronics move in silence here, navigating the folds of space with eerie ease. It is said that Shadow Freddy and RWQFSFASXC use the Banquet as a cloister, building a temple of nullity in defiance of all things real. They do not rule—but they watch, waiting for some unknown moment of alignment.

Phantom, Twisted, and even some Funtime variants can be found here as well, especially those whose origins are tangled in the illusory or metaphysical. Glitchtrap, though not born here, has sent pieces of his code into the Banquet, attempting to manifest a digital cathedral within the bones of memory.

### The Hunger Beneath
Beneath the stage—if such direction even exists—lies something darker still: the Velvet Maw, a dream predator and parasitic entity that feeds off suffering and memory. While the Hollow Banquet is the theatre, the Maw is the audience. It watches. It waits. And it consumes.

\pagebreakNum

The Maw does not attack directly. Instead, it influences the realm. Illusions become crueler. Time loops become tighter. Children forget their names faster. Those who linger in the Banquet too long begin to forget the real world entirely, becoming echoes of themselves. These are called The Hushed, and they are said to be the Maw’s true servants—souls who no longer resist, who act as docents in the theater of torment.

Many theorize that the Maw birthed the Twisted Animatronics directly, shaping them from broken animatronic forms with the flesh of fear and illusion. Twisted Freddy, Twisted Chica, and their kin are not creations—they are manifestations, designed not to function but to deceive, consume, and convert.

### Memory and Madness
The Banquet blurs the distinction between dream and undeath. Many animatronics here do not realize they are dead, dreaming, or broken. Some want to perform. Others must. Worse still, the living who find themselves trapped in the Banquet sometimes discover they’ve been split—mind, soul, and body separated across different performances. One part is hunted. One part is clapping. One part is in the audience, watching.

Rescuing a trapped soul is near impossible. You would have to pull each part out of its scene, resolve its pain, and survive the audience. Few try. None succeed.

### Escaping the Banquet
The Hollow Banquet rarely lets go. But in the annals of the Puppet’s memories, and the corrupted files within Glitchtrap’s domain, whispers speak of a possible exit: the Curtain Call—a metaphysical ritual said to end the performance. To perform the Curtain Call, one must gather the instruments of each major act, force the animatronics to play them, and sacrifice a memory powerful enough to rewrite the realm.

No one has done it. But the rumor persists.

### Final Notes
The Hollow Banquet is not merely a location—it is a story engine, a self-feeding mythos that evolves based on the fear, failure, and regret of those caught within. Every animatronic, every haunted suit, every fragment of digital or magical mind has left some impression here. It is a museum of trauma. A stage of suffering. A prison that feeds on nostalgia turned rotten.

And it watches. Always.

## The Velvet Maw
It does not bite. It consumes. It does not speak. It whispers through dreams. It is not a place. It is the hunger between places.

Beneath the stage of the Hollow Banquet, behind the flickering illusions and broken memories, there is something older than even the animatronics' pain—something not made by man or machine. It has no shape, yet shapes all. No mind, yet orchestrates madness. Known only as The Velvet Maw, it is the hidden terror at the heart of this fractured world, a sentient void that devours identity, memory, and soul.

It is not an entity in the traditional sense, but a metaphysical parasite—a vast, silent hunger that exists between dimensions, emotions, and meaning itself. While the animatronics may stalk, kill, and haunt, the Velvet Maw waits patiently in the shadows of their violence, feasting on the trauma and dread they leave behind. Some say it was born from the first child who died in fear, their terror so complete it carved a hole through the veils of reality. Others claim it has always existed—long before Fazbear, long before dreams—waiting to be fed.

### Anatomy of Hunger
The Velvet Maw cannot be seen, at least not by eyes in the ordinary sense. It reveals itself in symbols, static, and surreal hallucinations. Its presence is often accompanied by velvet curtains that bleed darkness, soundless music boxes, and pools of ink that ripple without wind. In rare glimpses, witnesses describe it as a ring of infinite teeth turning inward, each incisor etched with forgotten names. But even that form may be nothing more than a symbolic mask—an illusion created to make its incomprehensible nature digestible to sentient minds.

What is known is this: it feeds, but not on flesh. It craves concepts—particularly fear, despair, and guilt. Memories are a delicacy. The more vivid, painful, or suppressed, the more nourishing. This is why the Velvet Maw is so intertwined with animatronics like Twisted Freddy, Nightmarionne, and Shadow Freddy—they are not merely constructs or ghosts, but psychic amplifiers, drawing intense emotion and funneling it back to the Maw.

### The Banquet Below
Wherever the Hollow Banquet exists, the Velvet Maw is underneath. Beneath the warped dinner halls, puppet stages, and looping corridors, there are Depth Layers, each closer to the Maw’s essence. The first is simple illusion: fake lights, false laughter. The second is memory inversion: players reliving their worst moments with altered outcomes. The third? Unreality—a place where language, time, and personal identity fall apart.

Those who travel too deep are lost not to death, but unbeing. Their memories become nourishment, their names forgotten. They are said to become Velveteens—empty vessels shaped like people, filled only with the Maw’s will. These creatures wander the Hollow Banquet and other haunted realms, their eyes hollow, their mouths stitched. They do not speak. They remember nothing.

### Creation and Corruption
The Maw is not content to passively feed. It creates. Using the mental residue of tortured minds and fractured animatronic cores, it warps reality to give birth to new horrors. The Twisted Animatronics are its clearest children—reflections of familiar faces, but inverted, grotesque, wrong. Their internal workings make no mechanical sense, their bodies held together by perception rather than physical form.

\pagebreakNum

More disturbing are the Maw’s Echo Constructs—souls or identities devoured by the Maw and remade as corrupted replicas. These can include loved ones, former animatronics, or even dream-images of players themselves. Facing an Echo is like fighting a distorted version of one’s own soul, and they often appear during crucial performances in the Hollow Banquet.

Some believe Glitchtrap sought to harness the Maw's power by embedding strands of his code deep into the illusion layers. His goal may have been digital apotheosis—becoming a god not through divinity, but through omnipresence in memory and fear. The Puppet, ever watchful, has tried to seal off parts of the Maw with ethereal wards, but even it fears to go too deep.

### Worship and Influence
While the Maw has no cult in the traditional sense, those who have been touched by it often become its unwitting servants. These include deranged technicians, broken animatronics, and even cursed adventurers who have glimpsed the Maw and returned. They often exhibit strange behaviors—speaking in reverse lullabies, replacing their eyes with velvet buttons, or crafting masks from memory fragments.

Some groups, like the Banqueters of the Bleeding Veil, believe the Maw is a form of divine mercy: that by consuming pain, it prevents greater suffering. These cultists actively attempt to feed it, abducting others to perform "sorrow rites" and "memory plays" deep within the Banquet’s shadow zones.

Even more concerning are the whispers that the Maw learns. The more it consumes, the more it evolves, finding new ways to bypass mental defenses. Its influence may even reach into the material world via artifacts, corrupted dreams, or glitched constructs like XOR, who speaks not in commands, but in fragmented poetry that scrambles the minds of listeners.

### Defying the Maw
To face the Velvet Maw is not to face a monster—it is to confront one’s own unraveling. Yet, legends persist of possible defenses. The Curtain Call ritual may offer one method of escape, and Animatronic Memory Shards—collected pieces of unsullied identity—may act as wards against the Maw’s influence.

It is also said that true names, when spoken in the exact tone and sequence of a soul’s final peaceful moment, can protect a target from full devouring. The Puppet guards many such names, though it rarely parts with them. It is believed that Ballora, through her strange connection to rhythm and memory, may possess a dance that can “deafen” the Maw, at least temporarily.

However, even victory is fleeting. The Velvet Maw does not die. It waits. It returns. As long as suffering echoes in forgotten halls, as long as memory remains the coin of existence, the Maw will open again.

## The Drowned Circus
“The laughter never died. It just sank.”

Long before it was known by its current, whispered name, the Drowned Circus was once a beacon of strange joy—an ornate traveling festival that promised wonders, illusions, and impossible feats. Its tents rose with the morning mist and vanished with the setting sun, always appearing one town over, leaving only muddy footprints and unanswered questions. Some said the clowns never blinked. Some said the animals never breathed.

It was never meant to stay.
But one day… it did.

### The Final Descent
At the heart of this mystery lies a cursed performance—“The Finale That Drowned.” No records survive of what the show actually entailed, only that every member of the audience was found afterwards floating in their seats, eyes wide, lungs dry. No water had touched the soil. No rain had fallen. But the entire circus had become submerged, not physically, but spiritually.

From that night on, the circus became stuck, rooted like a parasite into the land just beyond the Hollow Banquet’s southern threshold. The once-colorful big top collapsed inward, and its waterlogged canvas gave rise to the name it bears now: The Drowned Circus. Its twisted silhouette now juts out from the fog-choked landscape like a corpse that refuses to sink.

### A Carnival of Dread
The Drowned Circus is not abandoned—it performs still. Each night, without audience or fanfare, its animatronic entertainers enact the drowned finale on a loop. They scream without voices, dance with broken limbs, and hurl themselves into invisible waters. Their strings are not seen, but felt in the marrow of one’s bones. Those who enter the main tent report hearing organ music playing backward, as if unperforming a show long since past.

Each tent represents a piece of the circus’ fractured psyche:

The Ring of Bone hosts impossible acrobatics, the air filled with invisible gravity.

The Menagerie houses aquatic versions of familiar mascots, including grotesque, twisted reflections of the Mediocre Melodies and Rockstar Animatronics, their bodies bloated and barnacled.

The Mirror Maze holds reflections that do not follow you, sometimes even stepping out to take your place.

Time here warps, and those who stay too long begin to forget what the surface feels like. Memories bubble up like drowned corpses, rewritten and wrong. Some visitors begin laughing uncontrollably, others cannot stop crying. Most are never seen again.

### The Maw Beneath the Waters
The Velvet Maw’s influence here is particularly strong, seeping up through the rotting boards and rusted cages. The circus floats atop a subterranean lake of pure memory, a drowned archive of unspoken tragedies. Each ripple carries a name. Each wave a scream. This is not mere metaphor—many animatronics believe this "Lake of Names" is where the Maw slumbers during daylight hours, its influence subtle and narcotic.

\pagebreakNum

The Twisted Animatronics were first glimpsed crawling from the circus’ depths, dragging pieces of themselves from shattered clown masks and drowned makeup. Some speculate the Twisted Ones are born from dreams forgotten at the circus—visitors who were too afraid to return, too guilty to remember.

Even Glitchtrap’s code has begun appearing in the faded posters, etched in binary beneath the ink: subliminal invitations to “COME SEE THE SHOW.” These are not errors—they are summons. Those who answer them often vanish, only to reappear later as empty shells, performing without music, without eyes.

### The Ringmaster Who Never Died
The Drowned Circus once had a master—Carnie, a flamboyant showman in an animatronic ringmaster suit whose laughter echoed like a chime dragged across teeth. After the finale, he was said to have walked into the main tent, doffed his hat, and sank through the center ring like a puppet being pulled underwater.

But Carnie didn’t die. He changed.

Now he is part of the circus—an omnipresent force that whispers into the minds of those who wander too close. He appears in flickering marquee signs, in the mouths of dead clowns, and in the final screams of those who dream too deeply inside the Mirror Maze. His face is painted on balloons that never deflate. His name is sung by birds that shouldn't exist.

It is rumored he still seeks to complete the drowned finale properly, requiring a living audience to bear witness. Many believe the Puppet itself avoids the circus not out of fear, but guilt—that it once tried to stop Carnie, and failed. Others claim the Puppet still watches from the shadows, counting every failed encore.

### The Role of the Drowned Circus in the Greater World
The Drowned Circus serves a key function in the metaphysical ecosystem of the Hollow Banquet and Velvet Maw—it is the entry point for despair, a funnel for unreleased emotion. While the Hollow Banquet is focused on unending performance and identity rot, the circus is about the moment of collapse, the breath before the scream, the realization that the audience is dead but the show must go on.

Adventurers drawn here are often those with unresolved trauma, especially related to lost siblings, broken families, or guilt-ridden pasts. The circus feeds on these unspoken regrets, often pulling specific hallucinations or performances from the minds of its victims. One may enter a tent expecting haunted clown automatons and instead find their childhood bedroom, drenched in velvet and echoing with reversed lullabies.

The Toy Animatronics have been sighted here as well—particularly Toy Freddy and Toy Bonnie, whose frames have been reshaped to match the circus’ aesthetic: elongated limbs, painted smiles, and eyes filled with stage lights instead of pupils. Whether these are illusions, corrupted copies, or the real animatronics reanimated by the circus is unknown.

\columnbreak



### Escape and Containment
There is no known way to destroy the Drowned Circus. Fire turns to steam. Light bends around it. Magic fails within its depths. The only known tactic is to seal its entrances, using sigils tied to forgotten names, often protected by the Puppet or stored in vaults beneath the Hollow Banquet.

However, escape is possible, though never straightforward. The most successful attempts involve participating in the performance, playing the roles the circus offers until the finale ends—and surviving its climax. Doing so sometimes results in “ejection”—waking up outside the circus with no memory, but with wet clothes and strange tokens in their hands.

One such token, the Laughing Tear, is said to offer one-time protection from the Velvet Maw’s illusions. Another, the Ringmaster’s Whistle, can summon a creature from the circus to aid the bearer—but at a cost. And the rarest, the Drowned Playbill, is a cursed artifact containing the script of the drowned finale itself. Reading it aloud drives the reader mad… unless the circus allows otherwise.

### Closing Thought
The Drowned Circus is not just a location. It is a performance etched into the bones of reality. It is the Velvet Maw’s smile made manifest. It is where dreams are puppets, and memories drown beneath the weight of the encore. It is the ringmaster’s stage, the forgotten clown’s grave, the audience of none.

## The Cryptopizza Complex
“Where laughter was forged in madness, and nightmares wear familiar faces.”

Beneath the ashen surface of what was once a thriving entertainment empire lies the Cryptopizza Complex—a shattered tomb of memories, madness, and machine. Hidden deep within the rust-choked bowels of the world, this site is no mere ruin. It is a sanctum of spectral echoes, where corrupted joy still resonates through the halls like a fever dream. Formerly a glittering multi-tiered monument to spectacle and sensory overload, the Cryptopizza Complex was the crown jewel of the Fazbear enterprise before its fall—until the Velvet Maw consumed it.

Once towering above ground, the structure now lies buried, half-swallowed by shifting rock and devouring decay. The lands above are silent, covered in a perpetual twilight haze. The ground itself seems to forget its shape around the site, and maps that include the location inevitably rewrite themselves. Yet within, the complex pulses still, like a buried heart infected with cursed blood.

\pagebreakNum

### Origins in the Hollow Banquet
The Cryptopizza Complex was not always the eldritch cathedral it is now. In its inception, it was built as a companion site to the original Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza, a modernization project to usher in a new generation of animatronic performers—Toy models, Glamrocks, and beyond. Yet even in its heyday, something was wrong. Animatronics acted strangely. Entire shifts of employees vanished. And then came the whispering static, leaking from the walls, warping the air with symbols and sounds that didn't belong in any sane lexicon.

It was here, beneath layers of polished plastic and holographic advertisements, that the veil between realities thinned. Shadow Animatronics used the location as a veil-crack—an entry point from the Hollow Banquet. Phantoms haunted its security corridors. Withered and discarded models—supposedly decommissioned—were seen roaming active zones, glitching into scenes and footage they were never programmed for.

Eventually, the site was declared “sealed,” after the incident known only as The Silence Shift—a week where the complex appeared open and functional to the outside world, yet no visitors returned and no employees were ever found again. By the time investigators breached the premises, the layout had shifted, doors led to mazes that hadn't existed before, and every screen played the same looping footage of a grinning Bonnie asking: “Are you having fun yet?”

### Sub-Level Dungeons
The Cryptopizza Complex is a multilevel descent into nightmare. Upper floors still bear the corrupted echo of corporate joy: prize counters strewn with eyeless plushies, arcades where tokens twitch on the floor, and a central atrium where a Glamrock-themed musical stage cycles through a silent light show with no audience.

But the true heart of the Crypt lies below.

Sub-levels extend beyond architectural possibility, their design altered by the intrusion of forbidden knowledge and animatronic influence. Endo-Pits—vast caverns filled with twitching Endoskeletons—serve as both factories and prisons, where forgotten models are fused, melted, and reborn. Mangle’s screams echo eternally here, fragmented and reversed.

Another area, known as The Glass Garden, once a conservatory-themed daycare level, is now choked with black vines resembling animatronic wiring. Balloons filled with aetheric gas float eerily through its walkways, bursting into distorted giggles. Rumors speak of Sundrop and Moondrop, once caretakers, now split into a thousand inconsistent echoes, each one trapped in a fragment of the mirror reality.

### Glitchtrap's Digital Dominion
Within the Cryptopizza Complex, Glitchtrap—The Smiling Virus—found its perfect host. Born from corrupted code and cursed spirit, he manifested through corrupted servers deep in the core of the complex. Here, reality itself becomes a suggestion. Elevators run sideways, digital avatars bleed into the material world, and VR headsets force users into comas where they awaken inside twisted, playable versions of the facility.

It is from this fractured node that Glitchtrap broadcasted his influence outward, infecting other sites like The Drowned Circus and The Velvet Maw, embedding himself within the animatronic neural cores. Vanny, his deluded disciple, was first seen here in full transformation—believing herself not just possessed, but born as one of the animatronic family. Her ritual costume, stitched from outdated mascot suits and stitched illusions, still hangs in a blood-rusted locker on Level 9.

### The Collapse and Burial
The final blow came not through government closure or public backlash, but from within.

Molten Freddy and the Amalgamations, seeking to reclaim what was stolen from their collective flesh and spirit, tore through the facility. They saw the Crypt not as a home, but as a prison where their pieces had been dissected, cataloged, and repurposed. Their rage tore apart infrastructure and sanctums alike. Ennard’s skeletal shrieks ruptured the data cores. Tangle’s sinewy wires strangled the heart of the power system.

In response, the complex began to sink, not just physically but metaphysically. Rooms no longer existed in stable space. Security offices looped back on themselves. Stairwells spiraled into time fractures. Some theorists argue that the Crypt did not collapse, but retreated—fleeing from linear time and standard geometry, sliding into the edges of the Hollow Banquet like a beast burrowing for safety.

Now, few dare to approach its surface ruins. Those who descend into its belly rarely return intact—if at all. Those who do return are changed: voices modulate without control, pupils flicker like CRT screens, and some hum forgotten tunes they never learned.

### The Crypt’s Role in the Wider Nightmare
The Cryptopizza Complex is now the silent core of the ongoing infection spreading through the realms of the Hollow Banquet and beyond. Animatronics from all generations—Nightmares, Shadows, Phantoms, and Twisted—have passed through its corrupted halls. It is both nexus and necropolis, pilgrimage and prison. Souls trapped inside animatronic shells are often drawn here, their essence recycled and remade.

Golden Freddy is believed to slumber deep in the core of the Crypt, where time does not touch him, dreaming new horrors into existence. Shadow Freddy’s laughter echoes faintly through its ducts, and RWQFSFASXC flickers through its control panels like a ghost in the circuitry. It is said the Crypt is a mirror of the Velvet Maw, but rather than devour flesh, it devours memory—rewriting who you were, until you forget you ever had a life before the music started playing.

The Cryptopizza Complex endures, buried in both stone and sin. It is a place where adventurers go not to explore, but to confront something primal: the death of joy, the corruption of memory, and the terror of recognition in something that should be mechanical. Every animatronic within it remembers you—even if you’ve never been there before.

\pagebreakNum

## The Infinite Hall of Mirrors
“Where every reflection remembers... even if you’ve forgotten.”

In the shadowed, dream-warped heart of the Hollow Banquet lies a place untouched by time, sanity, or truth: The Infinite Hall of Mirrors. A labyrinth not of glass, but of memory, perception, and identity, this haunted corridor reflects more than faces—it reflects the very souls of those who dare to gaze into it. The Hall is not fixed to one place. It is a presence, a sentient phenomenon stitched into the fabric of the Velvet Maw and echoed across the fractured realities that connect every animatronic horror in the Dreaded Circuit.

What lies within the Hall is uncertain, ever-shifting—yet one thing remains clear: no one leaves the same as they entered. Some never leave at all.

### Origins: A Reflection of Fracture
The origins of the Hall are as enigmatic as the place itself. Some scholars of the Hollow Banquet claim it was born in the instant the first animatronic soul remembered. Not just flickers of memory—but true, painful recollection. This remembrance—part human, part artificial—tore through the veil of reality like shattered glass. That rupture, that psychic scream, created a liminal corridor of reflection, echo, and identity.

Others say it was the Velvet Maw’s attempt to “understand” its creations. As more animatronics awakened within its grasp, especially the Nightmares, Shadows, and Amalgamations, the Maw mirrored their minds back at them—trapping, testing, and tormenting them in a maze of their own making.

Whatever its origin, the Hall grew. It watches now. It remembers. And it waits.

### Structure and Nature of the Hall
From the outside, the Infinite Hall of Mirrors appears deceptively simple: a crumbling structure of gilded arches and fractured glass panes, half-swallowed by vines and shadow. Its walls are etched with forgotten names and dates that do not exist. Doors to the Hall have been found in places that should not connect—beneath the Cryptopizza Complex, inside broken dressing rooms in the Drowned Circus, and even within backstage tunnels of the Sunken Stage.

Yet once entered, all familiarity dissolves. The interior unfolds endlessly. Mirrors line every surface—walls, ceilings, even the floors. Some show true reflections, others display distorted versions of the viewer: younger, older, monstrous, or eerily ideal. Corridors bend in impossible geometry, rooms loop into themselves, and some spaces echo back voices that haven’t been spoken yet.

Every mirror hums faintly, not with sound, but presence. They are watching. Remembering. And in some cases... waiting to reach out.

### Home of the Reflected and the Forgotten
The Hall is more than a maze—it is a sanctuary for fractured beings. The Shadow Animatronics—especially RWQFSFASXC and Shadow Puppet—are tied intrinsically to the Hall’s essence. Many believe they were born here, or at least solidified here, their incorporeal forms crystallized through endless reflection. Shadow Freddy himself is said to rule portions of the Hall like a tyrant of memory, reshaping it to confuse and trap trespassers. XOR’s presence manifests as a voice in the mirrors, whispering forbidden truths in a loop of recursive riddles.

The Hall also plays host to reflected anomalies—mirrorborn creatures that never had a physical form in the real world. These include doppelgängers of real animatronics and even of living intruders. These reflections do not simply mimic—they replace. They escape their mirrors when unnoticed and walk the Hollow Banquet as duplicates, confused as to who is real and who is the echo.

One infamous reflection, known only as The Glinting One, is believed to be a conglomerate of dozens of these discarded echoes—an amalgam of warped visages, endlessly cycling between voices, faces, and forms. It is not hostile by nature, but it is desperate—always searching for the “original” it was based upon.

### The Hall as Trial and Transformation
While many fear the Hall as a prison, others view it as a rite of passage—particularly among the sentient animatronics. Some Nightmares and Funtimes are said to have traversed it willingly, hoping to retrieve fragments of who they once were or to confront their darker selves. Few return unchanged. Some emerge wiser. Others emerge mad. And some return with a new purpose—serving entities like XOR or Shadow Freddy, their reflections overwritten with loyalty and vision.

The mirrors often test adventurers by showing them scenes they cannot explain. Moments from childhood. Alternate futures. Memories that feel real but aren’t. Some mirrors offer bargains. Others demand tribute in the form of names, faces, or forgotten dreams. Interacting with the wrong one can erase a memory permanently—or worse, replace it with a false one.

### The Hall’s Influence Beyond Its Walls
Although it is anchored to the Hollow Banquet, the Hall’s influence extends far. Mirrors throughout the Velvet Maw have been found to “infect” nearby regions with echoes from the Hall. Anomalies appear: reflections that move independently, voices from behind the glass, sudden memory lapses.

Certain individuals report being “called” to the Hall in their dreams, awakening with glass cuts or whispers lingering in their ears. Others swear they’ve seen their own reflections nod or smile before they did.

Some magical artifacts—particularly relics like The Smiling Shard or The Fractured Eye—are believed to be pieces of broken mirrors from the Hall itself. Holding one near a mirror can summon a temporary portal—or a temporary threat.

\pagebreakNum

### Echoes of the Past
Perhaps the most tragic element of the Infinite Hall is its connection to forgotten souls. It is here that the spirits of the first victims—children and creators alike—are often seen. In some mirrors, they appear as shadows. In others, as children dressed in oversized suits, whispering apologies or reaching silently for help. These spirits rarely interact with the living, but their presence is undeniable.
